A bedtime fantasy

~ 13:00 Rain, Dates, and Photos
Huh? Where is this? Oh! Is this a story? Reader! Reader! Can you see me?

Lapis, it’s too early for — where are we?

A story! Look up! Can’t you see the reader?

That’s a reader? No way, right? They’re not what I expected…

Blue, you have to realize readers are a lot less attractive than main characters.

Why is that?

Because readers are a group of pathetic (virgin) lowlifes who read about people they want to be to escape reality.

I guess. But still, just look at that!

I think this is a particularly pathetic type of reader. They’re almost as short as you!

Huuh? Shut up! Wait, if that’s a reader, what does an author look like?

This one probably looks great. I mean, they recognized that I’m the main character!

Author, can you please make Lapis less self-centered?

Author, can you shrink Blue to half their original size?

What? Why do you look so much taller? Wait, what?

Hah! Of course the author would listen to me over some measly extra.

How am I a measly extra? I’m literally the reason this story exis—

Oh, our time’s almost up? Reader! If you’ve stopped crying in self-pity, new chapters drop every Saturday night, so be sure to read, ok? Oh, we’re on hiatus? Nevermind!

Wait! Author! Author! Make me tall again!
You weren’t tall to begin wit—

~~ Prologue ~~

6 YEARS AGO
It was the start of a new day.

Remnants of the midsummer sun had long vanished beneath the cypress trees, leaving behind a path of shimmering stars in its wake. Their silver light scattered into the consuming darkness of the ocean and made its way along the waves towards the outskirts of a sandy beach. They tugged monotonously at the trail of footprints tracing the shore.

A young girl walked barefoot along the beach, grasping a small lantern in one hand and fiddling with a tiny pendant with the other. Her white dress and flaxen hair swayed rhythmically in time with the breeze, and she twitched her long pointed ears due to the cold. The flickering flame of the lantern reflected itself in her eyes — eyes the same colour as the pendant in her hand. They were a dark blue. The colour of lapis lazuli.

For a long time, the girl traversed the wet sand, feeling the waves form into a bubbly foam under her feet. And then, she felt something else. A sharp prick dug itself into her soles, causing her to leap back in pain. Half-embedded in the sand was a small wooden crate just beginning to rot apart. 

She tilted her head quizzically for a few seconds before peering tentatively into the top of the crate. Though it was dark, she could still see the outline of another box, also made from wood. On its front was a grey knob surrounded by numbers delicately etched around it in a semicircle. The girl brought the contraption closer to her lantern and squinted, barely able to make out each number as well as the word “OFF” scribbled in marker. She whispered each number to herself as she turned the knob clockwise through the list of numbers:

100.3, 103.6, 108.7, 110.1, 113.5, 115.9…

And then the box began buzzing softly. 

~

Somewhere an ocean away, a boy sat crosslegged on a bed with his back against the wall. He turned his red and swollen eyes blankly towards the ceiling — he hadn’t gotten any sleep for what seemed like an eternity now. He muttered something to himself, words without any particular meaning.

“Maybe I’ll write a story...”

Strewn all around him were heaps of dirty laundry, half-uneaten plates of food, and junk thrown haphazardly on the floor. In a corner of the room, there was a wooden box with a semi-circle of numbers neatly carved around a grey button in its center. The number 115.9 was circled in marker. 

The boy froze as the box began emitting a faint buzz.

~

The girl on the beach held the box against her ear, trying to decipher the reason for the buzzing. But then there was a soft click of a button, and just as quickly as it appeared, the static stopped.

They both heard another person’s light breaths on the other end. For a long time, there was no other sound beyond that.

And then they both spoke at the same time.

“H-Hello?”

“Could this be fate?”

~~ Shades of Blue  ~~
On an island in the middle of the ocean, life slowly awoke from a deep slumber. Squirrels poked their heads out of their hiding holes, timidly venturing out beneath the dawning light filtering into the forest floor. Gulls squawked raucously as they glided in wide spiraling loops above the crystal-clear water. Spring had arrived in the archipelago. 

Within the depths of the island was a large pit. Despite the lush bushes all around the pit, there was nearly no animal life inside the pit. Nothing, except for a large pulsing organism perched precariously on a wide ledge. It was around five feet tall and consisted of fine, silky thread wrapped millions of times around a beating core. As the sun climbed above the distant mountains, the silk began to unravel, spiraling upwards in delicate loops until it faded into the crisp spring air. Soon, all that was left of the cocoon was the small figure of a young girl. Two clear, grey eyes fluttered open softly.  

The girl was no more than eleven years old. She seemed almost human were it not for a vaguely holographic appearance and long sky-blue hair. Aquamarine crystals floated in the air encircling her as if by magic; they wrapped behind her simple white dress and fanned out in two arcs beside her. Sunlight shone through them and dispersed in faint iridescence. For a moment, it seemed like the dispersed light had created wings. But then the crystals shifted, overlapping, and the imaginary wings folded smoothly around her body.

She looked down at her hands, then knelt and felt the dirt beneath her. “I’m alive…”, she whispered to herself. As if to reaffirm her statement, a winged crest in her chest flashed slowly for a few moments before glowing a constant vivid blue. It was a human-like figure with two fairy wings outstretched on its back.

For a while, the girl patted her body all over as if trying to come to terms with her existence. And then, she looked up. Nearly vertical rock faces, fifteen feet high, loomed all around her.

The girl’s name was Bluebird. And for the time being, she was trapped. 

~

The sun was high overhead when Bluebird spotted a flicker of movement in the edges of her vision. A flash of black disappeared into the leafy foliage at the top of the pit. Bluebird had sensed the same flash for the past ten minutes and yelled upwards at it at first, only to give up when there was no response. The girl decided it was a wild animal and leaned back against the walls of the pit, tired.

Suddenly, a rock plunked down from the top of the pit above her. It bounced once by her feet before falling down into the water below. Two more followed and ricocheted off her head. Annoyed, Bluebird shielded her head with her hands and whirled around.

Someone leapt down the rock face beside her. 

Bluebird could see that she was older — somewhere in her late teens. Flaxen hair flowed out from underneath a white sailor cap adorned with bronze aviator goggles, reaching past her blouse towards a light brown miniskirt. A long jet-black coat caught the gusts of wind and fluttered behind her like a cape. Sharp, pointed ears peeked out from beneath her hair, and resting on her chest was a small pendant that glinted in the bright sunlight.

She landed gracefully, tucking into a roll that brought her to a crouching stop just before Bluebird’s. Dusting herself off, she turned around and looked up; her sparkling eyes met with Bluebird’s. They were the same colour as the pendant around her neck — a deep, vivid blue. For a long time, neither of them said a word. And then, the newcomer smiled broadly and whispered.

“Could this be fate?”

“...”

Silence, and then Bluebird’s indignant retort: “What fate? You’ve clearly been planning that out for the last ten minutes.” The newcomer chuckled and put her index finger to her lips. “Shh, the reader doesn’t need to know that.” 

“...”

The girl tried to comprehend her response as the woman began walking slowly towards her. Bluebird stood her ground and stared warily as a slender hand stretched out towards her, ready to fight back if necessarily. The hand paused over her head…and then ruffled her hair.

“You’re short, but you’ll do.”

“Shut up! I am not short!”

The woman laughed as Bluebird, squirming, struggled to push her hand away. Bluebird finally broke free and muttered, half to herself: “Who even greets someone with ‘Could this be fate’, anyways?” The woman shrugged. “Chekhov’s gun was fired six years ago. I needed to say it at some point.”

For the second time in ten seconds, Bluebird could not comprehend her response.

~ 

The two were sitting as they watched the gulls as they flew in frenzied circles past them. 

“So, who even are you?” Bluebird asked. At this, the woman turned towards her and grinned. “Glad you asked!” She stood up and placed one hand enigmatically over a closed eye before speaking in a clear voice.

“Rejoice! For I am Lapis of the infinite dawn, supreme commander of <Shadow> as well as all between the two ethereal—”

“...So just Lapis?” 

Lapis shrugged, sighing. “You can call me that.”

“So, why did you even jump down here in the first place? And do you have a plan to get out?” Bluebird asked.

Lapis idly fiddled with the pendant against her chest as she reseated herself. “You don’t know? I obviously needed a flashy entrance! And that jump was pretty cool, right?” Bluebird had to admit it looked cool, but decided it was better not to say anything aloud. “As for the second question,” she continued, “Since you’re a fairy, I can just fly out of here!”

Fairies. In the archipelago, there were five races, four of which were well known — elves, vampires, oni, and humans. The former two had an alliance known as <Shadow>, which Lapis had (quite dubiously) self-identified as the supreme commander of. Vampires and oni were typically human-like in appearance but could also transform into large, monstrous creatures at a whim. Elves and humans, meanwhile, didn’t have any transforming capabilities, although elves had access to weaponry from an ancient civilization. The locations of those four races were well-known as well: all of humanity was housed in seven complexes on the main continent, vampires and elves cohabited an island to its far south, and oni lived to the west on Oni Island.. 

The fifth race, fairies, was much more mysterious — up until a year ago no one had even seen one before, let alone knew where they lived. And even now, the only thing known about fairies was that they were eternal beings that — if you made a contract with them — lent you incredible magical powers and the ability to fly. 

Bluebird’s weird clothing and the crest glowing on her body were a dead giveaway. She couldn’t deny it. But still, she stared at her. “You do know we have to make a contract, right?”

Lapis looked at Bluebird like it was the most obvious thing in the world. “Yeah?”

“...You know I have to agree to the contract, right?”

“Yeah?”

This person couldn’t get a hint. Bluebird declared indignantly: “Well, I’m not doing it! So think of another way to get off this island!”

In response, Lapis looked genuinely surprised. “What? But why would you pass on a contract with the main character?”

“Of course I — wait, what? Main character? Who?”

Lapis grinned, blue eyes shining. “Me! I’m the main character.” Bluebird sighed and wondered why she wasn’t surprised at Lapis’ response, before looking her squarely in the eyes. “Nonsense aside, I am not ever going to make a contract with you, okay?”

A laugh. “You just set a flag, didn’t you?”

“What? Shut up! I meant that!”

The woman combed her long hair back, carefree. “No worries, I know it’s all part of the script. The main character always gets what she desires.”

Bluebird barely managed to stop herself from retorting: “What script?” She already knew better than to question her. 

With a start, Lapis leapt to her feet as if remembering something, and whirled around in an unnecessarily elaborate pirouette. “Right, what’s your name? I don’t want to call you ‘child’ once you become my fairy.”

Bluebird stood as tall as she could, almost going on her tiptoes. “I’m too tall to be a child! And I’m not your fairy, you old hag!”

Lapis laughed and ruffled Bluebird’s hair again despite her best attempts to dodge it. “Being angry really draws out your childish charm. Anyways, what’s your name?” The girl sat back down in a huff. “It’s Bluebird.” 

“...”

For the first time since she’d met her, Lapis seemed at a loss for words. “B-bluebird? Like… the colour and then the animal?”

“Yeah. Problem?”

Lapis put her index finger on her chin in thought. A silence settled over the two before she spoke again.

“I henceforth deem thee Jaquavious.”

“Wait, what? Don’t just change my name like that!” 

Bluebird's illusionary crystal wings began pummelling Lapis’ side in defiance. She was adamant, however. “The main character’s fairy can’t be called Bluebird! Imagine trying to do a signature move, and then you have to say”, here she paused and struck a pose as if she were casting magic towards the walls of the pit, “I banish you to the jaws of death, by the power of…Bluebird!” The woman turned back to Bluebird with desperation in her voice. “That’s just sad!’

Bluebird was unconvinced, especially given Lapis’ replacement name. “Then find another fairy! Besides, I like my name, okay?”

“...”

“...”

Lapis let out a loud sigh. “Ok, Bluebird.”

For the first time, Bluebird felt like she had emerged victorious from their conversation. 

The woman continued: “So, Bluebird, how did you get here in the first place?”

“I—” Bluebird began to speak, but was interrupted.

“Bluebird, what foods do you like? Bluebird, what’s your favourite colour? Bluebird, I guess you’d like blue, because your name is Bluebird, right, Bluebird?”

Ughhh. “Fine, shut up! I don’t like my name either, okay? So stop repeating it so much!”

The woman smirked at the red-faced girl. “Thank you, Bluebird.” Bluebird prepared for another assault with her illusionary wings. “Anyways, Jaquavi—”

“But I am NOT using that name!”

Lapis muttered:  “so picky.” She sat back down, evidently thinking of a new name to call “her fairy” by. Bluebird, meanwhile, took the opportunity to ask curiously: “your name’s weird too! What does Lapis even mean?”

“It’s supposedly short for lapis lazuli, an ancient gemstone lost to time, but in reality it enchants the user with mystical powers and gives them eternal youth…”

Bluebird spared herself the misinformation and interrupted: “How much of that is true?”

“At least the first half.” Lapis shrugged casually.

The two sat comfortably next to each other in silence until Lapis turned to Bluebird. “I think I’ll call you Blue.”

“Better than anything else you’ve said so far.”

Lapis played around with the name for a few seconds, repeating it to herself a few times. She turned around with a dissatisfied expression.

“I would call you Blue, but two people having basically the same name is just lazy character writing. Are you sure Jacquavious isn’t okay?”

Bluebird — now Blue — vigorously nodded.

~

The sun was now beginning to set, and an orange glow began to emanate across the ocean to their right. For the past few hours Lapis and Blue had tried, unsuccessfully, to scale the twenty feet of rock that separated them from freedom above. Now they were sitting at the base of the pit, having made no progress whatsoever. Blue, despite having done nothing but get carried, was breathing a bit harshly. Meanwhile, Lapis, who had done almost all the physical exertion, didn’t seem tired in the least — main characters don’t get exhausted.

As they stared up at the open sky seemingly far, far away Lapis sighed. “If only someone’s wings weren’t just a tacky decoration
“Shut up!” Over the past few hours Blue had to endure Lapis’ continuous jabs at her completely useless wings to the point that even she was starting to get mad at her inability to get more than a few centimeters off the ground. “So,” Lapis spoke again, “isn’t it about time for you to form a contract with me?” 

That was the other thing Blue had heard Lapis complain about for what seemed like an eternity now. Blue’s answer was still the same, and she shook her head vehemently. “No way!”

“Just think of it as becoming my deuteragonist!”

“How is that any better?” Blue half-yelled in exaggeration. Lapis pouted and pulled her knees closer to her body. “I guess the cognitive reasoning of children isn’t fully developed.”

“Shut up! Why are you so obsessed over me anyways? What do you want with my powers?”

Lapis didn’t hesitate. “Of course I want them! The main character needs one-of-a-kind powers, right?”

Blue sighed, evidently realizing she should have expected as much from the self-absorbed elf.  “How noble”, she remarked sarcastically. Lapis didn’t respond immediately, and the two quietly watched the sunset mark the end of a day and beckon for the beginning of another. Finally, Lapis spoke: “Do you know anything about the war?”

“Obviously —”

“Too bad! The reader needs an explanation!”

Ignoring Blue, Lapis explained the conflict that had been plaguing the archipelago for the last few years. Before that time, humans lived under fear and subjugation of the vampires. However, a year ago, the fairies sided with the humans — the first contact they had ever made with another race. With their powers, the humans began to fight back both to rescue the captives and wipe out the vampire race as a whole. The elves, being close friends with the vampires, sided with them while the oni remained neutral.

After she was done explaining things purportedly for the “reader”, Blue asked her: “So, you want to use my powers to fight against the humans and fairies?”

“And acquire one-of-a-kind powers—” Lapis began to clarify, but was swiftly interrupted by Blue.

“Why would I want to fight the fairies?”

“I’m just giving you an opportunity to join the winning side.”

“Screw you! We’ll win!”

Blue thought to herself that was a surprising amount of confidence for someone who was supposedly fighting mythical creatures with amazing magical powers — but then again, that someone was Lapis. Now, Blue watched as the elf got up and stretched her arms as she replied. “True, in any other world we would lose. But I’m here.” Confused, Blue looked at her figure questioningly as Lapis faced the setting sun with her back towards her. 

“Blue, do you know what the first rule of being a main character is?”

“No?” Blue shook her head. 

As if someone truly were writing a script, the last vestiges of clouds obscuring the sun parted. Light blazed through Lapis’ hair, and from Blue’s perspective it almost seemed as though it had captured a brilliant golden flame. Lapis turned her head just enough that Blue met the resolute gaze of her sparkling right eye. Her lips were parted in a faint smile, a smile that seemed poised to take on the world and win. 

“The main character always leads her friends to a better future.”

Suddenly, the clouds rolled back into their line of sight, and Lapis’ golden spotlight dispersed into a million intangible rays at her feet. Lapis’ smile broke into a childish grin. “Blue, how was that? I planned it out just so the sunlight would shine on me as I said that. I even made sure to time it with my pose!”

“...”

Blue yelled at Lapis: “That was decent until you said that!”

From above, the bushes shook violently; both of them looked up. Two large limbs made from what seemed like the same material as the pit walls crashed into view, destroying the foliage and leaving deep gouges in its wake. A body as wide as the ledge was long followed closely after. The monster’s beady green eyes swept across the area before landing on the fairy and the elf on the ledge. 

Both Blue and Lapis stood their ground. Blue turned to Lapis: “I should have asked this earlier, but where are we?” Lapis answered, dodging the cascade of rocks: “Oni Island, why?”

Blue knew about the oni. Human in one form, land-dwelling monster in the other, they lived as a solitary tribe, even electing not to join in the conflict between the other races. That being said, they were known for two inter-species interactions: a cultlike, grotesque obsession over the fairies, and a deep hatred for the elves. Neither seemed particularly helpful right now. 

Lapis brushed the dust off her black coat and asked jokingly: “Interested? They like to  experiment with fairies by torturing them.” Blue thought about it for a moment before asking with far more curiosity than fear: “How do they do that?”

Lapis sniffed. “You're weird.”

“Says you!”

The oni above them abruptly spun around and crashed through the greenery above, evidently to tell others about his discovery. Blue and Lapis watched him go.

“Okay”, Lapis spoke seriously to Blue, “here's the script.”

Again, what script?  Blue thought to herself.

“So when the Oni come back, I go engage them and fight really bravely, but I end up losing and almost dying.”

Blue stared at her uncertainly as Lapis continued. “And just as they land the fatal blow, you teach me the activation spell for the contract with tears in your eyes, I make the contract with you, and we fly out just in the nick of time!”

“...Why are you assuming that there's an activation spell you have to say?” Blue hesitated before asking. Lapis laughed. “Things of this nature do not elude the main character! Or am I wrong?”

Blue averted her gaze towards the ground. Lapis laughed even more. 

“You thought you could fool me? The script is absolute! The script -”

Blue interrupted her: “Bluebird of flight, guardian of this world, I beseech you! Lend my back your wings, my body your powers, and my cause your life!”

Lapis froze. “...eh?” Blue smiled smugly at her as the elf began to stammer: “Th-that’s not the spell, right? B-but the script?”

It was Blue's turn to laugh, having exacted her revenge. “Guess your script isn't absolute. And by the way, I need to accept the contract even if you do say those words, so don't think I've accepted being your fairy!” 

Lapis fell despondently to the ground. Blue was going to rub things in a bit more, but at that moment the ground rumbled above them . They watched as one oni leveraged their long limbs to land roughly on the ledge in front of them, followed by another; the surface they stood on shook violently as large chunks of rock fell into the sea below. The monsters began to lumber towards them. Lapis mustered what bit of willpower she could find after having her fantasies destroyed, and got to her feet with a wide sweep of her coat. 

“Short, but you really will do.”

Lapis ignored Blue’s surprised yelp of indignation and reached into the hidden folds of her coat, drawing out her weapon of choice. Though she likely had a million conventional options to choose from, her weapon was a sleek grey umbrella.

Why am I not surprised… Blue thought to herself.

The distance between her and the oni was rapidly decreasing. The oni at the front broke into a toothless grin. “A fairy and an elf? Guess we’re really lucky today.” Lapis flashed a smile back. “You even speak like a villain!” The oni raised one heavy stone arm and brought it down right at Lapis’ location. At the last second, the elf sidestepped and leapt onto a narrow foothold on the rock face before propelling herself directly towards the oni. She thrust the umbrella directly at one of the oni’s green eyes. With surprising agility, the oni twisted his body, and a second fist grazed Lapis, sending her flying away onto the ground.

A small cut appeared just under the oni’s eye; clearly the umbrella wasn’t made from conventional materials. Lapis braced her right arm as she smirked. The oni let out a low growl and lumbered towards her, sending a flurry of imprecise swings that swept powerful blows of wind towards Blue. She nimbly dodged the first dozen, but then planted her feet and opened her umbrella, instantly transforming it into a shield.

What an idiot. 

The umbrella crumpled under the force of the punch, then Lapis’ body nearly followed if she hadn’t twisted her body in the nick of time. The punch still caught her, and she slammed against the cliff. The oni’s large hand gripped Lapis’ frame and began squeezing.

Both Blue and Lapis knew she had done that on purpose. Now, as her body began to contort from the oni’s pressure, Lapis looked straight into the eyes of the young fairy girl on the side and recited:

“Bluebird of flight, guardian of this world, I beseech you! Lend my back your wings, my body your powers, and my cause your life!”

Complete silence enveloped the ledge. And then, nothing happened. 

The oni was confused for a moment, but then raised the fist containing Lapis, preparing to slam her on the ground. Blue weighed her options. On one hand, she could take her chances at a future trapped with the oni. On the other hand…

Ughhhhhhh.

Blue yelled at the top of her lungs: “Say ‘Bluebird, be mine!’”

As the hand gripping Lapis plummeted downwards, the corners of Lapis’ mouth lifted up. The oni’s fist smashed into the ground. For a split second, there was silence.

And then, a low whir. From within the oni’s clenched hand, a black figure flashed past the oni and into the orange hues of the sky. 

It looked almost alien. Black plating clad its entire body except for the crest of a fairy, shining a stunning sky blue in the middle of its chest. Wings extended from its back, and trails of blue flame flickering from its wingtips blazed a wide arc in the sky. Half of its face was completely black, except for a glowing blue slit where its eye should have been. The other half was shielded by a translucent honeycomb, and through it one could see long flaxen hair and a sparkling eye the colour of lapis lazuli. 

From within the mecha suit, Lapis laughed manically. “Blue! You thought you could defy the script? Fool! I told you, the script is absolute!”

Though the young girl with wings was nowhere to be seen, Blue’s very annoyed voice resounded from within the suit into Lapis’ ear. “Shut up! How am I already regretting my decision?”

Lapis and Blue flew through the sky, quickly leaving Oni Island behind. As it became no more than a speck on the suit’s visor, Lapis whispered to an unknown someone: “See you on the battlefield.”

Blue, still very unhappy, spoke up: “Is that your catchphrase? That’s lame.”

“Better than your catchphrase being ‘Shut up!’”

“Shu— ughh, screw you!”

And so the two flew east, racing the setting sun to the start of a new day.

~

Sometime that night, Lapis locked the door to her room. It was a surprisingly empty room for someone so flashy: the only things in it were a table with a few drawers, a wooden chair that seemed as though it had never been sat on, and a bed. Various items were on the table, one of which was what seemed like a wooden chest. Lapis walked over to it, withdrew a key from her coat, and opened the chest. 

Inside was a box. On its front was a grey knob, surrounded by numbers delicately etched in a semicircle around it. Almost no elf or vampire would be able to identify what it was. But the humans had built more and more of these when the war began, albeit with slightly different forms and numbers.

It was a radio. 

Lapis turned the knob clockwise through the list of numbers, stopping finally when the knob pointed at 115.9. For a moment, the box began to buzz. But then, it abruptly stopped, and was replaced by the hurried sounds of someone shuffling through a room.

“Hey, Akito.” Lapis greeted the person on the other end.

“Hi, Lazu.” The response was slightly distorted by the inner workings of the radio, but was the voice of a human male.

They talked about many things, as they had for almost six years now. Sometimes Lapis talked about her day first, and other times Akito did. Today, it was the latter. As Lapis listened, she thought silently about things she would never say aloud.

“Lazu, did you hear about the latest news?”

Sorry, but my name is Lapis, not Lazu. That’s just an alias.

“The army says it’s only a matter of months before we wipe out <Shadow>. Isn’t that good?”

But I’m not human. I’m one of the elves you’re trying to wipe out.

“Just wait for a bit; the army will rescue you soon, okay?”

Sorry, but I’m not a captive. I’m an enemy.

Akito concluded the recap of his normal day. “Enough about me though, did anything interesting happen to you today?”

Lapis thought back to her day and smiled softly before speaking into the radio with her usual dramatic voice: “I think I met my deuteragonist.”

At least that wasn’t a lie.

~~ On Fairy Wings ~~
Blue jolted awake. Her head hurt. She rubbed her eyes in an effort to dispel the sleepiness from her mind, before opening them long enough to take in her surroundings. Three concrete walls formed a grim enclosure around her location on the floor, and the fourth was a set of thick iron bars. Even by the nicest definition, Blue was in a prison cell. She groggily tried to remember what happened yesterday after she and Lapis escaped Oni Island, but her mind was too exhausted to really remember anything. Sighing, she began to study her wings listlessly. 

“You’re awake? Good morning.”

The fairy glanced up. A teenaged boy was looking at her amiably from outside the cell. He had jet black hair and one red eye; the other was hidden behind an eyepatch. Behind his back were two neatly tucked wings, also a deep black. Though she had never seen a vampire before, Blue thought to herself that this was what their human form probably looked like. “It’s not like I can sleep well in here,” Blue responded, gesturing at the cold concrete floor irritably. The vampire smiled gently and spoke in an apologetic tone. “Sorry. I’m sure we’ll find something better for you as soon as possible.”

In terms of first impressions, Blue certainly liked this one more than that of a certain elf. The vampire continued. “My name’s Mitsui. What’s yours?”

“Bluebi — just Blue.” 

Mitsui nodded softly. “Nice to meet you, Blue. Let me know if you need anything.” Blue shrugged snarkily. “Can you let me out of here? I’m literally harmless, you know.”

“Sorry. I believe you, but I don’t think Lapis would be happy about it.” Mitsui shook his head. Blue wasn’t surprised, but she still slouched disappointedly. Seeing this, Mitsui put his pointer finger to his chin and thought for a moment. “Would you like some breakfast though? I don’t think Lapis would be angry if I gave you food.” 

Despite being a fairy, Blue still got hungry, and now she (and her stomach) was realizing that she hadn’t had anything to eat since she first came into the world. She nodded eagerly. “What is there?”

“The chefs aren’t awake yet, but I can probably make some toast with honey if —”

“Wait, wait, wait, wait, you have honey?” Mitsui seemed taken aback for a moment, then smiled. “We do. Would you like some?”

“Yes please!”

Mitsui left Blue’s cell for a few minutes, and Blue heard the sound of light footsteps going up a flight of stairs. It wasn’t long before he returned with a plate of toast and a jar of honey. “I wasn’t sure how much you wanted, so…” He trailed off at Blue’s salivating face, sat down, and slipped the food through the bars of the cell. Blue pounced on it, took the spoon out of the jar of honey, and took a large bite.

“So gooooooooood!”

Mitsui laughed gently as Blue began to scoop spoonful after spoonful of honey into her mouth, almost as if she were drinking it. In between alternating bites of toast, Blue explained with her mouth full: “I’ve only heard of honey, but I’ve never actually had any.”

“Why? Isn’t it pretty common?”

Blue mumbled with her mouth full: “It was pretty rare for me.” Mitsui put his pointer finger to his chin again and was about to ask a question, but was suddenly interrupted by a voice charging down the stairs. Lapis’ long coat trailed behind her like a billowing cape and her dark blue eyes sparkled brightly as she leapt down the steps and struck a pose in front of Blue’s cell. 

“Blue! You insolent fool! You dare believe you can escape me? You can run, but you can’t hide!”

Blue, for her part, glared upwards with her face covered in honey and her location squarely ensnared within the concrete walls. “I’m not escaping though? How do you even expect me to escape?” Lapis grinned. “I’ve just always wanted to say that line. It sounded pretty good, right?” Mitsui let out a soft apologetic laugh as he and Lapis exchanged greetings. All the while, Blue stared daggers at Lapis as the fairy scraped away the last residues of honey in the jar. 

Another set of footsteps echoed down the stairs, in a much less dramatic manner than Lapis’. Another vampire appeared outside the cell, lazily rubbing her red eyes. She trotted over to Lapis’ side and leaned sleepily on her shoulder. Lapis smiled and spoke to Blue: “Blue…”

“Jaquavious,” Blue interjected resentfully, irritated at Lapis for a multitude of reasons. 
“You’re still stuck on that? Anyways, meet Evie. Evie, meet Blue.”

“Hi…” Blue started to greet her.

“Don’t talk to me, you piece of pixel art.”

“...Wait what? Why would you say that? Screw you! You suck!”

Mitsui once again laughed apologetically. Lapis patted Evie on the head, who immediately transitioned from her look of intense disdain towards Blue to a contented face that could rival a pet cat. Lapis spoke to her: “Evie, could you deal with the patrols this morning? I’ll be going out right now to test Blue.” 

“Leave it to me!” 

Blue, who was directing her attention at what little molecules of honey remained, glanced upwards in surprise. “Wait what?”

“See you, Evie, Mitsui.” Ignoring her, Lapis grinned. In a flash, the girl sitting in the prison cell was gone, and Lapis was now clad with wings and full black armour. Mitsui and Evie, who were probably seeing this for the first time, watched in awe. 

“But more honey…” Blue began.

“Sorry, I couldn’t hear you, did you have any objections? It might be hard for me to hear since I’m in my fairy’s mecha suit right now.”

“Ughhhhh, fine. Fine!”

Mitsui and Evie could only stare as Lapis flew up the stairs, exiting in exactly the same manner with which she entered. 

~

Lapis and Blue flew low along the coastline, weaving in and out of islands that Blue had never seen before. 

“Blue, I’m sorry for forcing you, okay? So stop the silent treatment?”

“...” Lapis couldn’t see the fairy’s physical form, but if she did she was sure Blue was pouting sullenly. She continued, sighing.

“Blue…you’re acting a lot like a tsundere who was caught saying she likes the main character. And we’ll have character overlap if you keep going, so please stop?”

“........”

The pair began circling a large outcrop jutting out from the ocean. Blue had still not talked since they departed from wherever they were this morning.

“Did you know I’m good friends with the chefs? I don’t think they would object if I hypothetically asked them to swap all the honey with canola oil. From a distance, they look exactly the same, you know.”

“Wait, wait, wait, wait. I’ll talk! I’ll talk!”

“I think it would be interesting, though. Maybe I’ll ask them when we get back—.”

“Heyyyyyyyy!” Blue interrupted, flustered. Lapis laughed, and though Blue couldn’t see her face she knew she was smirking. “That’s better. Save us both the trouble next time, okay?” 

Blue pouted but decided to drop the topic. Besides, from her shared view with Lapis’ visor, she could see the vast expanse of ocean dotted sporadically by islands whose landscapes were filled with scenery she had never seen before. She piped up excitedly. “So what are we even doing here? Exploring?”

“I told you! I want to experiment with you!”

Blue was confused. “What does that mean?” In response, Lapis let out a snort. “Isn’t it only natural for me to undergo a training arc and accustom herself with her abilities?” She spoke as if the answer was obvious. Blue interpreted that response as Lapis wanting to test out her unconventional, newfound weapon. Blue — the weapon herself — sighed. “I don’t think you need a training arc, since you figured out how to fly me in two seconds.” She was certain that it wasn’t easy to first learn to control a fairy: it was like controlling an extra limb. But Lapis had figured it out seconds after jumping from a cliff and trying it out for the first time.

Lapis grinned. “Well, it’s only natural for the main character to be a genius.” Blue made a mental note to never compliment her again as the elf continued. “So? How exactly do fairies work?” Blue thought for a moment. Though she had only been born into the world yesterday, she had been somehow preprogrammed with basic knowledge about herself and the fairies.

All fairies were mecha suits that could be activated and deactivated based on the user’s desires. These mecha suits all had a flight propulsion system as well as three abilities — attacks of sorts — that could be used in warfare. However, the appearance of the fairies, and what those abilities did, depended on the fairy’s attribute. 

Blue continued. “Though you can use abilities an infinite number of times, each ability has a certain reload speed and ammo count. My abilities are…”

“Don’t tell me!” Lapis interrupted. “Just tell me how to use them.”

“So pushy…” Blue thought to herself irritably. “Aren’t you a self-proclaimed genius?” She asked Lapis.

“I’m also self-proclaimed friends with the chefs.” Lapis replied, unconcerned.

“Ughh, fine! How are you controlling your flight right now?” Lapis tilted her head for a moment, thinking about the question. “I guess right now I imagine moving a joystick in my mind?”

That sounded correct to Blue: she knew that fairies were controlled by intuitive mental imagery in some way. “It’s the same thing with the weapons, but imagine you’re pulling a gun trigger with your hands.” Lapis moved her right arm slowly in a circular motion as if trying to get used to it. She held it up against the light and paused for a moment before casting it dramatically to the side. “I think I got it! Let’s see…”

The mecha suit’s bottom thruster whirred into action, firing a pale blue streak of what almost seemed like a comet’s stardust into the crisp spring air. Lapis spoke resoundingly, at an audience whose presence couldn’t be seen yet tangibly felt. “Behold! I am Lapis of the infinite dawn, ruler of the five seas and all within the two ethereal skies! You who gaze upon me,  receive this epitaph!” She stretched out her right arm, and the deep blue channels coursing through it began to glimmer ephemerally. “Azul Void!”

Attack name aside, Blue thought Lapis maybe was a genius. As much as she hated to admit it.

The light through her arm raced towards a focal point at the center of her palm, then vanished. A split second later, twenty thin rays of blazing light streaked through the air and vanished in the blink of an eye, leaving behind a dispersing trail of smoke in its wake.

Both of them stared in silence at the small cloud of debris that flared up as the bullets hit a pile of rock a few hundred meters away. They spoke at the same time.

“Wait, that’s amazing!”
“...That’s it?”

Blue let out a heated shout, her voice echoing indignantly in Lapis’ headgear. “What do you mean, that’s it? It’s a high-velocity Gatling gun with five rounds of ammo and fast reload…”

“But it’s just a regular boring gun? That’s like saying that plain toast is your favourite breakfast! Or that you like someone because they have a nice smile! Or that a fairy is supposed to be a short young girl with tacky wings!”

“S-shut up! What was the point of the last one?”

Lapis sighed, disappointed, and shook her head as if she was scolding a young child for not living up to expectations. “What a waste of my signature move. Surely you have better weapons, right?” She pointed her left arm at the sky and fired. A small missile encased within the suit’s forearm rocketed up into the air, and having found no targets, sputtered out and fell back into the ocean. Lapis and Blue followed its trajectory until it slipped into the water with an unassuming splash.

“...”

A sigh once more. “Blue, do you really want the main character to have less flashy attacks than our army’s mass-produced fighter jets?”

“That’s your problem!”

 Lapis shrugged. “I guess so…you said three abilities, right? What’s your last attack?” Blue, still unhappy at having her pride hurt, replied while pouting. “Try visualizing a trigger around your chest area, near where the fairy crest is.”

Lapis grinned childishly. “Could this be a secret ultimate attack? My suit opens up to reveal a prismatic ray of destruction that razes the world…” The suit did open up, but instead of a prismatic ray of destruction, a black lump tumbled out. It dropped below them and unfurled like a wide parachute, catching the wind briefly before it too vanished into the ocean. 

“...Blue, that doesn’t seem like an ultimate attack. What is that?”

“It’s just a shield to absorb enemy projectiles.” Lapis let out her breath unhappily. “You said three abilities? So that’s all you can do?” Blue reluctantly nodded and replied, “Yeah. All fairies have one ability for defense, one for attack, and one miscellaneous." 

In a voice thinly veiled with disappointment, Lapis complained: “Can someone get me a refund on this fairy?”

“It’s not like I was tearfully begging you to take me!” And as Blue thought back to when she had indeed tearfully yelled at Lapis to complete the contract, she blushed. “S-shut up!” Lapis chuckled in spite of her disappointment. “Anyways, don’t fairies have attributes? What’s yours? Bluebird of mediocrity? Or Bluebird of technology from the stone ages?”

Though the power of fairies were largely unknown by <Shadow>, they had fought enough fairies to realize that each fairy had a different attribute with which their powers were based off of. For instance, one of the largest threats to their army currently was the fairy of the stars, which could summon an instant-kill black hole at will. Lapis hoped Bluebird had something just as flashy.

“Rude! I have a perfectly good attribute! I’m Bluebird of flight.”

Blue could almost sense Lapis’ sarcastic stare despite neither being able to physically see the other. “Wow, your attribute is the one thing shared between all fairies? I’m impressed!” But for the first time since they had tested her abilities, Blue spoke with a hint of pride: “Say what you will, but I’m the best at flying out of all the fairies. Using the joystick like you are right now only uses a small fraction of my potential, since I have a unique flight system!”

From within the suit’s helmet, Lapis perked her ears with cautious interest. “Okay, so what should I be doing?” Blue sniffed disdainfully, sensing an opportunity to get revenge on Lapis for the past hour. “You’re a genius, figure it out.” Lapis just grinned. “And if I were to remind you that I’m friends with the chefs?” Blue said no emphatically, and Lapis continued, her grin spreading further. “If I were to secretly add a laxative to every jar of honey?” But instead of giving in, Blue confidently played the trump card she had recently thought of: "Should the main character really be using threats and blackmail instead of her own effort?” Lapis burst into laughter, and if Blue were physically present she would have ruffled her hair. “I’m proud. You’ve grown so much from being so naive.”

“...”

“Very well. I’ll show you the true power of the main character.”

Despite the bold proclamation, Lapis continued to hover in midair, motionless. Blue began laughing, gratified; Lapis ignored her and muttered to herself: “Does that not work? Then how about…”

One moment, Lapis and Blue were completely stationary. The next, a high-pitched hum emerged from within the suit. The mecha suit’s thrusters roared to life, and as if they were yanked up by an invisible string, they shot up into the blue sky up above. Through the suit’s visor, Lapis saw the clouds tumble endlessly into and out of view. As they continued accelerating like a rocket, her peripheral vision began to blur and warp around her. Blue’s elated screams rang in her head as if they were directly next to each other. 

They broke through a thick layer of clouds and found themselves in a completely different place. Contours of white cotton candy dotted the landscape below, forming a world of flying mountains and valleys. The bright blue sky they saw above was now replaced by an endless indigo. Though they had started in a vertical orientation, Lapis and Blue were now parallel to the ground miles below, as if they were a plane. 

“Cool…” Blue breathed out.

But then, they were suddenly freefalling. One of the thrusters went silent, and they began to rotate like a top as their view of the clouds was replaced with that of the sparkling ocean. Lapis cursed under her breath, trying to grasp any concept of flight that she could. But without any physical controls, the two continued plummeting to the ground, and her efforts just caused them to flip end-over-end as well. Now, the wind was buffering against them almost as hard as when they had first accelerated, and Lapis felt her heart fall to her stomach and move in a hundred different directions at once.

Blue seemed like she was having the time of her life, seemingly unconcerned about the imminent death approaching.

The ocean was now a thousand feet away. Nine hundred. Eight hundred. Despite her surreal predicament, Lapis began grinning. She flexed four of the fingers of her right hand. 

“I see. So I have four engines, and I control the thrust for each of them to fly?” 

Blue’s voice was completely unaffected by the noise of the wind “Yeah.” And then under her breath: “It’s kind of impressive that you figured that out so quickly.”

The ocean was now five hundred feet away. Lapis’ words were strained by the freefall, but Blue still heard them clearly:

“I’m not done here! After all, the main character… is made to soar!” 

Two hundred feet. Lapis’ two wing thrusters roared to life at the same time that the two at her rear cut out abruptly. They began to pitch back upwards. Just before they smashed into the ocean, Lapis pulled out of the dive, skimming the whitecaps breaking above its surface. And Lapis pulled away from the ocean and flew upwards. They spun gently and stopped, hovering, just above the clouds.

Blue’s grudge towards Lapis just a minute earlier was all but forgotten. She exclaimed joyously: “So fun! That was amazing!” Lapis smirked. It was obvious her disappointment had completely disappeared as she laughed. “What else did you expect?”

For a while after, neither spoke as they stared in awe at the alien world around them. Blue was the first to break the silence: “You figured out how to fly long before the nosedive, right? Did you cut it so close on purpose?”

Lapis winked — a futile gesture as Blue couldn’t see her face, but perhaps it was meant for someone else. “Well, the reader expects a show!” As Blue sighed with what even she had to admit was mock discontent, Lapis began to steer them back through the clouds. “Wanna give them a better show?”

Blue didn’t care about whether the readers were real or not as she answered with delight. “Okay!”


---------------------------------------------------------

LAPISNOTES

BLUEBIRD OF FLIGHT

Propulsion System: 4-thruster. Three secondary thrusters parallel to the coronal plane (two on the wingtips and one at the bottom of the fairy) and one main thruster parallel to the transverse plane (also located at the bottom of the fairy). The secondary thrusters provide lift in normal flight while the main thruster provides thrust. Pitch and roll are achieved by varying differential thrust between the secondary thrusters. All thrusters are unique in that they can apply reverse thrust.

Speed: Extremely Fast
Unique Traits: Propulsion System
Name: Self-explanatory. From the Twitter logo, obviously

Attack:
<GATLING GUN>
A regular-ass Gatling gun affixed to Bluebird’s right arm
Medium range, 5 rounds of ammo, fast reload speed, fast unload speed, medium damage

Defense:
<PARACHUTE>
A barrier which drops from Bluebird’s chest and freefalls to the ground
About the same size as Bluebird’s body
High survivability — a large portion of attacks that impact this will be nullified, though for very high-powered attacks it will break
Only one can be “on the field” at a time; has a ten second timer and will be destroyed after it

Misc:
<MISSILES> (Offense)
Regular-ass homing missiles; launcher is affixed to Bluebird’s left arm
Very long (theoretically infinite) range, 2 rounds of ammo, long reload speed, very fast unload speed, high damage
Homing is “dumb” and can be foiled by going behind sufficient cover with the right timing

---------------------------------------------------------
Blue and Lapis were now back on the island where they had woken up this morning. It occurred to Blue that she didn’t know what the island was, but the aerial view made it seem like a military base of sorts. 

They were walking on a well-paved path weaving through the undergrowth of the island. The moment they had landed, they were intercepted by two vampires; Blue now recognized them as the same two she had seen when they landed last night. She guessed that they were familiar with Lapis or at least with her antics; both resumed their guard shift without any further questions, though they casted dubious glances at the fairy.

The sky was glowing a brilliant red hue; it was just before sunset. They had spent all day doing what Lapis called the “training arc”. Through experimenting, they found that each of Blue’s abilities reloaded in about six seconds, and that there truly was infinite ammo (as the numerous gaping holes in the landscape could attest to) by some means of magic. And they had done a lot of flying. As the only fairy who flew horizontally like a bird instead of vertically like a traditional jetpack, Blue expected Lapis to get stuck somewhere on the learning curve. However, she had to admit that despite being annoying and arrogant, Lapis was a quick learner. 

They were out of mecha form, and Blue had taken on her appearance as an almost-regular young girl with sky blue hair. Lapis studied her. “So, you have two forms? A human form and a mecha form?”

“Kind of,” Blue responded. “When I’m not in a mecha suit, I can either look like this or I can…”

Blue suddenly vanished, leaving only a few tokens of shimmering light in her place. But Lapis could still hear her voice as Blue continued. “...Get rid of my physical form and become a voice in your head. Just like in my mech form, we can communicate with telepathy this way, and I share your senses.” 

“So you have a ghost form, a mech form, and a small child form.” Lapis summarized, without using her voice. Clearly the telepathy worked, as Blue let out an indignant protest upon hearing the words “small child.”  A thought crossed Lapis’ mind, and still conversing without words, she asked curiously: “So you can switch from child to ghost by yourself? Is there anything else you can do on your own?” 

Despite Lapis still not being able to see Blue, she could somehow sense the fairy shake her head. “No, you can decide what form I’m in, and you have full control over my mecha capabilities. And, you control when I die.”

Lapis seemed surprised by Blue’s last sentence. “What do you mean?”

Blue slipped back into her “small child” form.  “Fairies that aren’t bound by a contract are immortal. But now that I’ve made a contract with you, I can die either if my health reaches zero in my mecha form, or if you die.” Despite the topic, the young girl’s voice was casual, almost as if she were describing the weather.

“Hmm…” Blue could tell Lapis was thinking something dumb. “So you can’t die any other way?” Blue shook her head. “I don’t think so. Wanna try? I’m curious myself.”

Lapis pulled out her umbrella from within her coat. It was similar to the one that had been destroyed in her fight against the oni yesterday. “Why do you have another —”, Bluebird began. But she never got a chance to finish. Lapis swung the umbrella downwards, and its well-polished edge came down on Blue’s head as sharp and solid as any cleaver. But just before it sliced through her hair, the crest on Blue’s body emanated a radiant golden glow. A spherical barrier encircled the fairy’s body, preventing her from harm. 

“That’s amazing!” Blue exclaimed as the shield faded away and allowed her to move again. Lapis let out a satisfied grin. “I christen this ability ‘plot armour’”.  

“Don’t give it such a terrible name!” Blue launched a barrage of holographic wings at Lapis, who took the pains to gracefully dodge them despite knowing they weren’t real. 

Their meandering banter had taken them to the end of the path. Now, a large metal door loomed in front of them. It seemed to have been built within the island itself; there wasn’t anything else signifying civilization here. “What is that?” With eyes shining, Blue ran ahead. But just as she was about to excitedly open the door, Blue found herself dragged into Lapis’ consciousness. “That’s not how you open those.” The elf said. “Watch and learn.”

Blue was far too curious to care about the correct way to open doors. But still, she reluctantly watched through Lapis’ eyes as she planted both feet in front of the door. She pushed her cap downwards so it obscured her sparkling blue eyes and adjusted her cloak so it fluttered off to one side. And then, with one swift motion, she pushed the door open. Warm wind escaped from inside the entrance, catching Lapis’ cloak. Light flooded out from the entrance, plunging Lapis’ face in a shadowy darkness. From behind, she looked just like a hero from a fairytale, one that commanded respect and authority.

Blue, for her part, couldn’t believe she had to wait so long just for Lapis to pretend to be the main character. Even so, she decided it wasn’t worth it to get irritated. Lapis took a few resolute steps into the entrance, and Blue stared at the setting in amazement.

The space that stared back at her was impossibly huge, stretching so far and wide that Blue might have thought they were still outside. Artificial lighting rained down from high above, illuminating buildings made from metal and glass. Between the entrance and those buildings were rows and rows of tables, each stacked with food. People were seated at the tables, having interrupted their dinner to focus on Lapis and Blue. No, that’s not it, Blue realized. They weren’t really people, but hundreds of elves and vampires eating together.

Lapis’ entrance was somehow effective, as despite the large space and number of people serving as audience, they all stared in silence at her, surprised. Then, Blue heard the sound of a bench near them being pushed back. An elf, roughly the same age as Lapis, got up and walked briskly towards them. She had light brown hair done in neat braids, and piercing green eyes that did little to hide their anger. 

“Lapis, where were you? I was so worried! I wake up and hear that you’ve captured a fairy, and then you’re just gone for the whole day?”

Lapis, seemingly oblivious at the wrath of the elf talking to her, spoke telepathically to Blue in a flippant tone. “Blue, this is Erin. She’s the princess of the elves.” 

“...Right. In that case, shouldn’t you reply to her?”

Unaware of the conversation happening in Lapis’ mind, Erin continued in a resigned tone. “You can explain yourself later. Just hand over the fairy. It’s dangerous and an unknown weapon, so we can keep it in the cages and kill it later.”

“Aww, so fussy. Are you my mom or something?” With a grin, Lapis forcefully reverted Blue back to a child. With a petulant yelp, the young girl materialized in a heap on the smooth concrete floor of the room. Blue heard gasps of amazement from around her. Many of them hadn’t seen her before, since Lapis had arrived so late at night and left so early in the morning. As Blue quickly got to her feet, Erin, who had seemed ready to attack Lapis for calling her ‘mom’ as a joke, asked Lapis: “Is this the fairy?”

“Yeah.” Lapis shrugged, smiling. 

A long pause. “...I guess fairies are far too valuable a weapon to kill. And besides, you have control over it, so it should be safe.” Surprised, Blue met Erin’s eyes. Her anger was completely gone, and her gaze was infinitely friendlier as the elf muttered. “It’s obviously not just because you’re cute though. That would be a stupid reason. Obviously.”

“...”

Blue turned to face Lapis, who laughed. “Just be glad you’re adorable, Blue. Otherwise…” She mimed her neck getting cut off.

Of the four elves and vampires I’ve met so far, why is only one of them normal…

Erin headed back to her table, gesturing for Blue and Lapis to follow. Despite Erin being the supposed princess of the elves, Lapis walked beside her like it was natural. “You aren’t off the hook, Lapis,” Erin glared sharply at Lapis, who grinned in response. “Threats, coming from the person who went all kyaa-kyaa upon seeing Blue?” Erin started to retort, but then she glanced back at Blue and, as if to prove a point, lost all interest in arguing. As she started a friendly introduction to the fairy, Blue thought to herself that for a “dangerous and unknown weapon”, she was getting quite the warm welcome. 

The elves and vampires around them finally unfroze and began devouring their dinners. A loud, rowdy chatter arose between the tables, no doubt centering on Lapis and Blue.

Surprisingly, Mitsui and Evie, the two vampires who Blue had met this morning, were also at their table. As Erin sat down and pulled out the bench for Blue as well, Mitsui smiled lightly and dipped his head in greeting towards the three. Meanwhile, Evie could not have seemed less interested in Blue. Instead, she quickly piled food onto a plate and handed it to Lapis, who had taken a much more dramatic route to a seat beside Blue. She grinned at Blue as she began eating, and Blue sighed.

But even Lapis’ antics couldn’t distract Blue from the food. It smelled ridiculously good. Though Blue didn’t know how the elves and vampires lived during the war, she couldn’t have imagined their food was as good as this.

Not that I’ll complain…Blue realized the only thing she had eaten in the past two days was a slice of toast with honey, complimentary of Mitsui. She was beyond famished. Lapis was not taking good care of her. 

As Lapis began picking out her vegetables, Blue gratefully accepted the potatoes and fish Erin had picked out for her. Not caring about anything else, she dug into her food.



--------------------
