--------------------

~~ A War In Name Alone ~~

Ever since Lapis had first chanced upon the radio on the beach, she had talked with Akito starting every night at ten. It was a strange friendship. They had never met in person (and Lapis hoped that at least until the war was over, they never would — after all, Akito was human). But still, despite the lies Lapis told Akito, lies which he unwittingly accepted, they thought of each other as friends.

That was why Lapis was worried. Right now, she was sitting on the ground in the middle of a surprisingly sparse bedroom — the only thing of note was the radio and a study table with multiple cabinets. It had been four days since the night Lapis met Blue. Since that night, Akito hadn’t connected to the radio once. 

The clock in Lapis’ bedroom read one minute to ten. Deciding it was time, she turned the knob clockwise, letting it rest on the number 115.9. Unlike the past four days, the static was interrupted almost immediately. “Hi, Lazu! Sorry! I’m so sorry!” Akito greeted her hurriedly, as if he had been waiting there for a while. 

It took a moment for Lapis to register her alias. After all, Erin, Mitsui, Evie, and a certain young girl all called her Lapis. “I respect your audacity to ghost the main character. What happened?” Akito apologized again, and Lapis could almost visualize him bowing his head repeatedly. “Sorry! But,” it was rare for Akito to act so excited, “Guess what? You won’t believe it, but I made a contract with a fairy!”

Lapis’ words caught in her throat. Despite fighting with the fairies for over a year, humans knew almost as little about them as the elves. According to Akito, they never appeared in public, let alone interact with humans enough for a member of the general populace to be able to make a contract. And Akito hadn’t dropped any hints of this happening before. Lapis stared at the radio in silence as Akito continued: “So I’m in the army now! Though”, he added with a bit less childish joy, “I haven’t received any training yet. They told me I’d learn on the job….”

“That’s amazing! Has the world finally recognized your potential to be a main character?” The radio conveyed her awed voice, but not her thoughts. Akito said he was going to be in the army? He’s going to fight?

It was a proclamation Lapis was much more willing to accept if she really were Lazu — a normal eighteen-year-old human, part of a colony taken captive by the evil alliance <Shadow> from the time she was born. But not when she was Lapis, an elf fighting against that very army. Still, she masked her thoughts and enthusiastically fired question after question. “How did you meet them? Did they come cloaked in a mysterious light, with a booming voice that came from the heavens? And what attribute are they?”

Akito seemed overwhelmed by the torrent of words — ironic, since Lapis should have been the one struggling to find a response. “Well, it was a normal day, and —”

“But of course! That’s how all stories start.” Lapis interjected. Akito smiled before continuing.

When he was done, Lapis nodded appreciatively. “Akito, you really are a great storyteller. Though,” she added, “you’re terrible at talking! Where was the drama, the expression? Why did you only speak in monotone?”

“Wha-wha, um…” Akito stammered, too taken by her first compliment to care about her other complaints. Lapis asked her other question again. “So, what attribute is your fairy?” 

“I don’t know. My squadron members told me not to worry about that yet, so —”

“So you’re telling me, you get an ultra rare, completely mysterious weapon, and the first thing you do is not acquaint yourself with its abilities? The reader is sorely disappointed in you, Akito.”

“Sorry…” Akito responded automatically before addressing Lapis: “But my fairy is a bit weird, so I didn’t want to do anything rash. Besides, I don’t have any experience with fairies. I don’t know why they even accepted me…” What Akito considered rash, Lapis considered worldbuilding, but intrigued by Akito’s first words, she didn’t comment. “Weird? Weird how?”

“For one,” Akito began, “he has a physical body. My squadron members don’t have fairies like that — they only have fairy cores, which aren't actually fairies but just replicas of their powers. Just like the rest of the humans, they've basically never met a fairy before.”

That matched what Lapis thought before she had met Blue. The (admittedly few) soldiers they had captured during the war never mentioned they had a weird mythical humanoid companion, let alone talk to them. Furthermore, their level of understanding of the fairies was barely higher than the elves. They only knew they were mecha suits that one made a contract of sorts with; after, the user gained the ability to fly and a few other fairy-specific powers that depended on their attribute. Even the most basic things Lapis had learnt after meeting Blue, such as that fairies were sentient, weren’t things that the human army knew. 

It seemed that rather than actually fighting, the fairies had found a way to give the humans copies of their powers. Furthermore, they avoided interacting with the humans.

On that note, Blue was the first actual fairy <Shadow> had seen. This, despite being at war with them for a while now, and despite making multiple attempts to search and destroy them before that.

Of course, Akito didn’t know Blue existed and could not have guessed Lapis was thinking these things. He continued. “But even though Chiaros looks like a regular human, he —” 

Chiaros…now that’s a name befitting a fairy. Lapis thought to herself. Elsewhere on the island, Blue shivered. Somehow, she got the feeling that Lapis was thinking something bad about her. 

Akito agreed, before continuing tentatively, “He seems braindead? Like he doesn’t respond to anyone, wanders around aimlessly if I let him, and never talks.”

“Can I try? How do you even summon him?” Lapis decided to use the opportunity to gather some intel on the fairies, and none the wiser, Akito relented. “Sure. And, honestly, it’s hard to explain how I summon him. I just think about it, and it happens?” Lapis nodded. At least that much was similar between her contract and Akito’s. There was a faint rustling on the other end of the radio, and then Akito spoke up. “Okay, he’s here.”

The vague garbling of the radio was not enough to dull Lapis’ grand introduction. “Greetings, Chiaros! I am Lazu of the infinite dawn, supreme commander of all between the two ethereal horizons.” Unlike with her introduction to Blue, Lapis didn’t add that she was commander of <Shadow>. And unlike with Blue, her introduction wasn’t interrupted midway. In fact, it was met only with the faint buzz of the radio. Lapis sniffed disdainfully. “Not the most appreciative audience.”

“Sorry. Try asking ‘What’s the time?’” As if on cue, a blank voice responded robotically: “It’s three in the morning.” Lapis turned to look at the clock on her wall. It wasn’t ten minutes past ten. She laughed. “Are you sure that isn’t just a glorified broken clock?” Akito sighed. “And I really did want to help the war effort too. Since you’re there…”

His words trailed off at the end, but Lapis could still barely hear them. 

“The main character always leads her friends to a better future.” Those were the words Lapis had spoken to Blue, words which she had called the first rule of being the protagonist. Akito was one of her friends. And if he really did fight against Lapis and the elves…

Well, when have things ever been easy for the protagonist?

Lapis exclaimed with her usual grandiose confidence. “‘Since you’re there?’ So it’s all for me? That’s kind of sweet, Akito.” Complete silence on the other end. Lapis laughed. “Hey Chiaros, is Akito not responding because he’s blushing really hard right now? Tell him I look forward to his heroism, okay?” Chiaros didn’t acknowledge her, though Akito began to stammer profusely. “Uh, um…”

The door suddenly opened. Someone’s feminine voice cut loudly through the radio. “Akito, let’s make — what is that?” She asked tactlessly, walking into the room without so much as a knock on the door. Lapis heard Akito scramble to cut the connection, and before he could she teasingly commented:

“Wow, a fairy and a girlfriend in four days? I respect—"

Static filled Lapis’ room. She reached over to the radio and turned its knob counterclockwise. There was a quiet click, and the radio went silent. She got to her feet, picked up the radio and gently lowered it into the bottom drawer of her study table. Her gaze lingered on it a moment longer than usual, and then she withdrew a key from her coat pocket. She locked the cabinet, tugging on it twice to make sure it was secure. 

So Akito’s going to fight in the war, huh? That wasn’t part of the script.

From the depths of her thoughts came a smile, one poised to take on the world and win.

Guess I’ll have to improvise.

~

A beautiful sunrise illuminated the island — yet another day in the recent streak of excellent weather. It was days like this that made the island’s inhabitants wish their artificial lightning were replaced with a clear view into the clear March sky. 

Blue was leaning against the wall of her “room”, facing the grid of iron bars that fenced her off from the outside world. Her lodging was infinitely more comfortable than they had been five days ago, on her first night here. Thanks to Erin, she now had a warm fluffy bed crammed into the cell and an assortment of games and stuffed animals to keep her company. A soft woolen rug lay sprawled out across the floor, looking markedly out of place inside the cold, harsh concrete.

They apparently didn’t have a vacant room, and so Erin had initially offered to let Blue sleep in her room. Mitsui had to convince her that the princess of the elves probably shouldn’t let a fairy sleep in the same room as her.

Mitsui was seated quietly across from her. He seemed to be awake no matter how early Blue woke up, and came in everyday to hand her a glass of honey water. Blue quite liked his company. He provided some much needed calm, unlike a certain pretentious elf.

For the past few mornings just after Blue woke up, Mitsui had taught her about the archipelago. Blue had a feeling teaching her should have been Lapis’ job, but apart from growing increasingly better at controlling Blue's weaponry, the elf didn't contribute anything of note.

Most of humanity lived on the other side of the ocean in five self-sufficient complexes. Each was completely indoors, able to generate its own natural resources, and able to house and sustain tens of thousands of people each. Those complexes had been built by an ancient, much more technologically advanced civilization which had been destroyed long ago. Though the current humanity had inherited the large megacities, they didn't have any understanding of how that technology worked. Each complex was given a name based on an alphabet long lost to time. Complex Beta was the furthest North, followed by Gamma, Delta, Epsilon, and Zeta. 

In addition to those complexes, that ancient civilization had also built a test city. It was in the middle of the ocean, on an island an hour's flight away from the mainland where the humans resided. This complex, built into the island itself, was much smaller than the other cities, and it generated resources on a much smaller scale. Even so, it was enough for a few thousand occupants.

This place was called Complex Alpha. And ever since <Shadow> invaded it two decades ago, it was their home. 

Now, on her fifth day waking up in a cell on the second floor (the floor numbers counted downwards) of Complex Alpha, Blue had expected Mitsui to continue explaining where he left off. But today, Mitsui had offered a change of plans. Right now, they were playing Uno.

Blue frowned as she took a sip of the honey water beside her, warming her parched throat. Despite having been given an excellent starting hand, she was close to lost (though Mitsui was surprised she even knew how to play in the first place). And she had clearly overestimated how good she was at the game. 

“Uno.” Mitsui spoke gently. If it has been anyone else using that tone of voice, Blue might have thought they were mocking her. But she had never seen Mitsui express anything beyond his usual quiet composure. Sighing, half from disappointment at losing and half from annoyance at herself, she placed down a card at random and let Mitsui win. 

“You were close, Blue.” Mitsui began to collect the cards in a neat pile.

Blue sighed again, though she appreciated the comforting words. “If Lapis were here, she’d tease me to no end for losing that.” Mitsui chuckled, but before he could respond, he was interrupted by dramatic footsteps from behind him. Lapis flew down the stairs. Her usual black cloak fluttered behind her as she somersaulted into a graceful landing beside Mitsui. She grinned at Blue. “What do I need to tease you about?” 

Blue glared at her. She had obviously been there for a while, but only chose now to make an appearance. “How long were you eavesdropping for?”

“Enough to make an opportune entrance!” Lapis responded, chipper as ever. She turned towards Mitsui, and they greeted each other warmly. Lapis turned her attention to the cards in front of them. “What is that? Can I join?” 

“Do you not know what Uno is?” Blue replied testily. Lapis was unfazed by her attitude though. “Board games are far below my level. But teach me the rules!” Before Blue could respond, Lapis forced her into her ghost form and she vanished in a flash of light. A moment later, she reappeared beside Lapis, outside of the bars of the cell. Mitsui observed, amazed, as Blue dusted herself off. (Unfortunately, this jailbreak couldn’t happen regularly since Lapis blocked Blue from entering her ghost form without permission.)

“You're getting too accustomed to this.” Blue complained underneath her breath. 

“It's only natural for me to get accustomed to someone I have complete control over!” Lapis responded with a bright smile. But before Blue could make an effort to wipe that smile off her face, Lapis continued: “So how do you play?”

Mitsui taught Lapis the rules without protest, much to the annoyance of Blue, who had been planning to gaslight Lapis for a bit. Finally, Lapis declared, “Okay, I think I can win now.”

“Hmph, you didn't even know how to play ten minutes ago! What makes you think you can beat me?” As Mitsui began dealing the cards, Lapis laughed boldly. “We shall see. The main character always backs up her words.” 

Blue decided to ignore her delusions as she placed the first card. 

…

Less than five minutes later, Lapis placed the last card in her hand with a dramatic flourish. “Uno!” As Blue stared at her, dumbfounded, Mitsui applauded quietly and commented: “you don't have to say Uno when you win, Lapis.”

“It sounds cooler, though!” 

Blue finally regained the ability to question Lapis. “Didn't you say you never played before?”
“Yep, I’ve never played.” Lapis responded. Mitsui nodded, confirming her statement. “But I did say I had to back my words! So anyways,” Lapis smirked at Bluebird, “Mitsui won the one before, so you’re the only one without a win, you know. And who was it that said ‘what makes you think you can beat me’? 

Blue glared spiteful daggers at that smirk. “Screw you! I’m winning the next one! Just wait!”

Lapis grinned and began helping Mitsui collect the cards. “Try your best!”

It took one hour for Blue to win her first game. But before that, Lapis was completely undefeated.

~

Mitsui, Blue, and Lapis were now outside, on the first floor of the complex. It was the impossibly large communal space that Blue and Lapis had first made their grand entrance in. The long rows of dining tables and benches were sparsely populated with elves and vampires, eating breakfast. Many of them had greeted Lapis with a surprising amount of formality and respect — something Blue still couldn’t understand despite being here for a few days now. Maybe it was because Lapis was the first person to bring back a fairy.

The three of them were standing off to one side of the complex, next to a food stall where one could pick up breakfast. They were all eating virtually the same thing — a simple sandwich with lettuce, tomatoes, and an unidentified slice of meat — though Blue had successfully managed to add honey to her sandwich. From what Blue could determine, everyone in the complex ate the same thing for their three meals, though they only gathered together to eat at dinner time. 

Lapis turned to Mitsui as she took a bite of her sandwich. “When do you think she’s done?”

“I’m not sure.” Mitsui shook his head. Blue noticed that Mitsui’s slice of meat was a different colour than hers as she piped up. “Who’s she?” 

With her mouth still full, Lapis replied: “The people’s princess.” She gestured to a pottery stall adjacent to them, where Erin was chatting with the stall’s owner. Blue caught pieces of their conversation.

“That’s really amazing! But what about this piece? How’d you make it so smooth?.”

“Glad you asked, Erin! So you see…”

Erin listened, her full focus on the stall owner. In the few glimpses of morning life that Lapis afforded Blue the past few days, Erin was always checking in on the residents of the complex. Blue had to admit that, despite her odd first impression, Erin was rapidly growing on her.

A bored voice came from behind them. “What’s taking Erin — I mean, the food source — so long?” A vampire walked up to them and stood next to Lapis’ side. Turning around, Blue recognized her as the one who had called her a work of pixel art, Evie. 

“Hi, Evie.” Lapis and Mitsui greeted her at the same time. Evie left Mitsui’s salutation unanswered and only responded to Lapis, though Mitsui didn’t seem bothered by it. “Food source?” Blue asked the vampire, and she looked at Blue as if realizing she was there for the first time. Instead of answering the question, she turned to Lapis. Pointing at the fairy, she asked, “Can I drink some of her blood?”

“Why are you asking her for permission and not me?” Blue interjected indignantly. 

Evie gave her a disdainful look, but before she could say anything, Lapis reprimanded her. “No, Evie, don’t drink her blood.” Surprisingly, Evie obeyed without any grumbling, and went back to nibbling at her sandwich.

Blue also found it surprising that Lapis stood up for her, but then the elf continued with a smirk: “Though, if Blue’s not being compliant, maybe I’ll change my mind.”

“Screw you!” 

“Oh, is that some non-compliance I sense?” But just as Lapis seemed poised to unleash Evie’s vampiric fangs on Blue, Erin came running up to them. “Sorry I’m late!”

“Hey, Erin.”

“Finally. We can get on with this waste of time.”

Mitsui and Evie had vastly different responses to the princess of the elves. Lapis, took the middle of the two sides. “Morning. What took you so long today? We were waiting for all of breakfast.” Erin shot Lapis a withering glare. Clearly, she still hadn’t fully forgiven Lapis for her antics the past few days. “Now you know how I feel every day.”

Lapis grinned. “Aww, do you normally feel this lonely and abandoned? That’s cute.” Despite her words, Blue thought her tone lacked its usual teasing edge. Maybe she was feeling some remorse. Ignoring Lapis, Erin asked the rest of the group: “Anyways, what are we doing today?” 

“We’re doing something?” Blue looked at Erin, interested.

“Yeah! Every Sunday, us four go out and spend the morning together.”

That explained why Lapis hadn’t barged down the stairs this morning and whisked Blue away to their so-called training arc. 

Mitsui spoke up. “Do you all want to give Blue a tour of Complex Alpha?” Blue still hadn’t received a proper tour, and thanks to Lapis, spent more time far away from the island than on the island itself. Seeing the stars in Blue’s eyes at the thought of finally exploring her new home, Lapis and Erin both nodded. “That sounds good.” Behind them, Evie muttered to herself: “Whatever.” 

Mitsui flashed an apologetic smile towards Blue. “Don’t worry about her. She may say all that, but in reality she —”

“Shut up, pirate-wannabe.” As Evie stomped away, Mitsui gingerly touched his eyepatch. 

After some arguing, the group decided to start at the lowest level of the complex. They took an elevator to the fourth floor, two levels below Blue’s sleeping quarters. The brightly lit space was not nearly as high nor large as the communal first floor. Even so, it had enough space for a dozen or so conveyor belts, snaking their way to a series of mobile pods much like the elevator they had arrived in. 

Three elves were beside the conveyor belts. They were loading apples into large plastic crates, and Blue thought to herself that the red of the apples was markedly out of place amidst the colourless shades of the room. 

Erin returned the bow the elves gave her. For some reason, they bowed to Lapis as well, who proclaimed in a dramatic voice: “Raise your head, my dear allies.” They greeted Evie with bows as well, though they ignored Mitsui.

“Blue, how much do you know about the complex?” Erin turned to the fairy and asked. 

“From what Mitsui told me, it's a self-sufficient indoor city created from ancient technology?” Erin nodded. “That's basically it. And what you see here is what makes it self-sufficient.”

Blue didn't think the room looked like much, but Erin continued. “We can't access it, but deeper within the complex is ancient technology that provides all the natural resources we need.” As if to prove her point, Lapis pressed a few buttons on the conveyor belt with a dramatic flourish. The machinery sprung to life. A few seconds later, an apple rolled off the conveyor belt. She shrugged and added: “I imagine it's the same for the human population. There’s virtually no shortage of natural resources.”

Tentatively, Blue poked the apple before taking a bite. It was real. She looked back at them with eyes shining. “So this is where you get your honey from?” Mitsui laughed gently. “Literally everything but honey. We have to make honey.” Blue was a bit disappointed at her dreams of infinite honey being dashed. But she quickly connected a few loose ends in her mind. “No wonder why this doesn't feel like a war.” 

“What do you mean?” Evie, who had been silent and brooding by Lapis’ side the whole time, spoke up. “Well,” Blue tried to explain her logic, “in stories, I thought wars meant that everyone was always starving and suffering, and there wasn't any medicine and a lot of dead people. But with this, you wouldn't have to worry about food or supplies. But I’ve never felt this was like a war.”

In her first few days on the island, there were far more commodities than Blue had expected during wartime. The people in the complex seemed so peaceful and happy she never would have guessed they were in the middle of a war.

Erin thought for a moment. “Well, it's certainly a part of it. But honestly, it's also because this war is a war in name alone” 

Blue tilted her head in confusion. “So it’s not really a war?” 

“Blue, apart from food and all that, what’s the biggest resource to have in a war?”

Despite not fully grasping what Erin was getting at, Blue tried her best to answer. “Hmm…maybe weapons?” Lapis stretched out her hand to ruffle Blue’s hair and grinned as the fairy tried unsuccessfully to evade it. “Truly an intelligent child!”

“Screw you!” Blue looked to Erin for backup, but she seemed all too pleased to watch something cute getting petted (though she tried her best to hide it). Erin continued: “Right now, both sides of the war are in a stalemate because they have no way to create new weapons.” She listed off the three main weapons with her right hand. “The fighter jets we use are an ancient technology that no one knows how to make, vampires obviously can’t be created on demand…”

Lapis smirked. “Unless Mitsui finally gets together with his childhood crush.” Mitsui just laughed softly. 

“...and if the humans could create new fairies, they would have won the war a long time ago.” Truthfully, Blue was the first new fairy that they had seen since the war had started. And, Lapis thought a bit ruefully to herself, I guess Chiaros will belong on that list soon.

Blue finally understood what Erin was saying. “So because both sides can’t make new weapons, they’re too scared to commit to attacking the other?” Mitsui smiled, which Blue took as a sign that she was right. “The war was brutal in the first few months. But now, both sides mostly just go on patrols. Actual fighting isn’t as common these days.” 

“That’s also why our army hasn’t taken any offensive measures in the past month. I’m perfectly happy with our current situation.” Lapis took a break from ruffling Blue’s hair to add on, and Blue took the opportunity to finally duck away. The fairy pointed out in an aggrieved voice: “You’re implying that you have any say over what the army does.”

Mitsui, Erin, and Evie all looked at her curiously, though in the case of Evie that curiosity was as sharp as daggers. “I mean, she does? She is the commander of the army.”

“I see…wait. Whattttttttt?” Blue’s surprised shout echoed bounced between the metal conveyor belts.

Lapis gave Blue a disappointed glance. “Weren’t you listening to my intro? I literally said I was Lapis, supreme military commander of the elf and vampire army <Shadow>.” Blue thought back to Lapis’ self-introduction during the pit. Now that she thought about it, Lapis had said something like that. And it also explained all the bows and greetings Lapis received. Though…

“You can’t blame me for that! You also said you were the main character and that some gemstone gave you eternal youth. How was I supposed to know that wasn’t another fantasy of yours?” 

Erin and Mitsui both laughed. Even Evie, as much as she respected Lapis, was trying to hide a smile. “That’s a fair point,” Mitsui conceded. Lapis, meanwhile, looked a bit chagrined. It was a new look for her.

“Well, if you ignore all the disappearing and reckless behaviour, she’s not actually a bad commander. Pretty bad, but…” Erin began to somewhat vouch for Lapis, but trailed off. All four of them looked at Lapis.

“This army is screwed, isn’t it?”

“Definitely.”
“Maybe.”

Evie glared resentfully at Blue. “Stop insulting Lapis, you jetpack ripoff.” But then she thought for a moment: “Although…”

“Et tu, Evie?” The supreme commander of <Shadow> could only protest helplessly as her subordinates chipped at her dignity. 

~

Their tour meandered from the fourth floor through the first floor, travelled along the outside path Blue and Lapis had taken yesterday, and finally reentered the large metal door leading into the complex. Blue found that the layout of Complex Alpha was a lot simpler than it had first appeared.

The exterior of the island was encircled by a ring of manned watchtowers. A paved path connected all the watchtowers in an oblong semicircle, snaking past fruit orchards, strawberry fields, and, to Blue’s delight, a few honeycombs. It provided easy access to the first floor of the complex, where all the public facilities were constructed. Below that floor was a vast grid filled with long rows of pods three meters wide and across. Narrow beds were jammed into each, below a nondescript clock hanging on the wall. On the other side of these pods was a study table with a few cabinets. Not only was this floor home to Blue’s cell, it contained the living quarters for the elves and vampires. 

Erin didn’t allow them to go to the third floor. That was where they kept humans in captivity. 

Lapis had saved one place for last. At the very edge of the top floor, directly opposite the main entrance, the ground dropped off into a shallow ramp and funnelled into a long, starkly lit corridor. Inside the corridor was a complex control panel that controlled a set of doors.

Behind those doors was an aircraft hangar. It was carved directly out of a cliff face within the island. Numerous sleek metal contraptions dotted the impeccably maintained platform, looking like they were ready to take flight. These fighter jets were known as Nightjars, and they were piloted by the elves as their contribution to the war.

Now, sitting on the floor of the aircraft hangar, Lapis and Blue watched some elves maintain the Nightjars. A slice of vivid blue sky framed their view perfectly. 

A short distance away, Evie was sucking Erin’s blood, having overpowered her and pinned her down. Evie was the strongest fighter in the complex, and it didn't help that Evie genuinely saw Erin as a food source — she found her blood tastiest. Though, Erin had a surprisingly content look on her face as she pet Evie’s wings; the vampire was too preoccupied with her blood to care. 

As Lapis listened to the familiar commotion around her, Blue slipped into her mind — far more natural feeling than it suggested. “What is it?” Lapis communicated with telepathy, and Blue did the same. 

“I’m curious, why exactly are we fighting? No one’s actually told me before…If it’s as simple as humans being scared of vampires, then there’s no need to actually fight, right?” Lapis cracked a wry grin. “Unfortunately, it’s a simple answer too. Vampires need to eat humans to survive.”

“Oh. I see.” For better or worse, it was a far less nuanced answer than Blue was expecting, and her reply lacked her usual enthusiasm. The two of them sat in silence for a while, listening to the bantering around them. Until finally, Lapis stretched one hand outwards, as if grasping at the beautiful piece of sky just ahead of them.

“Conflict is inevitable. But just like I said…” The elf got up from the floor, back resolute.

“...The main character will grasp a better future.”

A moment of silence. Blue could already guess Lapis’ next words.

“Heh. Pretty cool line, right?”

“I couldn’t care less!”


--------------------

~~ First Interactions ~~
It was a few minutes past ten at night. Lapis was sitting on her bed, radio in front of her. She was sharing the details of her day with Akito.

Of course, there were many things she couldn’t share with Akito. Though she felt guilty about it, most of her daily events were fabricated to some extent. Right now, she was telling him about a short, childish girl that was extremely fun to poke fun at — an alias for a certain blue-haired fairy — when a sound caught the attention of her long ears. It sounded like someone was knocking lightly on a wooden door. Akito heard it too; the sound was coming from his end. 

“Sorry, one sec —”

But just as he was about to get up and investigate, Lapis heard the sound of a loud explosion through the radio. Two voices, distinctly different from Akito’s, overlapped as they spoke up.

“Hey, he’s trying to turn it off!”
“I’m on it!”

“T-tanner? V-violet?” Akito addressed the owners of the voices. They belonged to the two other members of Akito’s squadron.

Before Akito could hide the radio, a young man rushed through where a locked door should have been. The assailant moved with a gracefulness that defied his tall, well-built frame and placed Akito in a restraining hold. Akito quickly stopped resisting. The man - Tanner - spoke with a carefreeness that didn’t really seem appropriate for the occasion. “Don’t worry about it!” Akito looked at the door, which had been blown right off its hinges, and glanced silently back at him before averting eye contact.

I am definitely worrying…

Meanwhile, the other person — a girl about Akito’s age named Violet — approached the radio. She examined it briefly before speaking into it. “Hello, box?” No answer. Violet tried again. “Akito keeps talking to you, and he gets flustered whenever we try to figure out what he's doing.” 

“Uh, um, sorry…” Akito muttered, his voice barely above a whisper. Still, Lapis didn’t respond, even though the radio was still on. Akito figured she was probably up to something. Violet frowned at the silent box before turning to Akito.

“Are you schizo?”

In response to Violet’s frank question, Akito could only stutter incoherently. A laugh escaped the radio in front of them. Violet’s eyes lit up. “I knew it! Who are you?” Inwardly, Akito cringed a bit at the slightly accusatory introduction, though he was pretty sure Violet didn’t mean it like that. Lapis also seemed to take it in stride. “I am but a dismembered artificial brain, created by my master Akito.”

“Wait, really?” Violet turned to Akito, impressed. “So you’re actually smart?” 

“Uhh, t-that’s, um, she’s joking.”

Violet sounded a bit dejected as she replied: “Seriously? Okay.” Akito apologized, though he probably didn't need to. He had tried to avoid revealing the radio to Violet and Tanner in the belief that it would be a massive hassle. That belief was quickly coming true.

Tanner finally released his hold on Akito, who instinctively took a few steps backwards away from the nearest person. He plopped down next to the radio, and with a much more polite greeting than Violet’s, asked: “What’s your name?” Lapis had been waiting for that question. “Glad you asked! ”She took a dramatic pause: “I am Lazu of the infinite dawn, supreme commander of all between the two ethereal horizons. What is yours?” 

Akito had heard her introduction many times, mostly because there was a period of time where Lapis had recited it to him every day in an attempt to perfect it. But even though Tanner was hearing it for the first time, he didn’t skip a beat. He was all too happy to play along as he matched her animated tone word for word. “I am Tanner of the stars, curator of the celestial heavens. It is an honour to meet you, Lazu.”

Lapis grinned at his introduction. “Splendid! The honour is mine. And,” she addressed Tanner’s companion, “what of the naive girl’s name?” Akito couldn’t tell if Violet purposefully ignored Lapis’ jab or if it just didn’t register in her mind. “I’m Violet,” she responded bluntly. 

“...”

Clearly, Violet hadn’t realized that she should play along. Tanner leaned in and whispered something to her. Violet scratched her head for a moment, before speaking: “Oh! I’m Violet of the wind, who flies with wings swift as the north gale.” The inflection of her voice was completely off, but Lapis decided to let it slide. 

They all turned to look at Akito. Even Lapis’ eyes, unseen though they were, were boring holes through the radio. Akito knew why. Even still, he tried to feign ignorance. “U-uh, umm, sorry, do I also need to do that introduction? I-i mean, you all know me…”

“Why not?”
“Yes.”
“Can’t wait to hear it, Akito.”

Those last words were from Lapis. Akito could only imagine how big a smirk she had on her face at the moment. His pitiful attempts at getting out of the situation were promptly rejected by Tanner, Violet, and Lapis. 

“U-uhh, I-I-I’m…”

Violet and Tanner had convinced Akito to move to the living room in their base. Now, the three were seated around a circular table in the middle of a cozy, relatively normal communal space. A small kitchen was situated behind them; right now, Violet was listening to the radio from there as she sipped a glass of water. There was also a television, CDs of movies, and game consoles, all imported from one of humanity’s main complexes

Shortly after they had moved places, Lapis had launched into a flurry of questions about who they were. She had gleaned that Tanner and Violet were the other members of Akito’s squadron, and that they were also fighting in the army. Their fairy’s attributes were what they hinted at in their introductions: Tanner was the owner of the fairy of the stars while Violet’s was the fairy of the wind. Of course, Lapis couldn’t deny that she had ulterior motives for asking these questions. She was surprised at how readily they gave up that information. On one hand, they were still under the assumption she was a regular human and not one held captive in Complex Alpha, but on the other, there was a decent chance they wouldn’t care even if they did know.

Akito’s fairy, Chiaros, was slumped across a couch next to the table, staring blankly at empty space. He was still “defective”, unfortunately — he couldn't respond to basically any stimuli. Though the fact that he even had a physical busy was novel to Violet and Tanner. 

Lapis had also questioned Akito about Chiaros’ attribute. The answer was a bit obvious in hindsight — he was the fairy of time. Lapis was unusually excited upon hearing that.

“The power of time is so cool! You can say so many cool things with it?”

“Like what?” Violet had asked. 

“When you’re blocking someone’s attacks, you can say ‘Not this time!’ Or when the enemy is about to kill you, you can say: ‘What time is it?’” 

Tanner caught on quickly. “Oh! And then when they’re confused, you say ‘It’s time to win!’” 

“Exactly!” Time was definitely a better attribute for the main character than something like, say, flight.

Somewhere an ocean away from Akito, Tanner, and Violet, Blue sneezed. She got the feeling Lapis was thinking something bad about her.

The conversation on their fairies and daily activities continued for a long time, with Lapis managing to avoid talking about her own circumstances. Now, for the first time since she had turned on the radio, Lapis looked at the time on her clock. Somehow, it was already the start of a new day. As Akito excused herself to get a glass of water, Violet placed her head down on the table and complained to herself: “So sleepy…” Meanwhile, Tanner called out to the other side of the living room. “Chiaros, what time is it?”

“It’s four in the morning,” came the robotic reply. Tanner laughed and was about to say something, but Lapis spoke first. 

“Tanner, Violet?” She was aware her voice sounded a bit awkward. Right now, instead of being the main character, she sounded just like a regular girl.

“What is it?” Tanner responded, carefree despite the sudden shift of tone. There was a weighted pause. And then, Lapis finally pushed out the words she wanted to say — words which she didn’t have the heart to say with Akito around. 

“Please make sure Akito doesn’t die in this war. Please take care of him.”

It was the one thing she didn’t have the right to say. Especially right now, when they were on two sides of the ocean. When they were on two sides of the war. 

But luckily, Violet and Tanner didn’t know that. Two replies came instantaneously, one much sleepier than the other.

“Okay.”
“No problem!”

Alone in her room, Lapis smiled. She had been expecting them to agree, for obvious reasons. But still, she smiled. As if that one moment had been scripted, her next line of dialogue contained her usual dramatic flair.

“Then the main character owes you two a debt!”

~

Blue was standing alone in the aircraft hangar. It had been almost a week since her tour of the island, but this was only the second time she had been here; she desperately wanted to move her feet and explore the area. Blue stayed put, however. If she did move, Lapis would then take great happiness in trapping Blue in her mind. 

Lapis was also in the hangar. She was pouring over a few official maps of the archipelago with a group of vampires. Every once in a while, she would mark some of the places with a red marker. It was the closest Blue had seen Lapis act like a commander, though as with most things she did, she couldn’t gauge how performative it was.

Something else caught Blue’s attention — a spot of black, which despite being many miles away, already blocked out a visible portion of the sun. The black figure headed straight towards the hangar. As it got closer, Blue could make out bat-like wings, a giant, grotesque head, and two sharp talons that looked like they were ripped straight from a fairy tale. It was the first time Blue had seen a vampire that wasn’t in human form. This particular vampire had miscoloured eyes. One was red, just like all the vampires in human form. The other was pink. 

The hangar was already massive, about the size of a football field. Even still, the vampire would not be able to fit in it. He slowed down as he reached the lip of the platform, transforming back to human form just in time to avoid scraping the rock cliff and walls. His pink eye morphed away in the transformation, replaced by the eyepatch of a pirate. 

Almost all of the elves and vampires in the hangar ignored Mitsui as he walked over to greet Blue — it was probably a normal occurrence for them. “Good morning, Blue.” 

“You didn’t come this morning! And — What happened?” A series of deep, bloody gashes rendered Mitsui’s face nearly unrecognizable, reaching past the collar of his shirt and into his body. Mitsui shrugged, suggesting he was used to it. “It's fine,” he reassured Blue, “vampires have excellent strength and regeneration.” Sure enough, even as they were speaking, the gashes were noticeably changing colour, replaced with a more skin-like hue. 

Lapis quickly abandoned her chiefly duties when she saw Mitsui landing. As she went over to greet him, Mitsui continued: “And sorry I couldn’t see you this morning. Lapis gave me a longer shift.”

“Why would you do that?” Blue turned to the elf, who shrugged. “The story’s more cohesive if he makes a later entrance.” She didn’t comment on Mitsui’s injuries. It seemed both of them were used to it. Mitsui explained the real reason. “There’s been fighting to the northeast recently, so Lapis is assigning more patrols there.”

As if on cue, one of the inside pockets of Lapis’ coat buzzed to life. Lapis reached in and took out a small handheld radio. The three of them listened to the message. “Six fairies. 42 kilometers 33 degrees. Not yet engaged in combat.”

“Six? That’s a lot.” Mitsui commented. 

Lapis, meanwhile, focused on the latter half of the message. “That’s near an island…” she muttered. And then she turned to Blue. “We’re heading out.”

~

They flew just above the surface of the water. Blue, with her unique thrust system, was so much faster than regular fairies that it would take them only ten minutes to reach the location.

In mech form, Lapis viewed the world through a visor built into Blue’s body. While it looked like a regular, see-through piece of glass, multiple digital indications were projected holographically onto it. Among them was a health bar, an ammo count, thrust levels, and a radar interface. It was very video game-esque. There was also a compass, which Lapis was using to orient herself 33 degrees northeast. Blue shared the same view as Lapis, in addition to being able to communicate with her telepathically.

Visibility was excellent today. Blue could see further than the range of her radar, and already, they spotted the first signs of an aerial skirmish. A couple of the elven army’s fighter jets, Nightjars, were blasting off high-powered railgun attacks at what looked like a magical wall of fire. There was nothing else in sight, except for the vast ocean and a small island a few kilometers off to the west.

Lapis checked her radar. And then, instead of diving straight into the fight, she applied power to her right wing thruster. They banked sharply, veering to the west. 

“Where are you going? They’re fighting straight ahead!” Blue pointed out.

“Just a hunch.” Lapis chuckled. They circled around to the west side of the island. As Lapis expected, its densely packed forest blocked Blue’s radar. That likely meant that the enemy fairies couldn’t sense Lapis either. Blue realized what she was going for. “A surprise attack?”

“Elementary, my dear grade schooler.” Lapis continued as Blue let out a yelp of indignation: “Though if all goes well, our target won't be the fairies fighting up there.”

“What do you mean?”

But Lapis refused to elaborate. Instead, she applied power to the main thruster on her rear. They began accelerating forwards, straight into the forest.

“Wha — hey!”

But Lapis didn't slow down. Thanks to Blue's instantaneous throttle response, she could deftly maneuver the mecha suit through the narrow gaps in the trees. As they skimmed the forest floor, kicking up pinecones and dead leaves in their wake, Lapis asked Blue: “Do you remember the most dangerous threats in the human army?”

Surprised by the sudden question, Blue tried to remember back to a conversation she and Lapis had before. “I think it's the fairy of poison, fairy of the stars, and —”

The endless line of trees covering their line of sight suddenly opened up. For a split second, they were in a clearing. And they weren't the only ones. Blue glimpsed a translucent yellow orb, about the size of a human, in the center. 

“Look out!”

But before Blue could register what they were about to crash into, Lapis fired the two ammo stored in her left arm. Two missiles instantly unloaded and zeroed in on the orb. As Lapis gunned the thrusters and climbed steeply upwards, a violent explosion rocketed the forest beneath them. 

They broke through the canopy and traced a tight arc in the clear spring air. Blue complained irritably to Lapis: “Hey, stop being all mystifying and tell me what that —”

Bzzzzt.

A low crackle. The air to their left shifted slightly, uncomfortably. And then, it parted ways.  A bolt of lightning coursed through the gaps, racing the flash of midnight in the clear noon sky. Lapis grinned. “There he is. So that wasn’t enough to kill him.”

Floating a few dozen meters above the island was that same orb Blue had glimpsed. Now that Blue had a better look, she could see the orb wasn’t solid. Instead, it was made from what could only be described as electricity. Sparks formed around the orb, as did the stream of lightning that was blitzing its way towards them, which seemingly had a mind of its own as it bore down on them. 

There was a human within the orb. No, not just a human…Blue realized, it’s a fairy. Within their formless, flowing body was a fairy crest the colour of ivory. 

It was the third notable threat in the human army. Circe, the fairy of charge.
---------------------------------------------------------

LAPISNOTES

CIRCE OF CHARGE

Propulsion System: Normal
Speed: Normal
Unique Traits: Paralysis
Name: From the word circumire, root for the word circuit

Attack:
<SERIES>
User visualizes nodes in space, a ray of electricity flows from user through nodes. 
Nodes can only be made approximately 2m apart from the nearest node
Low Damage, Instantaneous reload speed, unload speed depends on user capabilities, Long range
Paralyzes targets for two seconds. Paralyzed targets will only be affected by external forces (and inertia) and cannot apply any internal forces to move, though they can still move their body parts.
Is interrupted when Circe is hit with either a non-physical fairy attack or any non-trivial physical object. Interrupting resets all nodes created, destroying <Series>
When user is grounded during activation of <Series>, user can still visualize nodes but by default, electricity will not flow between nodes
User can choose when to activate <Series> in this case

Defense:
<Break>
User teleports to any node they have already made. 
Instantaneous reload and unload speed, range depends on <Series>
This counts as an interruption and will destroy <Series>

Misc:
<Parallel> (Offense)
User can connect any/all pairs of nodes, and a high-damaging, non-paralyzing current of electricity passes through them 
Instantaneous reload and unload speed, range depends on <Series>
Can only be activated when the user creates a node at their location. This will mean a loop, or a circuit, has been created.

---------------------------------------------------------
While Blue was realizing that, Lapis was busy monologuing. “Circe and Nova are dangerous because if they can find some place safe to cast it, their attacks can trap enemies in a large radius and guarantee a kill on them. I figured the humans would try hiding one of them on land and lure us into the trap with a diversionary attack.”

“Never mind that! What is that lightning?”

 “Circe’s first attack, <Series>. Circe emanates a steady ray of lightning from her body. Deals little damage but paralyzes the things it touches.”

“Stop narrating!” Blue yelled at her. Lapis only grinned. “The reader needs an explanation!”

Just before <Series> was about to reach them, Lapis dove to the left. The stream of electricity coursed past them with a loud crackle. But just as quickly, it reversed course, chasing them down once again. 

“Is it homing?” 

“No, Circe can control it herself.”

The flashes of darkness and light zigzagged through the sky. Though Blue held unparalleled agility and maneuverability in the air compared to fairies, <Series> was faster, and Circe seemed to be getting used to Lapis’ well-timed dodges. 

“How do we get rid of that thing?” Blue asked, as Lapis feinted left before instantly applying maximum differential thrust between her left and right engines. Circe took the bait for a split second, enough for Lapis to evade the attack once more. Even so, the margin between them and the lightning was narrower than ever — it had only been a few inches away from grazing Blue’s wingtip. Lapis responded: “We just need to interrupt Circe. Any attack on that orb will work.”

“Then what are you waiting for?” 

“Not yet…” In the top right of her visor, Lapis saw that she had finally reloaded both her missiles. “...Now!” She fired one of them, and it quickly homed in on Circe. But then she climbed upwards, launching into a half barrel-roll until she was directly facing the stream of lightning charging towards it. Lapis fired the second missile straight at it. 

In the peripherals of their visor, Blue saw the orb suddenly disappear, leaving no trace as if it never existed to begin with. Instead, the yellow formless cloak was now directly in her field of vision — behind them, instead of in front. The first missile, having lost its target, didn’t have enough time to reorient itself and crashed into the island.

“What on earth?”

“<Break>. Circe teleports to a point on her lightning from <Series>.”

True to the name of the ability, the lightning chasing them instantaneously disappeared. Circe tried to use <Series> again in the hopes of teleporting once more. Before she could, the second missile slammed into her. 

As the explosion cleared, Lapis grumbled: “How little damage does that do?” Apart from being knocked back, there seemed to be no effect on Circe, and she formed the orb of electricity around her once more. But Blue was much less negative. “His crest is pretty dim though! He’s on low health.” Circe’s crest, which had been a slightly dull ivory before, was now nearly extinguished. Lapis estimated that <Missiles> probably did 40% health, and that Circe had teleported before her second missile on the island had hit. 

“So one more hit? Bring it on.”

But instead of directing <Series> towards them, Circe cast it North, towards the other fairies. By now, they were well aware of the attack on Circe. Three of them were headed directly towards Lapis while the others kept the elves and vampires distracted.

It was the smart move, given how valuable the fairy of electricity was to the human army according to Lapis. But Blue didn’t care much for that. “He’s running away! Hurry up and shoot!”

Lapis looked at her visor. A timer indicated that it took ten seconds for <Missiles> to reload. That was far too little time. Blue seemed to realize this too. “Then your gun?” Lapis still hadn’t used <Gatling Gun>, embedded in her right arm. But instead of acknowledging it, she burst into laughter. She had that smile on her face. 

“The main character must gamble every once in a while.”

Lapis applied power to her third thruster — the one that controlled her pitch. She brought Blue into a shallow dive and whispered two words.

“Full power.” 

The trails of blue flame rolling off Blue’s wingtips faltered. The whirring stopped. There was silence. 

Then, the world became a blur.

Lapis and Blue streaked across the ocean. The fairy crest on Blue’s chest shone brighter than ever, surrounding them in a vivid light the colour of the sky. As the thrusters roared, drowning out the noise of the wind, the black and blue bullet rocketed straight towards the orb of electricity.

Despite Lapis’ dramatics, Blue was unimpressed. “How is this any faster than just using our gun?” Lapis, meanwhile, continued her maniacal laughter. “You do not understand my genius, Blue!” 

The gun had less range than her missiles. Circe had more than enough time to teleport to safety were she to try. Instead, Lapis was betting on something else. <Series> could be interrupted by any attack, even if that attack was weak. Or even if that attack wasn’t really an attack. For instance, if a large object were to crash into them with sufficient momentum, Circe’s attack would be interrupted.

And right now, they had a ridiculous excess of momentum. 

A second before Lapis crashed into Circe, she used <Break>. But it wasn’t to teleport to safety, as Blue expected. She teleported only a few hundred meters forward, before instantly using <Series> again. This time, it was pointed straight at them.

Lapis’ gamble was believing that if she was reckless and tried to crash straight into Circe, she wouldn’t run away, though she very much could. Instead, she would counterattack. Now, the tendrils of lightning stretched towards her. Once it did, it would paralyze them, essentially placing them into momentary freefall and unable to reach Circe. This ability was partially why Circe was such a dangerous threat, and why Lapis believed she would counterattack.

“As expected,” Lapis whispered.  

Lapis applied maximum pitch up, exposing her fairy crest to the electricity. Her chest opened. A black parachute jettisoned out from the hidden compartment. The electricity collided with her defensive ability. It immediately began spreading across the parachute's black edges, trying to find a way to Lapis and Blue. 

But the electricity had been slowed enough. Before it could reach them, Lapis slammed into Circe. 

The impact took a few hitpoints off Lapis’ health and sent both fairies tumbling down together. The electricity finally slipped past the parachute. It crawled up Blue like an invasive vine, and though Lapis felt no pain, her HP dropped by a few more points and she felt her horizontal velocity slow drastically. It was as if those vines were restricting all forces on her except gravity.

Not like it mattered.

Lapis raised her right arm high in the air. As the two hurtled towards the sea below, it began glowing a deep, ephemeral blue. The muzzle of <Gatling Gun> flickered violently, then burst into light. 

“I am Lapis of the dawn!”

Lapis pointed the gun down, directly at the crest of Circe below her. 

“Just fire alrea —”

“AZUL VOID!”

But nothing fired. Her visor flashed red. A warning message appeared on her display, informing her that her right arm was inoperable. Lapis’ plan hinged on the electricity not destroying any of her functions. Evidently, that wasn’t the case. 

Her plan foiled, Lapis applied power to the thrusters in her wings, hoping she could generate enough thrust to break out of their freefall. None of Blue’s engines had been affected. But even so, they were unable to move — a result of the paralysis effect generated by Circe’s <Series>. All Lapis could do was watch the ocean rushing up to meet them.

“Blue, you suck!”

“How is any of this my fault?” 

There was a loud splash, followed by another in quick succession. The two fairies plunged into the water. 

Lapis registered her HP drop by a tenth — ecrashing into the water at that speed was bound to do some damage. Reorienting herself through the column of bubbles rising to the light above, she saw Circe trying to do the same a few meters away. They had also been affected by the fall. Their fairy crest was now emitting an exceedingly faint glow. 

They locked eyes. Lapis’ <Missile> reloaded one ammo. She began to point it towards Circe.

But before she could do so, a ray of electricity streamed out from Circe. Fast as lightning, it encircled Lapis and Blue before looping back towards Circe. A low crackle began spreading through the water. 

All fairies have three abilities, at least one of which was offensive and one defensive. In Circe’s case, their third attack was also used for offense. When the fairy of electricity looped their <Series> back to them — in other words, when they completed the circuit — they could connect every pair of points on the circuit with a powerful bolt of electricity. That bolt did far more damage than <Series>, and its power scaled with the size of the circuit. It was an attack Lapis had named <Parallel>. 

Now, that loop was connected. 

Lapis fired up her main thruster. Its response time was so fast that they could just barely dodge the initial current from <Parallel>. But that mattered little. They were facing the fairy of electricity — in water. 

“Oh sh —”

There wasn’t even enough time to finish thinking that thought. Current surged through the saltwater, and through Lapis and Blue. 

~

Three fairies had gathered above the water where Lapis and Circe had crashed into. They all had their weapons trained on the circle of coursing light that had permeated the water for almost a minute. Even so, they weren’t prepared for the speed of the black mecha suit as it spiraled out of the water and careened southwards. 

It was lucky they weren’t.

An array of warning alerts flooded the peripherals of Lapis’ visor as she and Blue headed back to Complex Alpha. Lapis dismissed them all. She couldn’t dismiss her HP indicator though, which was a sliver above 10%. 

Even though the mecha suit looked completely intact (it was unheard of for any sign of damage to visibly appear on a fairy), they most definitely had suffered severe losses in functionality. Notably, Blue’s right wing thruster was damaged and could only output 50% power; Lapis was having a difficult time maintaining level flight. Despite these “injuries”, Lapis didn’t feel the slightest sense of pain. It seemed that while the user was piloting the mech, they were protected from all physical injuries or sensations.

They flew in silence for a few minutes, following the compass south. Lapis spoke up: “Could have been worse.”

“Screw your gamble.” It was undoubtedly Blue’s voice in Lapis’ mind. But the voice was much quieter than usual, and had none of the child’s typical liveliness. 

“Hey, it would have paid off if not for someone’s right arm being useless. Besides, while we didn’t kill Circe, we did foil their trap, so I think it was a success.”

Blue didn’t answer, which was a bit abnormal. They continued their wordless flight until suddenly, Lapis informed the fairy of a change of plans. “Blue, we’re landing at the island up ahead.”

An uncomfortable pause. “Okay.”

Despite only having her main thruster being fully functional, Lapis guided them to a smooth landing on the soft sand of a beach. The island was close enough to Complex Alpha and their regular patrols that they weren’t at risk of being pursued by the fairies. Besides, while Circe wasn’t dead, they were critically injured, and as such, the fairies would have retreated back to their side of the ocean. Lapis transformed out of her mech form. A girl with sky blue hair appeared beside her, momentarily levitating above the sand before dropping to beside Lapis’ feet. 

“...”

The only uninjured parts of Blue’s body were her head and body. Her left arm had been disfigured beyond recognition. All over her body were severe burns, plainly visible past the charred fabric of her once-white dress. A gaping hole had been torn into her right side as if she had been eaten alive by some wild animal. Blue’s grey eyes were clouded; she was barely conscious. 

For the first time since Blue had met her, Lapis stayed completely silent. She didn’t move for a long time. Until finally, she sat down on the sand and placed Blue’s head in her lap. She ruffled her hair. 

Blue wasn’t in any position to object. All she could do was stare up at the sky.

Lapis sighed. “You should tell me these things.” Lapis had thought it was weird she didn’t suffer any repercussions from taking damage while piloting the mecha suit. Now, she knew all the pain and injury she should have suffered had been transferred to Blue. 

“It’s you. Would that have changed anything?” Blue’s reply, though quiet, didn’t waver. 

“Of course.” Lapis didn’t hesitate. “The main character would never willingly hurt her friends.” She looked down at the expression on Blue’s face. “Well, you don’t have to believe me now.”

Even without her saying that, Blue wouldn’t have believed her. Truth to be told, she didn’t even think Lapis would care about her injuries, seeing as she couldn’t die from them. That alone provided some sense of vindication. Blue’s voice regained a bit of strength as she answered: “Am I supposed to believe the person who decided to fight a fairy of electricity underwater?” 

“It wasn’t supposed to be underwater.”

“You’re not the one who got electrocuted a million times over. It hurts so much right now!” 

“l’ll give you what you want, so please stop guilt-tripping me, okay?” Lapis cracked a grin, and Blue smiled. Even though her injuries hurting a lot wasn’t a lie, guilt-tripping was her intention. After all, this was more or less the first time she held something over Lapis. 

“I’ll take a jar of honey, then. You’re good friends with the chefs, right?”

“Alright.” Then, Lapis shook her head mockingly. “So simple.”

“Shut up!”

“You’re going back to using ‘Shut up’ as your catchphrase? Shame.”

“It’s not a catchphrase!” 
~

Blue recovered from her injuries far quicker than an actual human would. By the time the sun was setting, the electrocution burns on her body had faded (and interestingly, her dress had also repaired itself). Her arms were as good as new.

As she told Lapis, it would have been a somewhat different story if she had dropped below 10% health. The amount of time it took to fully recover increased exponentially the lower her health, so while it only took a few minutes to recover from 90% HP and a few hours for above 10%, it took up to three days to recover health from 1% health. Furthermore, Blue would lose consciousness if her health dropped below that threshold. 

It was an exceptionally long-winded way of telling Lapis to be more careful with her fairy. 

With that said, Blue found it confusing how her weapons and thrusters had been destroyed so quickly. Though she had never been in a fight except for that one, Blue was pretty sure her parts — especially her thrusters, since with even one thruster fully unusable, she couldn’t maintain stable flight — were so durable that she would reach 0 HP before they broke. It seemed electricity was Blue’s nemesis. 

But those topics to discuss later. Now, it was well into the night. Though Blue was fully healed, she was sleeping in the infirmary of the complex (which was a welcome change from her jail cell). Lapis, meanwhile, was sitting on her bed. She turned the knob of the radio in front of her — something she had done many times before. She instantly connected with the other side.

“Hey, Lazurin!”
“That was fast.”
“Hi Lazu!”

This time, the greeting was different. There were three voices instead of one. 

Today seemed like a deviation from the old normal, for both armies alike 

For the human army, that came in the form of a fairy who was actively fighting against them, and had almost killed one of their most valuable fairies.

For <Shadow>, today was the first time they saw a new addition to the human army. This fairy was clad in a suit of bronze plating and had a belt with which four timepieces were affixed. He used a bow in the shape of a clock, shooting arrows which pierced straight through objects and beings alike. 

This was Chiaros, fairy of time.
