~~ The Lies Told ~~

“Akito’s first crush was when he was 13…”

It was another night in the archipelago. Violet and Tanner were listening to Lapis through the radio. Unlike the first time they talked, they hadn't needed to move the radio — Akito had been overwhelmed by Violet’s and Tanner’s insistence that they keep the radio on the round table in the living room. That was where they were now. Meanwhile, Akito was sitting cross-legged on the opposite side of the living room, having said he wanted some time to work on something by himself.

This time, the party asking the questions was switched. Lapis was fielding questions from Violet and Tanner, mainly about her and Akito. So far, among other things, she had told them about their first interaction on the beach. That “among other things” included topics Violet and Tanner hadn’t asked about, but things they were eager to learn about anyways. There was no way Lapis was missing this golden opportunity to share embarrassing details about Akito without him listening. Now, unbeknownst to the boy, Lapis talked in great length about Akito’s ill-advised first crush.  

After Lapis finished, it was Violet’s turn to ask a question. She went with a straightforward one. “What complex are you from?”

“Alpha.”

“Oh, cool! I’m from Epsi —”

Violet froze. Beside her, Tanner, having registered Lapis’ casual response far quicker than Violet, took it all in stride. “That’s so cool! I’ve never been there before!” Violet turned on him. “No shit, Sherlock!” But then, she took a moment to think about it. “Lazu, I’m not dumb enough to keep falling for your lies. This is just like when you said you were Akito’s artificial brain, right?”

“No, I’m being serious this time.”

“Yeah, right. I guarantee you’re lying!” And having triumphantly called Lapis’ bluff, Violet walked over to ask Akito if Lapis really was in Complex Alpha. Lapis heard two voices talking in the background, until finally Violet stomped back to the table and sat down in a petulant huff. Tanner asked her: “What did Aki-cchi say?”, using his nickname for Akito. Apparently, Tanner called Akito by that because he kept Chiaros within his mind so much that Tanner decided to combine their names into one. 

“Aki-cchi didn’t say anything.” Violet lied, evidently peeved. Lapis grinned. “Violet, are you sure? If you guaranteed that I was lying, surely Akito would agree with you, right?”
“Shut up!” Violet muttered, sounding a lot like Blue. 

“I’m surprised you’re able to talk to us.” Tanner spoke up. After all, having a direct line to the vampires’ enemy while being held captive by them seemed a bit far-fetched. Lapis turned to her cover story. “They don’t really check in on us. We’re free to do whatever we want, until…” She trailed off, her unspoken words being something along the lines of “they eat us.” Violet didn’t seem to realize why they were unspoken, however, and finished the sentence: “Until you become vampire food?” 

Lapis grinned at the radio. That was a pretty insensitive way to put it. 

“Lazurin,” Tanner addressed Lapis by the nickname he had given her, “does that mean you get to lie around all day?” Lapis assented, and Tanner continued: “That sounds nice…”

“Until you get chomped on,” Violet pointed out, not caring that the person that was supposedly being “chomped on” was on the other side of the radio. Tanner nonchalantly replied, “Eh, I’ll deal with that when the time comes!”

Their conversation quickly shifted to what Lapis did every day. Given that all her replies were fabricated, it wasn’t a topic Lapis was eager to discuss, but her cover story was mostly foolproof. Yes, we do get some comics to read. Yes, they let us go outside sometimes — that’s how I got the radio. No, the vampires don’t guard us that well. It’s not like they have anything to fear from us. No, they just choose at random who they eat. No, they don’t do it that often. Vampires don’t need incredible amounts of human meat to sustain themselves. 

Most of it were the true experiences of humans in Complex Alpha, though Lapis did have to admit a small portion was propaganda. 

“Aren’t you scared? Since you’re basically good as dead?” Violet asked Lapis bluntly. Tanner began to interject: “Violet…” (incidentally he didn’t have a nickname for her yet), but Lapis didn’t really mind the question. “The main character thrives in such a setting! I'd rather be here than in a complex where I have no fear for my life.”

Her declaration was met with silence. And then, Violet turned to face Akito. “Akito, I’ve been thinking this for a while now, but is Lazu also not okay in the head?” There was a muffled “W-what, uhhh…” from across the room, much quieter than Violet’s loud question. Lapis laughed. “Hah! Say what you will, Purple“.

“What did you call me?” Violet let out an outraged exclamation. At the same time, Tanner grinned as if he had uncovered a revelation: “That’s such a good nickname! I’m using it!”

“You are NOT calling me that!” Violet spun furiously on him. 

“Okay, Purple!” Both Lapis and Tanner said at the same time. Violet exclaimed in protest once again. 

Through the radio, Lapis could hear the hushed sound of shuffling feet as someone put away their equipment. Tanner looked over his shoulder and got up. “Akito, are you done?” As he left to go check on Akito, Lapis asked: “Violet, What is Akito doing?”

“We’re making a telescope,” Violet grumbled. Evidently, she was still peeved at her new nickname. “I was going through some of Akito’s belongings and found a blueprint of it in one of his books, so we tried to make it.” In a bit more detail, Violet had gone into Akito’s room without permission, read through some of the books he brought to the base, and then pestered him to build the telescope with her. Though he had only known her for a short time, Lapis figured Akito had already given up on enforcing personal boundaries.

“Violet, you really shouldn’t go through Akito’s stuff like that.”

“Really? Oh. I see.” The girl seemed genuinely apologetic. As Akito and Tanner came up to them, she apologized to Akito, who had absolutely no context for the conversation. Then, she followed up with: “Also, is it true you sent a love letter full of heart stickers to your first crush and then got ghosted forever?” Akito looked a bit like a fish as he stammered: “U-uh, w-w-w-hat?” Through the radio they could both hear unrestrained laughter. 

Tanner, meanwhile, was examining the telescope. He held it up with one hand to his eye. “I can’t see anything,” he observed. “S-sorry, uh, I don’t think using it indoors will work.” Akito spoke up, apologizing as well for no reason. Tanner placed his hand to his chin in thought.

“Then let’s go outside!” 

Akito and Violet both looked outside the window of their cabin. It was pitch black. “I-it’s dark, though?” Akito timidly objected.

“Would you rather go stargazing in the daytime?” Lapis pointed out. “True, but…” Akito trailed off, looking at the radio. Though he didn’t voice his thoughts, he wanted to talk to Lapis for a bit. But then, Tanner grinned. “Why not? Let’s bring Lazu along!” And before they could object, Tanner carried the radio with one hand, telescope in the other, and burst out of the cabin. Violet and Akito glanced at one another, then hurriedly followed. 
Outside, their view of the sky was blocked by large, formless trees. Their cabin was at the edge of a large swath of untouched forest, far away from the five complexes and the rest of humanity. In the near distance, they could hear the crashing of waves against a rocky beach. And beyond that was the ocean, separating them from Complex Alpha, the captive humans, and Lazu. Tanner, Akito, and Violet headed towards that beach, clambering through a narrow dirt path amidst the cypresses. As they walked, barely being able to see their own feet, Lapis and Akito talked with one another. 

“Why a telescope?”

“Well, Violet said she had gotten into astronomy, so she persuaded me to make one with her.”

“So you can speak normally,” Violet interjected at one point. Akito had no clue how to respond to that.

They reached the end of the forest. Ahead of them was the sand, the rocks, the shore. Then the ocean, which seemed only a sliver in width, a distance so small they could reach out their hands and cross it. And beyond that ocean was a vast field of stars. 

Akito and Violet set up the telescope. Tanner placed down the radio on the beach and sat next to it. For a while, the only sounds the radio picked up were Akito and Violet fussing over the telescope details (though it was more like Violet fussing and Akito apologizing). And then Tanner spoke to Lapis. “You said you were kept inside, so does that mean you can’t see the stars right now?”

Unbeknownst to them, Lapis had gotten up from her bed and moved beside the wall adjacent to her bed. She had pressed a button discretely placed by her bedside, and part of the wall had slid aside, revealing a large pane of glass. It was a feature found in the rooms at the edges of the complex, reserved only for a select few of high ranking among <Shadow>.

Now, Lapis looked outside. Through the clear window, she could see a remarkably vast field of stars. The elf smiled as she replied.

“No, I can’t”. 

~

Blue was walking on the first floor of the complex with a delighted smile. It was essentially the first time she had been left alone, free to do whatever she wanted. That was one of the causes for celebration. The other was clutched tightly in her arms — a massive jar of honey. Blue took a large spoonful of it with a silly grin on her face and devoured it in one bite. 

This morning, Mitsui had come over and given her the jar, telling her it was courtesy of Lapis. It was a few days after the fight with Circe, and truth to be told Blue had forgotten about her request from her owner as payback for injuring her so severely. The main character had kept her promise.

“Hey, Blue!”

Blue turned around. Erin was sitting on the steps of the stall where they met on Sundays, petting an oddly shaped black object nestled in her lap. As Blue went over to her, the object lifted its face, revealing two ruby eyes. Evie shot her an apathetic look before sinking her fangs back into Evie’s arm. 

“...”

“I’m not actually enjoying petting Evie, okay? It’s not like I can do anything against the strongest fighter in the complex!” Though Blue hadn’t said anything, Erin rushed an explanation as if she were caught red-handed. Despite her words, her contented expression was the same as whenever she saw one of the resident cats in the island. Evie never let Erin pet her except for when she was feeding on her blood, so it was clear Erin was just being her usual tsundere self.

In a tone much more fitting of elf royalty, she continued, “You should sit!” Erin looked oddly pleased as Blue sat down (though perhaps it wasn’t odd given her weakness for cute things and the two cute girls next to her). She asked Blue: “Did you not have patrols with Lapis today?” 

“Not yet. Maybe because it’s so foggy outside?” The streak of good weather had finally been broken as they approached the end of spring’s first month. A thick smog was smothering the archipelago today. Because fairies had decently weak radar and navigation systems (as compared to the technology of the Nightjars, or better yet, the echolocation of the vampires), the human army was at a disadvantage in fog and would likely not try any coordinated attacks. 

“Or Lapis is just being considerate of you,” Evie released her fangs from Erin’s pale skin to interject, “She gave you that jar of honey, right?” She pointed to the comically large supply beside Blue. 

“Hmph. Yeah, right. When has she ever been considerate of pixel art like me?” 

Erin stiffened. “Pixel art?” In response, Blue glared at Evie, recalling the words Evie had thrown her way when they first met. Erin turned on the vampire in her lap. “Evie, you shouldn’t —”

Just as Blue was deriving happiness in watching Evie be chewed out, Evie leapt straight up at Erin’s face, knocking into the ground. Erin didn't have time to react. Evie pinned her down and bared her fangs, watching Erin struggle beneath her like a cat with its food.

“Blue, let's go on patrol!” 

Blue looked upwards. Lapis was standing in front of them, arms crossed and black cloak billowing out behind her. Evie and Erin instantly froze and greeted her, while Blue asked: “Right now?”

Lapis grinned wryly. “I’m morally obligated to make sure you don't watch Evie and Erin making out.”

“That's not what this is!” Evie and Erin said in unison. Meanwhile, Blue asked confusedly, “what's making out?”

“I'll tell you if you grow older. Let's go.” Lapis beckoned for Blue to come, and though the girl relented, she scowled at her. Behind them, they heard Erin say: “Please come back safe.” Lapis chucked. “Okay, mom!”

Erin lunged at her, but she was a step too late. Lapis transformed into her sleek black mecha suit, and they took off.

~

As they patrolled, they chatted about random topics just like usual.

“Lapis, do you have a favourite food?”

“If I had to choose, I’d say broccoli.” This admission surprised Blue; when it came to dinner time Lapis always had to be coaxed into eating vegetables by Erin. “But you seem to hate vegetables?”

“That’s just characterization. Have you ever heard of a main character that likes broccoli? If I’m going to be the protagonist, sacrifices must be made.” 

“...”

Every once in a while, Blue thought Lapis was plain idiotic. Now was one of those times. Lapis brushed off her line of reasoning like it was nothing, though. “How about you, Blue? Any foods you dislike?” They both knew that was a far more interesting question than what foods Blue liked — the answer to that was obvious.

“Strawberries.” Blue replied to Lapis’ question. Lapis chuckled. “Cute as you are, even Erin would hate you for that. She loves those.”

And so they passed the time, traversing through the thick fog in a lazy, wide arc.

Around one hour into the patrol, a small dot appeared at the edge of Lapis’ radar. Unlike the clusters of islands scattered across her screen, which were coloured green for terrain, this dot was white. And it was moving. Lapis frowned at the same time Blue noticed the dot. The girl tried to see through the thick fog, but to no avail.  

“Let’s turn back. We’re pretty far from Complex Alpha,” Lapis told Blue. The fog had made it hard for them to keep track of their location, and they had traveled further outwards than their regular patrols. Whoever that dot on the other side of the screen was, they had probably done the same.

“I want to see what it is though!” Blue piped up, the curiosity evident in her voice. But Lapis denied her firmly: “Only if it attacks. Little children shouldn’t be so greedy.” It was a decision that contrasted her typically flamboyant personality, though she seemed to manage her army with the same conservative approach. Maybe she had taken such drastic risks against Circe because the fairy of electricity really was that valuable. 

The sky in front of them began to glow. Ever so faintly, it took on an unnatural luminosity, as if the sun had finally found a way to break past the fog. But then, it got brighter, and brighter, and brighter.

“It’s so hot,” Blue complained. 

What?

Lapis didn't feel anything, but she instantly applied full reverse power to her main thruster and banked sharply to the right. 

The sky looked as though it could shatter. And then, it did. From within the depths of the fog, a fireball parted the sky, its white flames scorching through where Lapis and Blue had been a second earlier. Their health dropped, though they had just barely grazed it. Molten metal from Blue’s shoulder plates dripped down onto Blue’s right arm before cooling in misshapen chunks. As Blue exclaimed in surprise, Lapis dove into the tunnel of empty sky that the flames had carved out. Something stared back at them.

He looked just like a creature from the netherworld. His body was an infusion of raging hot magma into a rough-cut chunk of volcanic rock. Crimson horns jutted out from a jagged head that seemed as if it were carved straight from a slab of obsidian, and his eyes blazed with flames from hell itself. The nine rings that extruded in procession from his fairy crest effused such scalding white flames that the air quivered, like a mirage, around him. 

Lapis and the fairy stared at one another. Neither made a move, eyeing one another through the channel of clear sky. But those nine rings grew more and more luminous, a foglight that sliced through the sky straight towards its target. Finally, Lapis spoke to Blue: “You’re okay, right?” 

“What is that?”

Lapis took that question as a sign Blue was okay. “Inferno, of the flames…” As she spoke, she pointed her left arm at the figure on the other side of the tunnel. 

They fired at the same time. The white flames collided with <Missile>, instantly devouring it without any resistance. Lapis once again had to dodge as a second fiery bullet drilled another tunnel into the fog, and she dove downwards towards the ocean. Blue spoke before she could: “Don’t you dare say my attacks are weak.”

“How’d you know?” 

“It’s written all over your face!” Blue complained. Though she couldn’t see Lapis’ face, she had no doubt what expression she was wearing right now. “My attacks are plenty strong if you don’t compare it to that.”  

Through the gaps in the fog, they saw the fairy follow them with his eyes — he was likely tracking them with the same radar system as Blue’s. His nine rings dispersed around him in a grid, changing colour from white to a much less calmer red. Each shot fireballs towards Lapis and Blue, and a barrage of scarlet flames rained down on the black mech as they skimmed the top of the waves. The distance Lapis had placed between them was great enough that she could weave through the fireballs. But Blue realized that any closer, and they’d be cut down by the firing squad above. They couldn’t make any progress towards the fairy. 

---------------------------------------------------------

LAPISNOTES

INFERNO OF THE FLAMES

Propulsion System: Normal
Speed: Slow
Unique Traits: None
Name: From the first part of Dante’s Divine Comedy

Attack:
<Circles of Hell>
User summons fireballs from nine rings surrounding their body
“Continuous ammo bar” (like Amber or Gigi), the “number” of ammo spent depends on the power of the fireballs the user decides to summon
Red < Orange < Yellow < White < Blue, with red taking almost no ammo to fire and each blue fireball taking roughly 1/20th of the bar
Very fast unload speed, very slow reload* speed (similar to amber, reloading e.g. “1” ammo is fast but reloading the whole bar is very slow), medium* damage (blue fireballs have very high damage, while red ones have very low), very long range

Defense:
<Lethe>
User creates a quarter-circle wall of flames anywhere on (not in, i.e. the flames are a fixed distance away from him) a 30 m radius around him
Low survivability — any medium-powered attack that hits this will break it
Medium reload speed

Misc:
<Acheron> (Offense)
User combines the power of all nine rings into one solo shot
Extremely long reload, instantaneous unload, two* ammo, extremely long range, extremely high damage
Similarly to <Circles of Hell>, he has a “continuous” ammo bar and can vary the power of <Acheron>, which will take away a proportional amount of ammo. For instance, with white flames, he has two ammo, but with blue flames, he has one

---------------------------------------------------------

Lapis eased into a gradual climb out from sea level, being sure to maintain the same distance. She fired one of her missiles. In a flash of light, a wall of flames manifested a dozen meters in front of Inferno — his defensive ability — and the missile crashed harmlessly into it with a loud bang. All the while, the nine rings continued their relentless bombardment. Though these red fireballs were nowhere near as intense as the white one Inferno had unleashed at the start, they were far greater in number and area covered.

“You haven’t been all dramatic and monologue-y yet.” Blue pointed out as they continued dodging. So far not a single fireball had hit them, but it wasn’t like they had done anything to affect Inferno either. 

“Aww, do you want me to? Are you feeling uncomfortable and worried because I haven’t?” Lapis didn’t miss her beat as she teased Blue.

“No way.” Blue instantly shot her down.

“You really are starting to overlap characters with Erin. It’s not good to have two tsunderes in a story!” 

“Screw you! I’m really not!”

Lapis laughed, evidently pleased at having gotten under Blue’s skin. “ I know you’re worried, but try not to be! I’m simply saving my talents for the finale.” It was a lot of unfounded confidence for something who had only evaded fireballs for the past few minutes. 

“Why not try getting a hit first?” Blue interjected testily.

“Hah. Didn’t you think his OHKO move was really cool? I want to try something like that too!” Lapis’ reply was unconcerned. With a hint of dissatisfaction, she added: “Too bad there’s a certain fairy whose attacks couldn’t snap a glowstick if she tried. I’ll need to improvise!” 

“...What’s a glowstick?” 

 “I’ll show you some time!” Though Blue didn’t know what it was, she got the feeling Lapis was still dissing her capabilities as a fairy. 

The rain of flames above them suddenly ceased. Inferno’s rings lost their red glow, taking on the same shade as the obsidian in his body. Silence ensued. And from that silence, four engines began spooling up. With an agility and speed Lapis had kept hidden up till now, she scythed through what little fog remained in the aerial arena and rocketed towards Inferno. Blue realized what she was going for.

All fairies had a restriction on their offensive capabilities. For many of them, that was a limited amount of ammo. Blue didn't know how Inferno’s ammo system worked, and it was likely even though Inferno wasn't firing, he was conserving ammo to prepare for a counterattack. But he had been continuously expending resources for three straight minutes. If there was a time to attack, it was now.

Lapis fired <Missile> towards the fairy, baiting out his wall of fire. She flew straight at it. At the last moment, she dove downwards, just out of grasp from the outstretched tendrils of flame. 

They were now nearly at top speed. One moment Inferno was a black and red speck in their visor, the next they were staring straight at each other, only a few dozen meters apart. For the first time since the fight had started, Inferno activated his main thruster, making a last ditch attempt to get away. But without Blue’s flight capabilities, he was far too late. Lapis pointed both her weapons towards him. She opened her mouth. 

It was hot. 

So unbearably hot.

The nine rings above the fairy of the flames burst into colour — first red, then orange, then yellow. Then, no colour at all. Just a dazzling, blistering white. Within each ring was a window into an uniquely grotesque landscape, and from them white flames poured outwards, torturing the foggy sky. They were within a heat so insufferable it could only be described as hellish.

Unable to alter her trajectory, Lapis and Inferno locked eyes. 

Then the flames surged towards them. 

Though Blue wasn't really that afraid, she instinctively closed her eyes as their field of vision was covered by a swath of hellfire. At best, she thought, Lapis would be able to avoid instant death. They were at full health, after all. As long as they dodged most of the fireballs, Blue was certain her thrusters wouldn't be affected and they'd be able to escape. 

But the pain she had been waiting for never came. 

When she opened her eyes, they were soaring inverted at an even greater velocity than before, only slightly injured. As Lapis turned her head, Blue could see Inferno rapidly receding in the distance. The fireballs careened off into the distance and melted into the waves.  An indication on Lapis’ visor blinked slowly. It was that of Blue’s defensive parachute, which had been used and was now reloading. 

“How did you…” Blue began to ask — Lapis shouldn’t have been able to react in time. But she cut herself off. The sky behind her wasn’t coloured blue, nor was it shrouded with the grey of the fog. Instead, it was alit in an endless sea of red flames — far more than what Inferno had produced in the entire fight. “No way…How? He’s used so much ammo already!” Lapis responded nonchalantly: “That’s what I was thinking too.”

“You don’t know why?”

Lapis did her best to shrug while flying at upwards of 250 kilometers per hour. “Our army doesn't even know all the fairies and their attacks, let alone any specifics on ability restrictions.” They had now flown into the fog a few kilometers away from Inferno, and from their radar they could see that he wasn’t giving chase. The sea of flames behind them quickly became nothing more than a hazy red projection. But just as Blue thought Lapis was leaving the conflict, they slowed down and banked shallowly to the right in a slow, lazy arc.

“Alright,” Lapis proclaimed, “here’s the script.”

“What script?” Blue got a sense of deja vu from when Lapis had said the exact same words back on Oni island. This time, Lapis didn’t answer. They broke out of the fog and instantly felt Inferno’s gaze upon them from above; judging by how his nine rings were still at the ready, he had expected them to come back. Just like in their first interaction, they stared each other down. But instead of raising her arm at Inferno just like before, Lapis lined her black mech up, straight at Inferno. And straight into the line of attack. 

Blue realized what she was going to do. “Lapis, are you insane?” 

“I admit I was reckless last time.” Lapis conceded. “But,” she added before Blue could object further, “this is well within my abilities. After all…”

Lapis pushed the thrust controls of her main thruster, willing them one defiant step, two, into the hellish landscape.

“...The main character makes the impossible possible.”

A thousand streaks of scarlet flame rained down from the sky. One streak of midnight black rose up to meet them. 

20%. 

The black mech flew deliberately, no faster than a regular fairy. They danced through the flames, a slow waltz taking center stage on a calamitous background. 

30%. 

The dance picked up pace, the tempo increased. The black mech shot through the first wave of flames, then the second. 

50%. 

Inferno’s nine rings burst into colour once more, now glowing a warm orange. The summoned flames poured out from a deeper circle of hell with renewed ferocity. But though these fireballs did more damage than their red counterparts, the streak of black didn’t slow down. 

70%. 

The world was now no more than a blur of orange. Then, as the rings changed colour, yellow, then finally white. But the black mech continued to weave in and out, sometimes ducking away only to renew its persistent charge. Not a single fireball in the storm of hell found its mark. Only a few hundred meters remained. 

90%. 

The grid of rings around Inferno crackled, then let out an otherworldly roar. White flames flickered, before being momentarily extinguished. 

There was one colour of fire hotter than white. Inferno’s nine rings were a surreal shade of blue. 

Amidst the apocalyptic flames, Blue heard four words just before Inferno fired. 

Too slow. 
Full power.

Nine fireballs of blue flame converged towards the black singularity in the sky. They collided at the focal point. A violent heat erupted, one so intense it vaporized every single speck of dust in its path, leaving nothing but a scalding carnage behind.

A single streak of midnight black shot out of the flames.

Inferno cast his wall of fire. But once again, he was a step too slow. Lapis and Blue blitzed past it, placing the fairy of the flames squarely in the view of their visor. Lapis pointed both weapons at the fairy. 

“Azul Void.” 

A powerful explosion sent shockwaves across the sky. Two missiles and five rounds of bullets had found their mark.

There hadn’t been enough time for Inferno to dodge or even react. As the black smoke dissipated into the sky, Inferno’s body followed suit, dissolving in a glimmer of light. All that was left of the fairy of the flames was a red fairy crest floating in the turbulent wind, its red glow leaking into the air until it finally stopped shining, nothing more than an oddly shaped gemstone. 

While a fairy’s user was in mech form, they couldn’t die, hiding behind the life of the fairy itself. Now that Inferno was dead, they could see their pilot where Inferno once was. It was a human boy, not much older than Lapis. 

One more time, they locked eyes. There was just enough time to catch his expression.

Then, two bullets from Lapis’ last round of <Gatling Gun> tore into his throat. As the fairy crest and the corpse began their long freefall into the water, never to be seen again, Lapis murmured a quiet epitaph. “See you on the battlefield.” 

Though their health bar was only a sliver below full health, Blue was quiet, just like in the aftermath of their fight against Circe. Unnaturally quiet. Recalling flashbacks of that fight, Lapis asked the fairy: “Blue, were you injured somewhere?”

Blue took a long time before finally responding. “I didn’t think…” She trailed off. Just like when she was near unconsciousness, her voice was distant, in a trance. 

“Think what?” Lapis prompted, worried.

When Blue opened her mouth again, she sounded like her usual self. So much so that Lapis wondered if she had imagined it. “...That you’d win! I thought for sure I could get another jar of honey.” 

Lapis laughed. “What can I say? I am the main character.” 

And so they headed back into the fog, back to Complex Alpha. 

~

It was dinnertime. Mitsui walked down the stairs of the complex to the second floor. He passed the lounge and peered into the cell adjacent from it. 

“Blue, it’s time for dinner.” 

In a corner of the cell, a girl with sky blue hair was curled into a ball. After her patrol, she had excused herself to her room. Since then, she hadn’t moved from that position.

It seemed to take all the energy she had to respond, but even then, her voice was dead, dull. “I’ll pass. I’m not hungry.”

Mitsui lingered outside Blue’s cell for a moment longer before responding. “Okay. I’ll tell them.”

Blue still didn’t move, even as his footsteps receded up the stairs.

~~ Dawn ~~
It had been three days since their fight against Inferno. Blue and Lapis had just finished a successful patrol, scoring their second kill. 

Almost nothing was out of place in the cell on the second floor of the complex. A pack of Uno and some other assorted games were lined up neatly against the concrete wall. The woolen rug sprawling on the floor, as well as the bed in the corner, looked as well-kept as ever. But on the bed was a young girl with sky-blue hair draped in long, messy strands across her face. 

Though perhaps even that couldn’t be called out of place. Ever since their fight against Inferno, Blue had been here whenever she wasn’t on patrol with Lapis. She rarely appeared outside, having skipped meal times and their regular Sunday excursion.

Blue heard footsteps coming down the stairs, just loud enough that they purposefully announced someone’s arrival. It was Mitsui. Just like he had for the past few days, he brought Blue her dinner, glazed with far more honey than usual. Blue didn't move as he slipped it through the bars.

“You should eat soon.”

Blue didn't give any indication that heard his words or would do that. Mitsui sat down outside the cell, placing the tip of his leathery wings placed just in Blue’s field of vision as if reminding her he was still there. “Let me know if you need anything, Blue.” They sat wordlessly for a long time. If there were the ticking of a clock to fill in the painfully empty silence, it might have ticked ten thousand times. Finally, Mitsui got up. “I'll be leaving now.” He spoke firmly, as if affirming something, “See you later, Blue.”

No response. 

Instead of going back up the stairs to the first floor of the complex, Mitsui headed to the living quarters for the elves and vampires. In front of Lapis’ room, he caught Erin and Lapis discussing something quietly. Both of them broke off when they saw Mitsui approach them. Erin started to ask him something, but Mitsui shook his head. Lapis gave Erin a pointed glance. “I told you Blue wouldn’t get better with time.”

Mitsui glared at Lapis. When he spoke, it wasn’t with his usual gentle demeanour. “Then why don’t you act more concerned and figure out what she will get better with?”

Lapis shrugged nonchalantly. “I don’t even know what her problem is.” Then, she presented her regular confident smile. “I’m the main character, and she’s my fairy. It’ll work out. The story does need to progress —”
“You’re an idiot, Lapis.” Mitsui cut her off icily. He spun on his heel and left Lapis and Erin, the clacking of his heels echoing against the concrete floor. Erin started to chase after him. But just before she rounded the corner, she looked back towards Lapis.

There was no one there. Only a soft click could be heard as Lapis closed her bedroom door.

~

“Lazu, Lazu, guess what?”

Violet greeted her excitedly the moment Lapis turned on the radio. She figured it was something to do with their latest project. After they had completed their telescope, Violet had quickly pivoted from an interest in astronomy to one in photography, and they were once again following blueprints from one of Akito’s books to make a camera. Though, she did hear from Tanner that Akito still tinkered with the telescope from time to time, trying to perfect it. 

Behind Violet, she could hear the alarmed stutters of Akito, trying to prevent her from saying what she was going to say. But with Violet, that was a lost cause. “So, I was going through the belongings in Akito’s room —”

“You really should stop doing that,” Lapis interjected, chiding her. All she got in return was a confused response: “But his bedroom door wasn’t closed?” 

“T-that’s b-because you and Tanner destroyed my door!” Akito exclaimed in a panicked voice. If he was willing to raise his voice like that, he must really have wanted Violet to stay silent. His intentions didn’t get through to Violet, though. “Anyways, I found some books! Not the blueprint books, but books that Akito wrote!” 

That was an unexpected topic for Lapis. With a smile in her tone, she disclosed to Akito, “This is the first I’ve heard of this, Akito. You never told me you’re an author!” The boy groaned. In a low voice, he muttered: “I-I kept it a secret on purpose, Lazu. I was planning to tell y-you when I was done, but…”

Silence. And then Violet spoke bluntly: “That’s kinda cute.” All her words did, though, was elicit a more pained groan from Akito. He knew that Lazu wouldn’t let the topic drop now that she’d heard of it. Sure enough, the voice coming through the radio was filled to the brim with a teasing curiosity. “So what are the books about?” 

“It’s all part of one fantasy series,” Violet responded, eager to oblige to Lapis’ questions, “I’m only halfway through the second book, but —”
“Wait, you read it?” Akito cut in, too stunned to even stutter. Violet nodded. “The writing was unpolished, but everything else was really good.” 

“W-wha, n-no,” Lapis laughed as Akito stumbled around for words. Given that Violet wasn’t one to mince words, it was essentially the most genuine compliment you could receive, and evidently Akito hadn’t expected his writing to be good enough to warrant such praise. As he stuttered, Violet began explaining the story to Lapis. “So the series is called Selfish. Let’s see, where should I start…oh, right, the main character is a bit of a bitch. I really don’t like him…let’s see, he’s selfish, fights with a glorified umbrella, and…”

That weapon seemed familiar to Lapis. And now that she thought about it, she remembered telling Akito a long time ago that if, hypothetically (since captive humans didn’t have weapons), she could use a weapon, it would be an umbrella. Her voice was dripping with a lighthearted poison as she interrogated Akito: “Akito, is this…me?”

“It is based on you, but he’s a lot better than what Violet is saying!” He whirled on Violet. “What don’t you like about him? I spent the most time on his character, you know!”

“He’s pretentious,” Violet replied frankly, before making a sound as if she just thought of something. She addressed Lapis: “Just to clarify, that wasn’t about you. It was for the character that Akito based on you — Ow!” Akito swiftly kicked her in the leg, and she grumbled at him. “What was that for?” 

“You were smiling like you handled that well!” Akito retorted.

Much to Akito’s chagrin, the conversation continued revolving around his novel series. He and Violet began arguing over all the major plot points and characters in the story. The author and reader had drastically different viewpoints over the story, though it was Violet that seemed to like Akito’s work more than Akito himself. Lapis didn’t interrupt them. She just listened silently to their heated discussion with a smile on her face. After a while, the radio became nothing more than a comforting stream of white noise, a natural complement to her true underlying thoughts. 

Lapis almost missed the words directed at her, the first in a while. “Lazu, we’re going to get an umbrella. Violet thinks an umbrella isn’t a feasible weapon.” Lapis laughed. “A braindead take, as expected of our resident Purple.” 

“You’re wrong! And stop calling me that!” Violet stormed out of the living room in a huff, trying to figure out where their squadron placed their little-used umbrellas. Akito followed her, telling Lapis: “Sorry, we’ll be back.”

There was the sound of scuffling slippers. And then, silence settled over Lapis’ room. She lay on the bed, kicking her feet restlessly like she was trying to paddle through water. Then, Lapis got up and pressed the button by her bedside. She looked outside the window. It was another impossibly clear starry night. 

“...Tanner, you there?”

“Evening, Lazurin!” Though Lapis hadn’t really expected a response, she got one immediately. “What are you doing?” She asked. “I’m reading Akito’s book right now, since he left it on the table.” Tanner replied. “It’s really interesting!” Lapis laughed. Akito probably wouldn’t be too happy upon hearing that. Or maybe he would, since he clearly was getting closer to Violet and Tanner. It seemed the two were indeed taking good care of Akito. 

Through the radio, Lapis could hear the muffled sounds of Akito and Violet tearing the cabin apart for a single umbrella. She glanced at the clock on her wall. It was nearly half past ten. Blue would be nearly asleep by now. On a regular day. 

“Tanner, can you tell them that I’m sorry, but I’m leaving early?” 

“Okay, see you tomorrow!” Tanner responded lazily. He didn’t seem surprised, and somehow Lapis got the feeling that was less because of his personality and more because he felt something was off. Lapis to leave early. Either way, she was a bit thankful he didn’t pry any further; she could only imagine the questions Violet would ask if she were still there. 

“See you.”

Lapis twisted the knob on the radio, letting it pass through a world of varying static before finally falling silent.
---------------------------------------------------------

From Akito’s Notebook
Selfish, Prologue

Rain. It dripped, softly, a drizzle onto the rough gravel roads. A boy walked through the rain, holding a bright red umbrella up towards the sky. 

It was just before dinner. A few children passed by him, laughing as the rain soaked their clothes. Farmers hurried inside the thatched straw huts that dotted the roadside, awaiting a warm dinner. Down the street, a news-boy broadcasted the latest warning to people who had already heard it many times over the last few months. Something about a monster that could turn paper to metal. 

The boy kept his umbrella down as they all passed. When he looked up again, his eyes met that of a girl’s. She was in her late teens and, despite the cold rain, was wearing a grey dress that seemed to reflect the clouds above. Her soaked brown hair flowed past her thin shoulders. 

For a moment, the boy stopped walking. They stared at each other. The boy, without even realizing, muttered:

“Could this be fate?”

The girl’s sneer caught his attention. “Ew. That is disgusting.” As the boy lowered his head and tried to shuffle past her, she caught his arm. “I’m Skye Arling. What’s your name?”

“Yes, yes, I’m so very sorry. Take this for your troubles.” The boy withdrew a dirty copper coin from within his robe and tossed it to the girl, who let out a surprised laugh. He shook his arm free. “Good luck in this shitty world.”

“What makes you think it’s shitty?”

“...”

A pause. Then, the boy let out a wry smile. He began heading down the road once more, his red umbrella facing the relentless rain. 

“The name’s Rubio Carone. And this world is selfless.”

---------------------------------------------------------
~

Someone walked quietly down the stairs leading to the second floor of the complex. Blue didn’t look up as they stopped in front of her cell. It seemed that Mitsui really did mean it when he said, “See you later.” 

Metal keys jangled softly. The person unlocked her jail cell and swung its thick iron bars outwards. It wasn’t something Mitsui could do — he didn’t have the keys to her cell. The only person with the keys was the one standing in front of Blue right now.

Lapis entered Blue’s cell and sat down beside her.   

The stairwell lights were the only source of illumination for the two silhouettes in the cell. Long, dark shadows hovered over them both. They only dully felt the presence of the other through the two indentations on the fluffy bed, a few centimeters apart from each other. Lapis stretched her hand out those few centimeters, towards Blue. She ruffled her hair. The fairy didn’t move nor respond, and Lapis quickly pulled back.

Neither spoke for a long time. Until Lapis asked: “Blue, wanna bet something with the main character?” Her voice was as self-assured as ever, as if it were a bet she knew she could win. Blue didn't respond, though, and Lapis continued. “Tell me why you're sad. If it's nothing I can fix, then I'll do anything you want from me.” Lapis paused. “That includes breaking my contract with you.”

Her offer lingered in the air, untaken. The girl in the corner remained unresponsive, and Lapis fiddled with the pendant on her collarbone, lost in thought. No matter how much she mulled over it, she couldn't deduce the source of Blue’s pain. The main character wasn't omniscient. 

The stairwell lights flickered once, then turned off as part of their automatic nightly routine. Their shadows became one with the darkness. Lapis began to get up. “Feel free to take that offer any time,” she added loudly, a proxy for parting words she'd prefer not to say. “I am the main character.”

“You'll lose that bet.” Blue’s voice was flat, dull, lifeless. 

But even still, a smile crossed Lapis’ face. It was a surprisingly loud smile, one that matched the volume of her voice as she replied: “We'll see about that. I am the main character.”

In the darkness, Blue unfurled the wings she had kept wrapped around her body. For an even longer period of time than before, a heavy silence settled over the cell until finally, Blue began with the same dull voice as before.

“I didn't think…” It was the same three words she had spoken after their fight against Inferno. But this time, the words that came tumbling after were far different from that day. 

“I didn’t think people would actually die. I’m not sure what I thought would happen. I knew that they wouldn’t just magically respawn, completely uninjured. But it never occurred to me that when you fight them and win, they’d just…not exist anymore.”

“And I know they were also trying to kill us. I know if they didn’t die, then they would kill us. I know all that. But…I didn’t realize.” Blue’s voice didn’t waver. But even still, she seemed so unimaginably fragile. Quietly, she whispered into the emptiness.

“I’ve never really thought much of death, so…I don’t know.”

It wasn’t a statement from someone only a month old. She seemed like she had been in this world for far longer. But it was definitely a statement from a child. Silence once again returned to accompany the darkness. Blue hugged her knees closer to her thin frame. She stared at the floor, unable to glance up at Lapis’ expression.

And then from within that silence came the soft tinkling of laughter. It filled in the emptiness in the cell, encircled Blue’s diminutive body, intruded every dark nook and cranny. Blue hadn’t felt anything when Lapis said she was the main character. But now, that laugh…the elf in front of her, and the main character, Blue realized they were one and the same. They were both Lapis.

“I was worried I really would lose the bet.” 

Blue couldn't say anything. All she could do was stare at Lapis’ faint smile, one which could take on the world and win. 

“Let's make another contract, Blue!”

A contract. It was the reason Blue and Lapis were together to begin with. 

“I won't ever kill humans again. I'll still fight fairies, and I'll still destroy their cores, but I'll save their user every time. How does that sound?”

And this offer was just like the first contract. A one-sided deal, nothing more than a few spoken sentences, that intertwined both their destinies. 

For a long time, Blue studied Lapis, piecing together her expression through the strands of sky-blue hair blocking her view. And then, she looked back down at the ground. “No.” 

“Why not?” Lapis asked, although she didn’t seem too surprised by her rejection. “You can ask anything of me if I break the contract.” 

Blue’s voice was low, barely a mutter. “You can’t. You saw the end of the fight against Inferno. I don’t have hands in mech form. How are you going to catch them?”

“That’s for me to prove.”

“It’s a war. You’ll have to kill them.”

“It’s the fairy cores that I need to destroy, not the humans.”

“You’re used to killing humans. You don’t have a reason to do this.”

“I’ve accepted it. But you haven’t. Isn’t that reason enough?”

As they went back and forth, Blue kept searching for reasons Lapis couldn’t keep her end of the contract. Finally, with her head pressed tightly against her knees, she mumbled. “You’re lying. You won’t do it.”

Lapis sighed. “Haven’t I told you? The main character backs up her words —”

“You don’t understand!” Blue’s words came out as a scream. Her shoulders quivered slightly, as if raising her voice was taking out all the energy she needed to maintain her posture. She wrapped her wings tighter around her body, forcing out a cry from her throat. “You’re the enemy!” 

“...” 

Lapis didn’t answer immediately. 

Instead, as Blue curled up into a fragile ball, she turned her pendant over and over, letting it spin back to its natural position. Even with such little light in the cell, one could tell it was a deep, deep blue. The colour of lapis lazuli. 

“Blue, do you remember the first rule of being the main character?” 

Blue remained silent. But of course she remembered. It was the phrase Lapis had spoken back in the pit on Oni Island, just before they made their first contract. The main character always leads her friends to a better future.

Lapis got up. Blue could just barely see her figure as she walked out of the cell, closing the formless iron bars behind her. She didn’t bother locking the door. Just before footsteps retreated up the stairs, Blue heard her voice one last time for the night. 

“Try to get some sleep, okay?” Lapis called out. “See you tomorrow.”

~

Early the next morning, Lapis and Blue flew out of Complex Alpha, their wings of pitch black contrasting the wisps of cirrus clouds high above them. Neither looked back at the island quickly receding behind them. And both stayed silent — they hadn’t exchanged words all morning. 

The island quickly disappeared from the display on their visor, and though vampire echolocation had a much further range than fairy radar, they soon slipped away from that too. There was nothing to sense them as they flew over the tessellation of barren outcrops and water beneath them. Minute after minute passed in silence. Soon, they were at the furthest point Lapis had allowed them to go on their patrols. 

But Lapis didn’t bring that up. She only increased the power to her thrusters as they intruded what was considered human territory. Today, she was the one looking for a fight. 

Apart from the thin layer of clouds, the sky was crystal clear. Visibility was excellent, and so the being lazily floating in the sky appeared in their field of view before it showed on their radar. It shone brighter than the rest of the horizon, scattering a corona of rainbows into the warm spring air. 

The moment that they entered each other’s radar range, the being suddenly stopped and turned to face them. Lapis didn’t reduce her speed nor change her heading, however. As they closed the gap, Blue could see two delicately shaped arms differentiate themselves from a lustrous body of pure, unmelting ice. Above her body was a sculpted, impassive head from which two cold eyes glared as if judging them. 

The fairy of ice seemed to realize Lapis and Blue weren’t a friendly fairy. But she didn’t run away, either. Instead, as Lapis and Blue skimmed the surface of the waves, icicles as large as them appeared below the clouds, refracting the sunlight. It was her response to their abrupt declaration of war. 

Lapis visualized a trigger in her left arm — a mental image that had become second nature over the past month — and reached out to it with an imaginary hand. The tips of her fingers passed through it at first, then took hold of it. Light the colour of the sky gathered in her left arm, flaring up as if it couldn’t wait to be released. But before she could:

“No using that.” It was the first words Blue had spoken all morning. 

“Huh?” Lapis was caught off guard. The light in her arm dissipated into the wind as Blue repeated herself flatly. “No using your missiles.” 

Blue half-expected Lapis to ignore her — there was no reason to listen to such an absurd request. But instead, the elf just responded quietly: “Okay.” She focused her visualization towards her feet just like a sprinter pressing against their start block. At the same time, the fairy in front of them smudged her fingers across a small glass sphere — a snow globe. With a flick of her wrist, the globe flipped upside down. 

---------------------------------------------------------

LAPISNOTES

ANTARC OF ICE

Propulsion System: Normal
Speed: Normal
Unique Traits: None
Name: From Land of the Lustrous

Attack:
<Snowstorm>
Has a snow globe, representing a spherical area of 5 km with user at its edge
User marks any area on the snow globe with their hand; large icicle spears appear in the corresponding location in the real life spherical area
When user shakes the globe or tilts it, the icicles fall down, aimed at a location determined by the user
Extremely short reload, 6 rounds of ammo (waves of icicles) medium unload, long range, medium damage* (assuming all icicles hit) 

Defense:
<Deep Freeze>
User marks a location in a two kilometer radius; an iceberg materializes in that area, freezing anything within it
Sky shimmers for a second before iceberg materializes
Low survivability, fast reload, medium unload

Misc:
<Whitespace> (Utility)
User marks a location in a two kilometer radius, a screen of ice around 10 m x 10 m materializes in that area
Does no damage, but slows down all projectiles travelling through the screen by a factor of their initial velocity
User can also choose to invert the screen, which increases the speed of all projectiles travelling through the screen
Instantaneous unload, fast reload, one ammo
Fairy itself is not affected by speed boosts (i.e. cannot use <Slippery Slope> to change their own speed)

---------------------------------------------------------

A high-powered whir reverberated through Blue’s body. As a thousand icicles pierced their last location, they rocketed into the sky beyond. 

~

In the five minutes since the fight began, Lapis hadn't spoken a word. Blue hadn’t either. It was completely silent within the mecha suit, jarringly so.

The hellscape of fire they had been exposed to three days ago had become one of ice. Above them, a blanket of icicles refracted the morning sun, illuminating the world below in a mirage-like lighting. Around them, pieces of the sky glimmered slightly before suddenly collapsing into large icebergs blocking their path. It seemed that everywhere around Lapis and Blue was a frozen wasteland. 

Lapis had obeyed Blue’s whim. She hadn’t used her <Missiles>, arguably her first offensive option, once. Instead, she had slowly chipped away health points off their opponent, bullet by bullet. Because of the nature of <Gatling Gun>, Lapis had done less cumulative damage than she would have with just two <Missile> hits.  

But that was far more damage than had been done to them. 

The icy hand crushing the world around them should have also crushed the black mech firmly within its grasp. But Lapis dodged every icicle, every wall of ice that restricted her movement, and every iceberg that spawned around her. Unlike her fights against Circe and Inferno, she stayed firmly at mid-range instead of engaging in close combat — an avoidant, drawn-out fighting style that best suited Bluebird of flight (given her mid-range weapons and aerial agility) but carried none of Lapis’ usual flamboyance.

Either way, the fairy of ice seemed to be aggravated at their dominance. As she placed extra distance between them, she clenched the snow globe in her palm harder, spinning it in place as if painting its exterior with a dusting of snow. All around them, rows upon rows of unseen archers appeared, taking the stage at every loci in the aerial arena. Only the wickedly sharp tips of ice arrows were visible to Lapis and Blue, tracking their every movement as they streaked towards the fairy. The fairy waved her hand at the sky and earth of ice around them. Screens, looking just like cracked floes of ice, materialized in front of the archers — it was the fairy’s third ability, able to increase or decrease the speed of projectiles passing through them. 

Lapis visualized a trigger in her right arm. Just as she reached it, the archers released. The arrows were slow enough to be tracked at first, but then, they reached the first layer of screens, then the second. The arrows sped up exponentially, and just an instant later, the icicles from the sky collided with those from the earth, turning the aerial arena into nothing more than a crumpled snowball. 

From within this null, five rounds of blazing light shot out from beneath the fairy of ice towards her. The first two she blocked with an iceberg at her feet, manifesting from the sky. But Lapis swept her arm upwards, and like a whip, her bullets curved past the wall of ice. They struck the fairy’s base. Her crest of glacial white lost a bit more of its vigorous glow. 

Lapis and Blue emerged wordlessly out of the ice, unscathed. The compartment in her chest was just beginning to close, and scraps of <Parachute> were tumbling to an island a few kilometers away. It had absorbed enough of the ice for Lapis to simply dodge the rest. She was, almost comically, unfazed by anything thrown at her. 

The main character would never willingly hurt her friends. That was what Lapis had said to Blue, back on the beach. Right now, their health bar was full. It was a promise she wasn’t backing away from. But she also had another promise to keep. 

As if on cue, the fairy of ice’s thruster, which was shining a fiery white, suddenly sputtered, then went out. Even though the fairy of ice still had health to spare, she suddenly found herself in freefall. Both her, and Blue perceived what had happened at the same time. 

Normally, the thruster on the base of a fairy was one of the most durable parts — after all, it was the only component keeping them in the air. If you fired shots at random, the fairy would long run out of health points before the thruster broke. But if you targeted it, that was a completely different story.

It was a strategy so impossible Blue hadn’t even realized Lapis was doing it. After all, the fairy of ice had been moving the whole time. For someone to be able to aim at her thrusters so accurately, while also moving, and simultaneously avoid both enemy attacks and hitting her elsewhere was far too much for anyone normal to keep track of. Especially not when Lapis was limited to only one weapon. 

But Lapis had succeeded in only targeting the fairy’s thrusters. Now, she soared up into the sky, away from the fairy of ice. At the apex of her climb, she tucked into a roll. Light surged into her thrusters as she dove back towards the ground. 

If this were a normal fight, she would have whispered, “Full Power”. But the mecha suit remained silent except for the whir of the most powerful engine in the archipelago. 

They caught up to the freefalling fairy a few hundred meters above the water. Without her thruster, she couldn’t do anything to avoid them. Even still, she stretched out her hand, and a screen of cracked ice appeared just in front of them. But at this point, it was just a formality. Lapis effortlessly dodged the screen and charged directly at the fairy of ice. Below them was the endless cerulean ocean. 

No, Blue realized, that wasn’t true. Lapis had driven the fairy of ice back during the course of the fight, roughly a kilometer off from where they first started. Now, they were over the shoreline of a small, deserted island. 

It seemed Lapis had planned this too. 

A second before they collided mid-air, Lapis applied maximum reverse thrust to her three secondary thrusters. The cushion of air they blasted away was just enough to slow them down and bring them alongside the fairy of ice, within arm’s reach. Lapis pointed her <Gatling Gun> directly at the fairy’s chest. 

“Azul Void.”

It was the first Blue had heard from her since the beginning of the fight. She said those words the same way she did against Inferno. Like it was a simple fact, a quiet finality. But this time, it wasn’t meant as a killing blow. 

The gun embedded in her Lapis’ arm never lit up. Instead, she placed it on the fairy of ice’s crest. Lapis pushed her away, altering her trajectory just enough that instead of falling into the water, she would fall onto the island. Lapis and Blue pulled out of their dive. A moment later, a large plume of sand bloomed from the beach on the island as the fairy of ice slammed into it. 

While a fairy’s user was in mech form, they couldn’t die, hiding behind the life of the fairy itself. No matter the damage the user took while piloting the mech, they were unscathed until the fairy was defeated. Now, the cloud of sand cleared, revealing a girl in her twenties. She was in a heap on the beach, unharmed. Besides her, a crest of dull white lay, lusterless, on the sand, having given up her “life” (if you could call it a life, since they were just cores, not actual fairies) in place of its user.

Lapis landed on the beach. She stopped right in front of the girl, who looked up at her in a daze. “Do you have a radio?” Lapis asked the human, her voice slightly muffled by the mecha suit.  

“Y-yeah.” As if in a trance, the girl swept aside her coat, revealing a small handheld device in her inner pockets — the radio used by the human army. Lapis nodded once. In that case, the girl wasn’t in danger of being stranded. Some way or another, she could get back. 

“Good. Then see you on the battlefield.” 

And with those parting words, Lapis and Blue took off into a brilliantly clear sky, devoid of any ice. Soon, there was no trace of the attack, except for the girl on the beach and the lifeless crest beside her. 

Just like their flight there, the return trip to Complex Alpha was almost completely silent. The only words spoken were the ones Lapis told Blue as the complex came into view. 

“Blue, I’ll be doing that till the war ends.” 

Blue hadn’t responded. It was unclear whether or not she believed that. 

~

Early the next morning, the princess of the elves tiptoed down the stairs. It was a motion she had done often as a child, when she wanted to evade her bodyguard. Though today, she had a completely different purpose for doing so. Erin padded past the lounge on the second floor of Complex Alpha. She stopped short, just before a series of thick iron bars, and leaned her back against the wall.

Erin took a deep breath. And then, without looking at the being she was talking to, she rushed through her words.

“Blue, there was a bedroom that was freed up recently, so I was wondering if you’d want to sleep there from now on? I was hoping that would cheer you up more than this cell, since I’m a bit worried about you..”

A pause. And then, she heard laughter from within the cell. Laughter befitting a child — though the one laughing would get mad if someone said that. “Erin, you really should look at people before talking.” 

Whirling around, Erin peeked inside the jail cell. The corner of the bed, which had been frequently occupied the last few days, was empty. Blue was pacing restlessly in the cell, clearly wanting to do something other than be cooped inside for the whole day. She beamed when her eyes met Erin’s. “Sorry for worrying you.” 

Erin stared at her, a mixture of expressions crossing her face. Then, as if remembering she wasn’t supposed to be showing such emotion, Erin quickly turned her head. “I wasn’t worried.” 

In response, Blue laughed even harder. “Oh, but I’ll take the bedroom! I’m starting to hate this cell.” The princess continued her indifferent facade, but she was evidently relieved. “Alright,” she paused, her voice barely repressing her happiness, before continuing: “Does this mean Lapis was able to…make things work?” 

Blue scoffed. “That elf is an idiot…” But then, the fairy with sky blue hair smiled.

“...But I’ve decided to believe her a bit.”  

On an island in the middle of the ocean, Complex Alpha slowly awoke. Squirrels poked their heads out of their hiding holes, timidly venturing out beneath the first light. Gulls squawked raucously as they glided in wide spiraling loops above the crystal-clear water. 

A month had passed since spring arrived in the archipelago. This scene was just like any other spring morning, this act like any other new beginning. The characters took the stage. 

It was dawn.  







Part 1: FIN
Interludes: N/A
