~~ Daily Lives ~~


It was five in the morning. Blue was prancing around a bedroom on the second floor of Complex Alpha. More specifically, her bedroom. 

Her surroundings were in marked contrast to the jail cell she had spent her first month in. Blue now had access to a clock on her wall and a wooden study desk containing the assorted games Erin had given her. The thick iron bars she woke up to every day were gone, replaced with a faintly glowing sliding door. 

Blue had spent the past hour going through every nook and cranny of her bedroom, and though the room was still very bare, it was infinitely better than her cell. Now, she cautiously took hold of the door handle and pulled on it. The door parted with ease. After marveling at the fact that she could lock and unlock the door of her own free will, Blue gently shut the door behind her and ventured out into the maze of corridors. The few elves and vampires Blue passed greeted her cheerfully. For the residents of Complex Alpha, the novelty of Blue’s existence had worn off after a month, and now they treated her regularly.

After tracing the endless routes with sparkles in her eyes and getting lost on purpose, Blue made her way to the jail cell she had been inured to. It was now empty, once again the concrete cage that showed no signs someone had lived there. Blue stuck her tongue at it. From behind her, she heard a serene laugh. “Good morning, Blue.” 

“Mitsui!” The vampire with an eyepatch was seated in the lounge, drinking a glass of water by himself. He smiled at Blue as she ran up to him. “Are you enjoying your new lodgings?” 

“Of course!” A wide grin, before Blue reconsidered something, “But, I guess you won’t visit me every day.” 

“I’ll be here if you want to find me.”

Hearing this, Blue reached up towards one of the aquamarine crystals circulating her body. She reached inside like it was a handbag and pulled out a pack of Uno. “I still need to beat you.” Blue surveyed the area before continuing, as if afraid of a certain someone making an entrance. “Now that Lapis isn’t here to interfere.” Mitsui nodded, accepting the challenge. As he took out the deck and shuffled it, he asked Blue: “So those crystals are pouches?” 

“Yep! I can’t fit anything big inside them though.” Blue experimented by putting a spoon inside one of her crystals. It vanished, and no sign of the spoon was evident until Blue pulled it back out. She began with a self-satisfied smirk: “I’ll never tell Lapis what they are, though. Since she says —”


There was a flash of black as someone launched into a backflip down the stairs, sticking the landing besides them. “That they’re just decorations?” 

Blue jumped at the voice pressed next to her ears, and the elf standing next to her laughed wholeheartedly at her reaction. Her flaxen hair fell in luscious waves across her jet-black cloak, and the pendant on her collarbone seemed to mirror the deep blue of her eyes. Lapis sat next to Blue and grinned dashingly at Mitsui. “Count me in. Let me interfere a bit.”

“Wait, Mitsui, don’t!” 
“Sore loser much, Blue? I know you’re a bit irritated that you didn’t win a single game —”

“I won one!” Blue reminded her pettily. 

“Yeah, but the main character needs to lose some!” Lapis winked. “It’s not interesting if I win every one.” 

“So you’re saying you lost on purpose? Nevermind, Mitsui, let her play!” As Mitsui chuckled softly and dealt cards for three people, Blue glared at Lapis. “I need to teach her a lesson.”

“That line rarely works in the movies,” Lapis remarked as she took one look at her hand, collapsed them into a pile, and began building a small house of cards.

“Screw you!” Blue retorted. 

Unfortunately for Blue, she would soon realize that line didn’t work in reality, either. 

Lapis relentlessly taunted Blue for her streak of losses all the way till breakfast, where they met up with first Erin, then Evie. Today was a Sunday, and instead of directly eating their usual breakfast of sandwiches at the complex, Mitsui suggested they have a picnic for their Sunday excursion. Now, the five of them were heading down the gravel path leading out of the complex. Mitsui took a right and led them down a shortcut of gently rolling meadows that climbed up and down the variable terrain. 

“Harken to my words! With this, I convey the blessing of the dawn, which illuminates even the eleventh hour!”

Lapis leapt off one of the granite ridges, drawing out her umbrella at the same time she frontflipped down to the ledge below. She slammed the umbrella into the meadow, and a shower of dew flew high into the air. 

 Behind her, Erin reprimanded her, telling her to behave lest she wake someone up. Evie clapped, enthused. Lapis took a bow and sheathed her umbrella with theatrics that clearly suggested she regularly practiced it. 

 Though Blue would never admit it, she secretly also thought it was pretty cool.

Despite the regular dips in altitude, the five had steadily made progress up the hill from which Complex Alpha was carved out of. Now, they were at the top. Blue spun around in a delighted circle, trying to take in the foaming seas, the seabirds soaring around them, and the sunrise to the west all at once. She collapsed on the soft grass and stared up at the sky while Erin and Mitsui laid out the picnic blanket. 

“Evie, stop lolling about and help out.”
“And why should I listen to my budget buffet?” 
“Erin, if you add ‘I’ll let you do anything to me’ I’m sure she’ll be glad to oblige!”
“I’d rather poison myself before tarnishing the pride of the elves in that way.”
“Pride? What pride? I know Lapis has it, but some loose girl like you?”

And so the three of them continued bantering while Mitsui observed. At some point, the food was set, and he called Blue over to eat. In addition to the usual breakfast sandwiches, a charcuterie board, salad, and some small pastries were spread out before them. Some condiments sat besides them, and Blue eagerly eyed the honey in the jar. Lapis handed Blue a sandwich. “Here, I already added honey.” Blue accepted it and took a bite. It was delicious, and the meat in the sandwich had an unfamiliar yet distinct taste that elevated the rest of the ingredients. “This is so good! What meat is this?”

“Human.” 

A loud series of coughs and noises, as Blue tried to take back what she had just swallowed, failed, and then drank two cups of water to get rid of the taste in her mouth. Lapis grinned at her in mock concern. “Sorry, did it taste that terrible? I thought you’d be curious and then I heard you say it was good, but maybe I was just hallucinating…”

“Screw you! Never feed me that again!”

Evie took the sandwich from her hand, muttered “Your loss, overheal,” and finished it all in three bites. 

Despite the decently large amount of food they had brought, their appetites were even larger. Blue couldn’t die from hunger. Even still, she did get hungry, and especially after not eating for four days due to circumstances that only Lapis knew (though Mitsui did have a hunch), she devoured everything that didn’t contain human meat. The full jar of honey, somehow, was the first thing to be depleted, then went the sandwiches and charcuterie. As they divided up the rest of the salad, Lapis tried to pass her portion to Evie. 

“Eat your vegetables…” Erin warned her. 

“Okay, mom. So fussy.” Before she could finish enunciating that last word, Erin had a dagger pressed to Lapis’ throat. It seemed the princess had at least a bit of experience in hand-to-hand combat. 

Lapis resigned herself to her fate. As she picked at her broccoli and ate it with a look of mild disgust, Blue thought she could sense a bit of happiness behind her frown. She remembered that broccoli was the elf’s favourite food. Lapis really was a weird person.

Mitsui and Lapis cleaned up after breakfast was over. Erin tried to help, but she was inevitably getting punished by Evie for attacking Lapis in broad daylight. Right now, ample amounts of her blood were leaving her body and quenching the vampire’s thirst. Blue wondered if it hurt. 

The sun had barely peeked over the horizon as they discussed what to do next. “Do you all want to go swimming!” Mitsui suggested, peering over the top of the hill towards the calm, waveless water. 

“It’s time for some fanservice?” Lapis spoke nonsense, as usual. “I’m in. Let’s give the readers what they want!”

Erin, who had been laying limply on the grass courtesy of Evie’s actions, suddenly came back to life. She and Blue spoke at the same time. “No way. I’m not touching water.” Blue glanced at her, and they smiled at each other. It was apparently some common ground Blue didn’t know they had. 

Lapis grinned at Blue. “Erin I knew beforehand, but you? Do you have hidden trauma to water or something?” 

“You are the trauma!” Blue retorted, recalling their fight with Circe in which Lapis had decided to go for a swim in an electrocuted ocean. Though, even without that, she was averse to water to begin with. Perhaps it was because the fairy of the skies didn’t belong beneath the seas. 

A laugh. “Well, too bad! Majority rules, and since Erin is a tsundere, her vote is the opposite of what she says it is, so —”

“I am not a tsundere!”

“Very nice. The first rule of a tsundere is to deny that they are one, of course.” Erin looked like she wanted to press a dagger to Lapis’ neck again, but Lapis continued before she could. “Anyways, it’s 2 against 2. Evie, how about you?”

“My vote is the same as Lapis.” The vampire replied with no hesitation. Lapis leered triumphantly at Erin and Blue while Erin shouted at Evie. “Hey! Didn’t you also not like swimming? Why are you siding with Lapis?”

“I’d rather side with my saviour instead of kibble, obviously! And well,” Evie added, “there’s another reason the likes of you don't need to know.”  

Blue, meanwhile, thought of something. Like a heroine foiling the villain’s plot, she thwarted Lapis’ evil intentions: “We don’t have swimsuits, though. Shame, but swimming’s not an option!”

Lapis’ smile crumbled. In a dejected voice, she began: “Yeah, you’re right…”

“So let’s think of something else —”

“Nah, just kidding!” Lapis swept aside her cloak, revealing that she had brought swimsuits herself. Mitsui had brought his own, evidently being a part of her schemes. “It was hard to find swimsuits for all of us, but I got it done!”

Blue stared at her, mouth agape. Erin came over and took one look at the swimsuits, before shaking her head vigorously. “No way. Why’d you have to choose some that show that much skin?” 

Lapis responded with a serious sigh. “Erin, I know in those romance manga you read, the heroine wears a swimsuit that covers more skin than a parka because she’s too poor to afford anything else, and everyone finds it attractive. Well, it's not! These are regular swimsuits, not the bullshit that occurs when the author is a coward and doesn’t let the reader dream a bit, so hurry up and change!”

Erin was unconvinced by Lapis’ rant. (Though for what it’s worth, they were pretty regular swimsuits; Erin was just being sheltered). She stubbornly insisted that she was swimming in her clothes — a long-sleeved dress that seemed like it was made for staying firmly on land.

And so their plans were set. Blue had given up on resisting the moment Lapis revealed she brought swimsuits. As Erin kept watch on Mitsui — making sure he didn’t peek in spite of Lapis and Evie both telling her he was too obsessed with his crush to care about them — Blue asked Lapis for her swimsuit. 

“I didn’t bring one for you. It’s not like you can take your clothes off, right?” Blue tugged at her white dress, but though it swayed holographically in the wind, it resisted her efforts to take it off. She sighed, knowing Lapis’ next words: “So in a way, you’re already in your swimsuit!”

There was no point resisting. Lapis clearly had thought this out.

Now, they were all changed, shivering in spite of the cool heat that marked the coming of a warmer season. Blue glanced dubiously down at the water, a few hundred feet beneath them. “How are we going to get down?” She asked Lapis. 

Lapis only ruffled her hair lightly. Then, she grabbed her hand. Before Blue could register what was happening, they jumped off the edge of the cliff.

“Don’t you remember?” Lapis yelled to Blue as they fell down to the sea below, the wind buffeting their ears. 

“We can fly!”

~

Though, Blue couldn’t swim. 

As she clambered onto the slippery slice of rock jutting out of the side of the island opposite Complex Alpha, she felt her muscles ache all over from just trying not to sink to the bottom of the sea — Lapis had blocked her from freeloading by entering her mind, and truthfully Erin (who had ridden on one of the vampires down to the water) and Mitsui had to prop her up at times. Blue shook her head from side to side like a dog. The water in her ears refused to get out though, and finally she slipped into Lapis’ mind before slipping out; that seemed to fix her hearing and wet clothes. Not her tiredness, though.

What she saw next did cure her tiredness. As she blinked the seawater out from her eyes, Blue came face to face with the entrance to a massive grotto. Its entrance was roughly circular, as if it were manmade. Within its pitch-black depths, Blue could hear water drip onto the puddles pooled on its floor and wildlife skittering about its deep crevices. 

“Lapis, Lapis, can we go in?” 

Lapis, who was as energetic as ever, replied with a bright smile. “Of course! That’s what we’re here for!” Blue hadn’t known there was a destination to their swim, but she didn’t complain as she merrily scampered inside, waiting briefly for Mitsui, who followed her in. Erin went in after them. Impressively, she hadn’t given in the swimsuit and though she didn’t seem tired despite the extra physical exertion, she was complaining about the damp fabric sticking to her skin. Lapis and Evie brought up the rear. 

Their hollow footsteps echoed in the dark cave. As there was very little light, they relied mostly on the vampires’ echolocation, which was easily enough to navigate the grotto — after all, it was of a higher quality and range than both fairy and Nightjar radar. Mitsui pointed out landmarks to Blue, who fearlessly ran over and examined them as closely as she could. 

As she ran in circles around the group, exploring the texture of the shapeless rocks and stalactites, she heard Lapis talking to Evie. 

“You mentioned another reason you wanted to swim, right? Was it so you could see Erin in a swimsuit? You played it off tough, but it was pretty obvious to everyone but her…”

If it were anyone else but Lapis saying that, Blue was sure Evie would have turned them into a raisin by now. But despite the immensely irritated look on her face, the vampire held back. Blue wondered what Lapis did for Evie to respect her that much. 

Ahead of them, a faint, bioluminescent glow began to emanate from within the cave. It seemed as if the gentle light of the sun had found a way to pierce them, but instead of the warm colours of the sunlight, this glow was a deep, tranquil blue. Curious, Blue ran towards it. She rounded a corner, following the glow…

The boulder in front of her was massive. Or perhaps it was more apt to call it something other than a boulder, since that word evoked shades of dull grey, colours characteristic of regular rocks. It seemed like a jewel, the size of a boulder. 

The jewel’s rough, unpolished facets seemed like they were impossibly old, from a time long past. Each face was easily the size of Blue, and she saw her face reflected into each and every one, all staring back at her with a mirrored look of awe. Though there was no light source in the grotto, the cavern was filled with the deep blue light. It was emanating from the jewel itself. 

“Whoaa! What is that?” Blue breathed out. It was dazzlingly beautiful. 

Lapis, having sauntered up to her, answered. “No clue. It’s always been here, though we only found it a bit before the war began.”

The answer surprised Blue. “No clue? But isn’t this the same jewel as your pendant?” 

Lapis held her pendant up to the light. The deep blue gem encased in it melted into the glow of the jewel, as if affirming that they were one and the same. With a soft smile, she clarified: “I don’t know the name of the gem in my pendant either, though. It adds to the mystery of the main character!”

Blue thought back to when they first met. “But didn’t you say something about your name being a gemstone? Lapis…Lazuli, was it?” 

This time, it was Erin that replied. “That’s a gem long lost to time. We only know of it in passing from folklore. Today, no one knows what it looks like, what colour it is, or if it’s even real.”

“It is real!” Lapis protested. “It enchants the user with mystical powers. I learnt that in a dream!”

Erin snorted and smiled at Blue. “It’d have to be a dream. Since Lapis doesn’t recall what happened for her to ‘learn’ that.” Glancing back at the gemstone, she added: “At the very least, we don’t know what ‘lapis’ is. We had guards monitoring the humans before the war, so unless humans learned about it this past year, they don’t know what it is. Though I guess we’ve never asked a fairy. Do you know what it is?” 

Blue processed the question. She stared at the jewel. The fairy of flight stared back at the young girl. They locked eyes. 

But as for the question itself, Blue didn’t know. 

For a long time, Blue was silent. Then, she turned to Erin. “I tried to think through all my memories, but I found nothing. I wish I did, though. It seems so cool!” Erin let out a relieved breath, more from seeing Blue talk than from her answer. Lapis, meanwhile, spoke up in a low voice: “But within the fairy’s eyes lay deeper thoughts. Thoughts from some other time. Back when she was a child, she —”

“Don’t rewrite my backstory!” Blue snapped at her. 

“Who said it was your backstory?” Lapis immediately replied. She grinned wickedly. “Aren’t you still a child?”

From within the depths of the island came an aggrieved yell, echoing off the facets of the gem, the stalactites hanging off the limestone, and the walls of the grotto.  

“Screw youuuuuuuuuuuuuuu!”

~

On the other side of the ocean, Akito lay on the mattress, staring at the wooden ceiling. He was in a room that was just beginning to get familiar to him. Its wooden walls were devoid of any decorations, the only source of light came from the sunlight streaming through the window, and apart from his bed and the stack of books stacked underneath it, the room was stripped bare. Even so, Akito did have to admit that he was getting used to waking up here. 

“Chiaros, what time is it?” He asked absentmindedly, to seemingly no one. And it didn’t seem like anyone replied, either way. But, Akito heard a voice in his mind, as robotic as always: “It’s seven in the morning.”

Huh, he might actually be correct. Akito didn’t have a clock in his room to verify that, though, and so he got out of bed. After getting dressed in a dark grey t-shirt and sweatpants, he sleepily made his way past the (now fixed) door of his bedroom and was about to emerge from the hallway when he heard two voices arguing. 

“Tanner, hurry up and make breakfast!”

“I’m sleepy, though…”

“You’ve slept for eighteen hours! At least Akito has an excuse since he had the late patrol shift last night.” Violet didn’t care much for Tanner’s excuse. Emphatically, she added: “I’m hungry! Aren’t you? You skipped dinner last night!” As Akito glanced at the clock in the common space and realized he had severely overslept, Tanner mumbled lethargically: “Yeah, but if I’m asleep, then I don’t feel hungry.” 

“Just make food!” Violet glanced up, and her eyes met Akito’s. She didn’t bother greeting him and pleaded: “Help me convince him!” 

“Uh, um, good morning. Sorry, I am a bit hungry too, so…” Akito trailed off. But his words were enough to sway Tanner. With a wide, dog-like yawn, Tanner rolled off the couch he had slept in all night. 

The human army was composed of 52 squadrons — a word that greatly oversold the small size of each crew of fairy pilots. Each was housed in a small wooden cabin hastily constructed when the war began, colloquially known as bases. The bases were assigned a number based on how far west they were, with zero being the easternmost base and 24 being the southernmost one, closest to <Shadow>, the army of elves and vampires. 

Despite Chiaros’ words, it was ten in the morning. The three squadron members residing in Base 33 were just beginning to start a new day. 

~

In fifteen minutes, Tanner had cooked up a scrumptious breakfast for the three of them, consisting of buttered toast, a small bowl of soup, and a large omelette with mushrooms and some dark, mysterious meat. None of it was fancy, but it was all incredibly delicious — Tanner, despite not being the most reliable person to make breakfast, served as their chef for a reason. Violet wolfed it down gratefully. Between bites of her omelette, she asked him: “What meat is this?”

“Vampire.” 

“I’ve never had tha —” Violet’s face froze as she realized what he said. And then she promptly spit out her omelette. Meanwhile, Tanner continued eating his food like there was nothing wrong with it. 

“...Why?” The normally talkative Violet could only muster up this one word. In response, Tanner shrugged. “Seemed fun. And it’s delicious?” If it were anyone else, Akito would have quickly laughed it off inside his mind as a joke. The only issue was that he was pretty certain Tanner wasn’t joking. A multitude of thoughts flooded into his mind.

Truthfully, this war was built on lies. It wasn’t the vampires that saw humans as a vital food source. It was the other way around. It was the vampires that were trying to escape the oppression spearheaded by one man, the mastermind Tanner. 

That would be a fun plot twist. 

Of course, Akito kept his thoughts to himself. He speared the omelette with his fork and lifted it up to his mouth — Tanner had spent effort making it, after all. But before he could, Violet glared daggers at him. “Don’t you dare eat that.” Akito reluctantly obliged and turned his attention to the soup. 

After breakfast, Tanner promptly went back to sleep on the couch, having once again been too lazy to go to his room. Akito and Violet did the dishes together, with the latter taking extra care not to even touch the bits of meat she and Akito had left on their plate. Tanner’s plate was clear, and as Violet applied copious amounts of soap to it, she threw a scowl in the direction of the couch. 

And then…there was essentially nothing left to do.

When Akito had first been accepted by the army, he had serious doubts about why they would just let someone in who had no prior experience, training, or inkling of knowledge of how to pilot a fairy. Though he still had his doubts, he believed a part of it was that the war oftentimes barely concerned them. With the exception of an ambush on the fairy of ice a few days ago, <Shadow> almost never directly attacked them. Instead they focused on defending the sparsely planned offensive measures taken by the humans, and as the commanders of the human army preferred to mobilize the eastern squadrons due to the island cover, Base 33 saw little actual fighting. Once, he had heard Violet call the war one in name alone. 

Their daily wartime duties was a two-hour patrol extending roughly fifty kilometers from the mainland. The area they covered overlapped with that of other squadrons, and so there was plenty of time where the three members of Base 33 were together. While Tanner was sleeping, Akito and Violet passed the time in the living room, doing their own activities — they had an unspoken agreement to only start working on the blueprints in Akito’s books after they were both done with patrols. 

Violet was drawing something. Sheets of paper were scattered all across the round table in the center of the living room, with some nudging against Akito’s radio. Every so often, she glanced at a notebook, studying it before returning back to her drawings. With a sinking feeling, Akito realized that was the notebook he had used to write his story series — Selfish. Violet had said that his illustrations were terrible, and she was taking it upon herself to improve them. 

Akito thought back to the conversation about the story with Violet and Lazu a few days ago. He remembered how frank and probably insensitive he had been with Violet, to the point that he had kicked her.

In other words, he wanted to hit himself. 

Violet was blissfully unaware of Akito’s inner turmoil. She continued drawing, breaking her concentration every once in a while to clarify some of the character designs with him. A short while later, it was time for her patrol, and then the moment she got back, it was Tanner’s. Or at least, it should have been, but Tanner decided to procrastinate for three hours before finally transforming into the fairy of the stars. 

He really doesn’t mind jeopardizing the safety of the human race…

The hour hand of the clock in the living room was a smidge past four. Akito was sitting by the round table, in place of Violet. He put his pen to his chin. In front of him was his notebook, containing the words he wrote in handwriting he wished could be better. Normally, he only wrote his story when he got permission to leave Base 33 and nestle in the forest around him. But today, he didn’t really mind the warmth of the cabin, nor Violet’s incessant questions about his writing. They passed the time through stints of idle chatter and comfortable silence. 

“I’m going to the washroom,” Violet announced at some point. Akito nodded in acknowledgement, though he did think to himself that wasn’t something Violet needed to proclaim. He was left in the living room by himself, and as he eyed the radio on the table distantly, he decided to start writing again.

Start with the first thought that comes to mind.

Right…today we ate vampire meat… 

Akito wasn’t sure if that was how all authors got inspiration, but it worked for him.

The main entrance to the cabin creaked open, tearing him from his inner ramblings. It didn’t have a lock, given how remote Base 33 was, so Akito was given little notice beforehand. He glanced at the clock. Tanner must have decided to turn back after just ten minutes in the air; Akito wouldn’t put it past him to do that. “Welcome back”, he began, before cutting himself short as a stranger walked through the doorway. Her shoulder-length hair swished silently as she closed the door behind her. She and Akito made eye contact, and Akito quickly averted his gaze. 

“You’re Akito, correct?” The stranger, who seemed older than Akito and about the same age as Tanner, asked. “I apologize it took us this long to get acquainted.” Akito tried his best to stammer out a reply, and failed miserably. The stranger continued. “I’m Minji, commander of the 33rd squadron. It’s a pleasure to meet you.” Minji extended her hand, and Akito fumbled around, trying to connect his limbs in a working manner, before shaking it. 

“Akito, what happened? Why are you so scared?” Violet’s voice came from the hallway at the absolute worst time, and Akito could just stare at her dumbfoundedly. Thankfully, though, Minji didn’t mind.

“Good to see you, Violet.”

“Oh, you’re back!”

Violet clearly wasn’t as shocked as Akito that there even was a fourth member of the squadron, let alone the commander. 

Though Minji kept her attention on the two, her eyes had been scanning the room for something else since she walked in. A slight frown creased her black eyes. “Is Tanner not back? Was his shift not three hours ago?” Akito tried to explain, but the words caught in his throat. Violet bailed him out. “He just left for patrol, like ten minutes ago.” 

“Oh.” Minji sighed. “I’ll have to scold him later.” But her frown relaxed, as if contradicting her words. She turned to Akito. “I’ll be in your care.” 

“W-wha, um, uh, sorry, same.”

Violet was looking at him oddly and seemed primed to comment something that would surely destroy Akito’s self-esteem further, but Minji continued before she could say something. “I’ll be working in my room. If you’ll excuse me.” She took off her shoes at the entrance and walked past them, turning into the first corridor to the right. With a soft click, the padlock guarding the door unlocked, and Minji disappeared inside before gently shutting the door behind her. 

Akito collapsed on the table, drained. Violet stared uncomfortably at Akito before finally saying to him: “You…tried, I guess.” That was about as close to an attempt at consolation as one would ever get from Violet, but even so, Akito turned on her. “Sorry if I'm wrong, but you’ve never mentioned anything about a fourth member.” 

“Didn’t Tanner?” Violet asked frankly. “She is his wife.”

Wait, what? Akito froze, while Violet continued looking at him like that was common knowledge. “And besides,” she continued, gesturing to the room that Minji just disappeared into, “why else would we have four bedrooms?”

“I thought that was because someone died!” Akito protested, though Violet seemed unable to process that nuance. “Anyways, Tanner has a wife???” Violet shrugged. In a voice so blunt it didn’t even seem like she was making a jab at Tanner, she responded: “No clue how he did it.” 

For better or worse, the person in question was off on patrol, unable to defend himself. I guess I’ll have to wait two hours for him to come back so I can ask him…

Four hours later, Akito found himself cursing his naivety. Tanner still hadn’t come back.

~

“Purple, Aki-cchi, I’m back!” At half past eight, there was a whirlwind of commotion at the entrance. Tanner, still equipped in the spacesuit-esque garb of Nova, flew through the front door. 

“Don’t call me that!” Violet used the last of her energy reserves to interject. She and Akito had been sprawled out underneath the round table for the past few minutes, doing their best to ignore the growling of their stomachs. In the sink was a pile of mildly burnt kitchinery, leftovers from their attempts to try and make lunch and dinner themselves. “Where were you?” Akito asked him. 

Tanner transformed back to his messy shirt and shorts, but before he could answer, a door to his right unlocked. Minji walked briskly to him and pulled him into a stiff hug. Tanner seemed surprised to see her, then melted into his regular goofy grin. 

“Welcome back, Minji — ow!” He yelped in surprise as Minji promptly stepped back from the embrace and flicked his forehead with her index finger. “You didn’t take your assigned shift.” Tanner began to speak, but he was cut off by another three forehead flicks, each making a distressingly hollow clunk. “And. You’re. Late,” Minji pointed out dispassionately, flicking his forehead in time with her words. She glared at him, leaving him to explain himself. 

“Well,” Tanner began, “when I was patrolling, I saw a big eagle…ack!” As Tanner rubbed his forehead gingerly, Minji scolded him further. “<Shadow> finally makes a move for the first time in months, successfully kills two fairies, and almost kills Circe. And you decide to come back two hours later than you should have?”

“It’s fine, no? And besides, if I knew you were coming back, I would have come home earlier,” Tanner pointed out in a small voice, but was instantly silenced by a cold glare. “It's not fine. Understood?” In response, Tanner could only meekly nod. 

“Good. Then I’ll be working in my room.” Minji spun on her heel and marched back to her room. She opened her door. Her hand hesitated on the handle. “And I’m looking forward to dinner.” She glanced briefly at Tanner before averting her gaze and locking the door behind her. “Okay!” Tanner called out, with a tone that didn’t contain a trace of the scolding he had just received. He turned to Akito and Violet. “What do y’all want for dinner?” 

The mention of food was enough to rouse Akito and Violet. Their eyes regained some light as they thought about what they wanted to eat. They came to one consensus answer. 

“NOT vampire!” 

…

The next day, Akito woke up at his usual time, having slept off the effects of his night patrol. He sang — privately, of course: he didn’t think he could handle it if Violet heard —  as he got ready for a new day. As he walked out the corridor, a perpetually cheerful voice greeted him. “Morning, Aki-cchi!”

Wow, Tanner’s up early for once. No, more than that, he had prepared breakfast too. Tanner had decided to use some of the rice that had just been delivered to them from the main complex, and four steaming plates of fried rice with assorted mushrooms and vegetables lined the counter. Akito was pretty sure he had eaten better since he joined the wartime army than before it. 

As Akito greeted him in return, Tanner carried a plate of rice over to Minji’s room. He knocked twice, and Minji opened the door from inside. It was the first time Akito had seen her since when she greeted Tanner yesterday: she hadn’t joined them for dinner and had seemingly pulled an all-nighter within the confines of her room. She accepted the plate gratefully, and they exchanged a few words Akito couldn’t quite catch before Minji closed the door somewhat in Tanner’s face. 

Tanner didn’t seem to mind, though. He turned around without skipping a beat and told Akito: “I’m going to sleep now!” 

Right…of course.

~~ Another ~~

“Well then, may we meet beneath an infinite dawn!”
“See you, Lazurin!”
“G’night!”

The sky outside Base 33 was pitch black. Another day had concluded with their meeting with Lazu over the radio. Akito stretched his arms as Tanner turned the knob on the radio, quickly reducing the static to a comfortable silence. It had been an incredibly peaceful week for the western front.

Violet was already in her bed. They had gone past their regular ending times, and now Akito yawned. I should go to sleep too. 

Just before Akito got up, he heard Tanner speak up. “Minji, do you need anything?” 

“Thanks, but I’m good.” The voice came from behind him, and Akito whirled around. It was one of the few times he had seen her since their introduction over a week ago. She was always either away or holed herself in her room working. Truth to be told, he was impressed by her productivity — though, neither he nor Violet knew what she was productive on. “And I wanted to ask,” Minji turned to the wooden box on the table, “is that a radio?” 

Akito nodded. It looked nothing like the handheld radio conventionally used by the human army. In fact, if she hadn’t listened in to their conversation, she might not have thought it was a radio at all. 

A shift in her expression. “Who are you radioing?” 

“A-a friend,” Akito replied. Explaining who was actually behind the radio was a hassle he didn’t want to get into. But avoiding the question only made the corners of Minji’s lips crease downwards slightly. Ignoring Akito’s slightly pained look, she asked: “Could you describe your friend?”

As Akito explained more and more about Lazu, he started to realize her circumstances didn’t exactly paint her in the best light. When he was done talking about how she was one of the humans held captive on Complex Alpha and how they had started communicating with one another, Minji turned to Tanner. “Did you know about all this?” Tanner shrugged, unworried. “Yeah, but it’s fine, right?” 

He was silenced by a flick to the forehead. Minji’s voice was even and composed as she replied, but Tanner knew her well enough to realize she was quite irritated. “The circumstances Akito is describing cannot be completely true. The most logical conclusion would be that the person on the other end of the radio is an elf —”

“Lazu isn’t an enemy.” 

Akito’s words were spoken in a low, unhesitating voice, far removed from his typical demeanour. Minji turned her eyes on him, seemingly surprised by something in his gaze. There was a stretch of tense silence. And then, as if realizing he was the one who said those words, he began stammering and bowing in quick succession. “Uh, um, s-sorry.”

Minji shook her head. “I should be the one apologizing. That was insensitive of me. But,” she continued, “it would not be surprising if the elves and vampires are listening in on your conversations without Lazu realizing.”

Truth to be told, Akito had realized this possibility a long time ago. He started to object, but then fell silent. Minji let out a small, appreciative smile seeing this. “I trust as soldiers of the army, there hasn’t been anything important you’ve shared with her?” 

“Sorry, just f-fairy attributes,” Akito clarified. There had been a lot of things he had hid from Lazu pertaining to how the human army operated. Though he didn’t want to admit it, he knew Minji was right about their conversations being leaked to the enemy (if they cared enough). Minji seemed satisfied with that answer.  “Good. Then would it be possible if I confiscated the radio —”

“B-but! Wouldn’t it be a good idea to have a spy on the island? We could use Lazu to get information about the enemy, right?” It was Akito’s last resort, and though he was afraid Minji wouldn’t take it seriously, the commander of Base 33 gave it some thought. Finally: “Though I admit there is some value in having an ear within Complex Alpha, how can you guarantee that you won’t be the ones accidentally revealing information you shouldn’t be? Given how close you have become with her.” Her stance was reasonable — if anything, it was the expected reaction and far more rational than Violet and Tanner’s acceptance. Akito was lost for words. 

“So, if we can guarantee it, then it’s okay?” Tanner, who had stayed silent the whole time, spoke up. Minji turned to him, considering his words, before assenting. “I suppose that is my main concern.”

“Then just join us for our meetings! You can guarantee it yourself, right?” 

Minji and Akito both gaped at him. Evidently, none of them had realized that was even an option. “But, I have work…” Minji began to object. 

“It’s fine! I want you to take a break! Besides, you said you wouldn’t be leaving Base 33 again for a while, right?” Tanner replied.

“Y-yeah!”

Akito chimed in, sensing merit in Tanner’s method. Even so, Minji kept muttering to herself: “And you met for over an hour today…that’s a lot of time…”

“How about this!” Tanner exclaimed. “You don’t work during meals, right? So just save your breakfast, lunch, and dinner until our meeting! That way, you can just eat in the hour that we meet, so you won’t lose any time!”

“...”

Akito glanced at Tanner. “Not helping.” Tanner, meanwhile, seemed genuinely confused. “I am helping?”

“No, you’re not! You're the only one who thinks that’s how meals work!”

Though Minji kept her unexpressive appearance, she let out a sigh, barely perceptible amidst the commotion, as she watched the three go back and forth. It was evident she was still undecided. Tanner, who had been stretching out his arms on the table like a cat, turned his face towards her. His eyes made contact with hers through his wavy brown hair.

“Minji, I’ll get to see you more often.”

Minji stared at him. And then, she averted her gaze. “Fine, I’ll allow the radio.” She turned away from them and began heading back to her room. “In that case, I better get back to work.” She briskly walked back to her room, and there was silence until they heard the sound of a lock clicking and the door closing. 

Tanner flashed a V for victory before promptly flopping lazily onto the couch and setting up a game console on the television. As if he had completely forgotten about the conversation a few seconds ago, he spoke to Akito: “Akito, play with me!”

Surprised by the sudden shift in topic, Akito replied: “I need to sleep though…”

“No you don’t! Come on!”

Akito, much to his chagrin, quickly folded despite his tiredness. As he sat down on the couch besides Tanner, he decided not to think about the surprising amount of charm Tanner just displayed. 

~

Six fairies had been killed since Blue had met Lapis. Of those six, five had met their fate at the hands of the fairy of flight. 

All of their kills after Antarc were them aggressing into enemy territory and hunting down fairies indiscriminately. They went solo. Blue still hadn’t fought with the vampires or Nightjars, though as Lapis once remarked to Blue, there wasn’t much difference between solo fights and large-scale conflicts: the fairies liked to spread out and fight one-on-one anyways to avoid having their attacks getting in each other’s way.

There was one other common thread in their fights. Lapis had kept her promises to Blue. From their fight against Antarc onwards, not a single human pilot they were fighting had died. Lapis did say to Blue that the rest of the elf/vampire army couldn’t keep the same promise — in fact, Blue had heard traces of dissatisfactory muttering about how Lapis favoured the humans far too much, behind the elf's back. But, no one complained directly to the supreme commander. Everyone Blue asked said she was doing an excellent job leading the army, far better than anyone else could have.

Blue herself didn’t have anything to complain about. If anything, Blue thought Lapis was making it look too easy. After their flight against Antarc, Blue had lifted her temporary ban on <Missiles>, and since then Blue’s health bar hadn’t even lost a smidge.

Now, walking down the gravel road outside the complex, Blue thought about all of this. A while ago, they had come back from yet another peaceful patrol. Human attacks were less and less frequent — losing five fairies was a sizable blow to an army of roughly two hundred. She had entertained the idea of asking Lapis to spare the fairies themselves. That was incredibly unrealistic, though. Besides, Lapis had told her they fairies were just cores anyways.

She came across a fork in the path. When they had gone on their picnic two weeks ago, Mitsui had taken the right, towards the meadows. Today, Blue went left. With a spring in her step, she traced a path above the shore. The tall cliffs gradually leveled out, then transitioned into a long, sandy beach. Blue could see a trail of footsteps stretching into the distance. She hopped like a rabbit, jumping from footstep to footstep, trying not to make any new indentations in the sand. 

The sound of squealing took her attention away from the sand. Blue looked up. A makeshift net was set up on two poles, and four people were tossing a ball within a box drawn in the sand. Blue vaguely recognized it as a game of volleyball — though it was the first time Blue had seen it played on a beach. 

Erin was sitting on the sand, so focused on the game that she didn’t hear Blue run up to her. Blue opened her mouth to greet Erin, but then decided otherwise and crept the last few steps in silence. She silently observed Erin with amusement as the princess loudly cheered for any good play and hollered words of encouragement to the losers. Pairs of players cycled on and off the court until Blue finally spoke up. “You aren’t playing?” 

“Oh, hey Blue! Yeah, I’m not playing.” That was surprising — Erin at the very least seemed interested in the sport. Blue pressed further: “Why not?”

“I’m not interested at all in volleyball.” Erin answered flatly, before adding, “So, even if there were an even number of players so I could partner up with someone, it’s not like I’d really want to play. Not at all!”

Blue sighed. This person was a lost cause at times. She stepped forward onto the court, where a pair of elves was just coming off. “Erin, I want to try playing! You should be my partner!” The princess stared at her, mouth struggling to form words, before she turned her head to the side and got up. “Guess it can’t be helped. Okay!” She said, completely unable to hide her smile even though she tried.

A murmur spread among the gathering crowd as Erin and Blue took the court. Blue glanced at them; they were probably realizing that a princess and a child wouldn’t make for a dominant team. Blue just hoped Erin had fun. On the plus side, the winner stayed on the court while the loser got off. That meant Blue didn’t have to do much physical exertion.

They got into position. A vampire, presumably the referee, announced: “0 - 0. Start game!” Erin tossed the ball high up in the air. Blue blinked.

She could have sworn the object that flew over her head, past the net, and just within the outer corner of the court was a missile. 

~

Before they began playing, Blue was under the impression that maybe Erin was interested in playing volleyball, but didn’t play because she was bad at it. Blue couldn’t have been more wrong, and in hindsight, maybe she should have taken the hint about Erin’s athletic capabilities from when they went swimming. One hour later, they were still on the court.

Despite the nature of the sport, Erin seemed more than capable of soloing the opponents. Even so, she made sure to include Blue as well, while keeping track of when the fairy seemed out of breath and playing accordingly. Blue hadn’t broken a sweat. She was enjoying the game as well. Now, as she flailed her arms and managed to get the ball across the net and onto the sand, she accepted Erin’s enthusiastic high-five with a wide grin; they had won another match.

The next partners to challenge them, though, were a bit different from the rest. One had small fangs and black hair that reached just past her ruby red eyes. The other had a sailor cap and a pendant that glistened in the sunlight. “What are you two doing here?” Erin asked Lapis and Evie. The former grinned. “Scared? We will be victorious.” 

Erin stiffened, falling for the cheap provocation. 

“Bring it on!” 

…

…

“14 - 14. Erin serves.” The vampire referee announced. He was on his feet, as engrossed in the match as the rest of the crowd. Blue thought she saw Mitsui somewhere in there, but he blended in with the crowd so well that she couldn’t tell for sure. Though Erin and Blue had built up an early lead, their opponents had won five of the past six points, and they were now even. It was a simple first to 15.

Bang! The ball hurtled across the net, aimed right at the empty space in the back of the court. Blue could tell that was easily the fastest serve Erin had unleashed all afternoon. But just before it hit the ground, Evie’s delicate hand launched the ball into the air. Lapis set the ball up, and with unnerving speed, Evie rose up in the air, flaring her wings as she spiked the ball down. But Erin was there to block it, and after Blue kept the point alive, the rally continued. 

Back and forth they went. Erin somehow compensated for Blue’s lack of ability, seemingly being able to control Lapis and Evie’s moves. One bad return by them, and she lifted the ball over the net, opposite where Lapis and Evie both stood. They were both out of position. 

A dazzling laugh. A streak of black. The entire crowd heard her words. “Didn’t I tell you?” One leap, then another, as Lapis flew across the sand. Both her feet touched the ground. Her cloak scraped the sand, then billowed upwards like the cape of a hero. “The main character…”

Lapis didn’t go for the ball. Contrary to a normal person’s intuition, she leapt straight in the air. Saving the ball wasn’t her role. 

Most vampires could only switch between their fully transformed state and their human state. Though both states had echolocation and enhanced regeneration, vampires could either only be a winged bat with super strength the size of a football field, or a regular human with average physical attributes and capabilities. In fact, all vampires were this way, except one. 

By some abnormality during birth, Evie could control the extent of her transformation. She could transform select body parts, be it turning her hand into sharp talons, or the “decorative” wing on her back into the feared one of a vampire. And while maintaining roughly the same mass and physical size, she could replicate vampiric super strength within her human body. Combined, this allowed her to fly much faster than other vampires, since she could reproduce the same wing area and strength without much of the mass. The same applied on land.

That was a key part in what made her the strongest fighter. Though, it wasn’t just for fights.

Evie tensed the muscles in her leg, and enough sand to fill a house shifted under her power. Then, she released, and with a velocity far greater than what any other human-like creature could accomplish, Evie dove straight at the ball. Her fingertips made contact with the ball. She flicked it upwards. For a brief moment, it soared into the air, waiting. 

Waiting for Lapis. 

“Leads their allies…”

The main character pulled her arm backwards. Her flaxen hair caught the wind and streamed backwards, revealing a dazzling smile. She brought her arm down.

“...to victory!”

A large cloud of sand as the ball impacted the ground. And then, when it settled, the announcer exclaimed in a hoarse voice: “Out! Erin and Bluebird win!” 

Stunned silence. And then, cheers and applause erupted from the crowd. Lapis fell to her feet, whimpering: “But…the main character…” Erin glanced down at her uncomfortably, unable to decide whether to console Lapis or gloat in her face. 

As for Blue, she quickly chose the latter. 

~

“Let me get this straight.” The stern voice belonged, unusually, to Mitsui. He was speaking loudly, and with more force than Blue had ever heard from him. “You and Erin decided to play more volleyball after Lapis and everyone left, and for some inane reason you decided to use your full force again. Only this time, you used it in a spike?” 

The subject of his scolding was staring aloofly into the distance, seemingly unable to care less about his rant. Evie replied indifferently: “I didn’t think that idiot would try to return it.”

“You’re the idiotic one. You know Erin as well as us. Of course she’d try to return it.” Mitsui hissed coldly. 

The princess hadn’t appeared for her daily tour of the complex today. She had argued that her physical condition was mostly fine and tried to show up, but her bodyguard had quarantined Erin to her bedroom. Erin was recovering from her injuries after Evie had placed all her vampiric super strength into a spike and she had tried to receive it.  

Now, the culprit glared at Mitsui. “Don’t preach to me, invisible man.” She stormed off, her footsteps echoing hollowly across the floor of the complex. Mitsui watched her go with a tumultuous expression. When he turned back, his voice was guarded. “I’m going to go check on Erin. I’ll leave it to you two.” Blue wondered what he was leaving, but Lapis seemed to have a good idea of what he was talking about. She asked him a bit cryptically: “Why’d you do that if you know what’s going to happen?”

A shrug. And then, Mitsui turned towards the stairs to the second floor and left without a word. Lapis and Blue were left alone for a moment. Then, the former grinned. “Blue, wanna see something interesting?”

They took a different route than both Evie and Mitsui, heading down the ramp to the aircraft hangar. Lapis flipped open the control panel just in front of the hangar doors, while Blue stood on her tiptoes to try and see what she was pressing. A few button presses later, the front of the hangar slid open, and the two of them took to the sky. Blue wondered where Lapis was taking them, but the elf seemed to want to keep it a surprise. They talked about other things as the scenery of the island passed beneath them. 

“I’ve never seen Mitsui mad before. That was surprising,” Blue commented telepathically. She hadn’t expected Mitsui of all people to be telling Evie off like that. Lapis nodded in agreement. “He was also mad at me when you were in depressed pillbug form. When Mitsui tells you that you’re an idiot, you know you are one.” 

Blue started to speak, about to reply to the ‘depressed pillbug’ comment, but she clammed up. That was a pretty apt description. Lapis chuckled at her reaction and continued: “It’s one of the things I envy about him.” 

Blue didn’t expect that from Lapis. She tried to figure out what Lapis was getting at. “...That he tells people they’re idiots?”

“That he communicates his thoughts to people.” But just as Blue was going to ask for further clarification, Lapis added: “For instance, I’ve never told you how fun you are to tease, right?” 

“Huh?” 

“Here goes.” Lapis leaned in close to Blue, and placed her index finger underneath Blue’s chin. She tilted it upwards and stared directly into her eyes. “You’re adorable when you tell me to shut up, my little puppy.” 

Blue tried to physically jump away, but then remembered she was in mech form. “Shu — screw you! And what do you mean ‘my little puppy’?”

A boisterous laugh. “That’s something the main character of a story would say, right? I’ve always wanted to say that.”

“What stories are you reading?” Blue yelped in exasperation.

“Well, let’s see…” They launched into a conversation about their favourite books. There had been a small collection of digital reading tablets left by the ancients. One of them was owned by Erin, and Lapis often snuck into her bedroom to read. Unsurprisingly, the main character preferred action and fantasy. Blue, meanwhile, realized she couldn’t contribute to this conversation at all — all the titles Lapis mentioned were ones she hadn’t read. Instead, she listened with great interest as Lapis spoiled some of the books to her. 

Though, the stories Lapis was talking about weren’t completely foreign to her. 

They hadn’t left the confines of the island during their flight. Instead, they had circled its perimeter idly, as if stalling for time. Now, amidst a conversation about a book called Alice in Wonderland, they landed in one of the grassy meadows near Complex Alpha. Enjoying the sunshine, they strolled through the meadow to a field of strawberries, where Lapis suddenly stopped Blue.

“What are we doing here?” Blue asked her. Lapis gestured to her to stay quiet and duck behind some bushes. They both peeked out. 

Evie was kneeling between the rows of plants, searching for strawberries. It was the very beginning of strawberry season and so many of the fruits hanging from the undersides of the leafy herbs weren't ripe. Even so, the vampire went plant by plant. She finally found one that was ready and clumsily tried to pick it, but it slipped from her fingers and rolled to the ground. Wings wrapped tightly around her, she clambered on all fours to retrieve it.

The look on her face was one far removed from her usual disdainful expression. Blue was beginning to see things from Erin’s point of view — she had to admit Evie was cute. 

“Well, there is a reason we, especially Erin, put up with Evie,” Lapis spoke up, having predicted as much along with Mitsui. “Let's go, Blue.” Remembering that Erin’s favorite food was strawberries, Blue connected the dots. 

Evie didn't sense their approach until Lapis placed another strawberry in the basket next to her. She looked up, her large ruby eyes giving the impression that she could cry at any moment. Lapis chided her gently. “Dumbass.”

“Muuuuu.” The creature in front of them, which was far too cute to be the same being as the prickly Evie, let out what seemed like a low purr. Lapis turned to Blue. “I'll help out. You too, Blue?”

Blue nodded. She had originally planned to exact revenge on Evie for the things she had done, but it wasn’t easy saying no to such a creature. 

And so they spent the afternoon picking strawberries. 

~

On the second floor of the complex, there was a space that was far more spacious and luxurious than the others. Unlike the other single-room pods, it had multiple rooms, a main hallway filled with art installations, and even a private kitchen and bathrooms. The master bedroom had a bed wide enough for two people, a reclining chair and bookshelf, and a picturesque balcony that jutted out of the cliffside. 

Lapis called it the princess’ palace. It was the royal family’s living quarters, though Erin had been sharing it with a few other families ever since her parents died. Today, Erin’s bodyguard lay with her eyes closed by the front porch, half-expecting someone to show up even though they hadn’t made prior arrangements. At around dinnertime, her prediction came true. 

Evie shuffled towards her, having retracted her fangs as a show of amity. Clutched tightly in her arms was a large basket of strawberries. Evie stopped in front of her and peeked out from under her bangs, bowing slightly. Erin’s bodyguard got up and let out a long sigh. “My lady is currently resting in her room.” 

A knock startled Erin as she lay idly in bed. There had been nothing for her to do all day except reread manga with her reading tablet. She sluggishly wondered if the knock was her bodyguard delivering dinner. 

“Come in. The door’s unlocked.” 

But instead of her bodyguard, it was another familiar face that entered. Her ruby eyes glanced up at Erin, then, having quickly verified she looked okay, quickly dropped down to the floor. As Evie crossed the room briskly, Erin smiled at her. “Sorry I couldn’t get out today. I’m honestly fine; I don’t know why I’m being kept here. I’m just a bit tired.” 

“U-um, no, uh,” the vampire stammered docilely — a complete contrast from her usual behaviour — “I’m sorry!” She bowed and extended the basket of strawberries to Erin. The princess’ eyes lit up. She quickly snatched the basket, as a precaution in case Evie changed her mind or someone took it away. Without any delay, she began eating.

“Are you going to sit?” Erin asked with her mouth full. Evie hesitated for a moment, before climbing onto the bed and wrapping her wings tightly around her like a sausage roll. She didn’t move as Erin drew closer, as if signalling that the princess could pet her to her heart’s content without any of the usual repercussions. But instead, Erin lay down beside her. She took out her reading tablet and placed it in front of them both. “I’d be angrier at you if you didn’t use your full strength. Anyways, you haven’t read this one, right? Let’s read it together!”

Evie was momentarily surprised, but then she nodded, still clearly a bit guilty. “Okay.” 

They read side-by-side in comfortable silence, taking every so often to discuss the story. The bowl of strawberries that Evie, Lapis, and Blue had taken three hours to collect had been depleted by Erin within the span of ten minutes. Neither of them moved away or even noticed the half-hour allotted for dinner come and go. Finally, as they finished the second volume, Erin asked Evie: “Sorry, could you get me some water?” 

A bit unwillingly, Evie rolled off the bed and went to the private kitchen. When she came back with a glass of water, Erin was already asleep. She hadn’t even bothered to put the covers over her body, and was sprawled across the bed. Evie could just barely pick up the sound of her even breathing. 

The vampire tried to pull the covers out from underneath Erin, but the princess shifted slightly, and Evie quickly let go, unwilling to wake up Erin. Even so, the room was cold. Evie glanced around the room, searching for something suitable to cover Erin with. There was nothing. 

Evie took one last glance around the room. And then, finding no other alternative, she climbed onto the bed and wrapped her wings lightly around Erin. Hopefully that would be enough to keep her warm.

…
When Evie next opened her eyes, she found Erin staring at her. The light outside the balcony had changed from a deep black to a hopeful saffron. They had apparently slept into the morning.

Erin laughed gently as her eyes made contact with Evie’s. “Good morning, Evie.” Then, in a quieter voice, she added: “Thanks.”

“...”

Suddenly, there was a burst of movement. Before Erin could react, Evie had used her super strength, jumped off the bed, and raced to the balcony. She stayed perched on top of the balcony railing for a moment, face pointedly turned away from Erin. 

“Know your place, food source,” she growled. 

There was a flash of black, a spreading of wings, as the vampire leapt from the railing and was gone. Evie didn’t look back. She couldn’t, lest she show Erin the rapidly spreading heat across her cheeks. 

~

For some reason, Lazu hadn’t connected to the radio the day after Minji had allowed its existence. It wasn’t unusual for Lazu to skip a day, and they never really minded nor asked her why she did. Even still, Akito couldn’t help but worry about her. 

Tonight, there was a new addition joining Tanner by the couch. Minji had brought some of her work documents out to the common space, and despite the loud chatter between Violet and Akito as well as the TV show Tanner was watching, she was impressively focused on her work. From the glimpses Akito caught, it seemed related to their patrol routes. She really didn’t seem to take breaks — though Tanner had managed to wrench her attention away every once in a while.

As the hours ticked down to ten in the evening, Akito flipped through the first book of Selfish. He had the habit of randomly going back to previous excerpts long after he had finished them — for better or worse, he was always under the nagging belief that he could improve them. Now, he stopped at a page in the middle of the notebook.
---------------------------------------------------------

From Akito’s Notebook
Selfish, Chapter 2

Rubio sighed as he picked up the umbrella. Its paper canopy disappeared in a small glimmer of light, leaving him with an ubiquitous wooden cane. Sitting besides him, Skye spoke up in an unusually timid voice. “You’re not killing him?”

At Rubio’s feet was the government soldier with the Blessing of fire — Rubio vaguely remembered that he gave his name as Anton. The pinapera had worked itself into Anton’s body long ago, and now he was unconscious. Rubio gave his body a rough kick with his boot. “No point. Whether or not he dies, the government knows who we both are thanks to someone choosing to be a saint.” He threw a sharp glance at Skye, one far more scathing than any words he could have said. Skye said nothing in return. She just hunched her figure further and concentrated on the red of his umbrella. 

For a few seconds, Rubio glared soundlessly at her. The only sound came from the distant town, now shrouded by the forest. No doubt, every single government member there was on a manhunt for a Blessed with an umbrella and an idiot. 

Finally, Rubio turned his attention back to the body in front of him. He sighed. He was far too selfish to spare Anton’s life. But Skye had wanted to save the life of the government guard who had tried to kill them, and by extension, Rubio, who was under the influence of her Blessing, could not kill him. 

I suppose in the end, I’m the idiot for revealing my name. 

Rubio turned around abruptly, his brown robe swishing against the dead leaves on the ground. Facing the depths of the forest, he said: “We’re going.” Skye’s eyes turned towards the seemingly never-ending mass of trees. “But…go where?”

“Obviously the main road, I bet the million Authority members there will be happy to see us…”

Skye looked at his back, confused. “But then they’ll capture…”

“No shit. We’re going to Aria through the forest. I didn’t want to do this, but since someone decided to attack the all-powerful government…” Even as he began twirling the umbrella-turned-stick impatiently, she still made no move and only stared blankly at him. This was getting mildly annoying. Rubio extended a hand to her. 

“Just take my hand.”

And finally, Skye cracked a smile. She emphatically ignored his hand, pushed herself onto her two feet, and slipped her bow back into her sling. “You should thank me for giving you a noble cause to use your Blessing. Knowing you, you probably would have revealed it in the stupidest way sooner or later.”

No remorse, huh?  Rubio sighed and turned his attention onto the path ahead.

As the clamor around the city grew increasingly louder, two figures left an unconscious body behind and disappeared into the brush.

---------------------------------------------------------
Obviously Anton survives since he’s a main character, and I like the plot point of Skye saving his life. But given her character development up to this point, would Skye really save him out of the goodness of her heart?

Before he could come up with an answer to his own question, the clock struck ten. This time, when Violet turned the knob on the radio, it connected immediately. She burst in before either Akito or Lazu could speak. “Lazu, there’s someone you should meet!” A pause. And then, with her usual flamboyant voice, Lapis mused: “A new character this late into the story? They must be quite plot relevant, then. Who is it?”

Minji got off the couch and kneeled primly next to the table. “Hello. Is it Lazu?”

In her bedroom on the other side of the radio, Lapis smiled. “Indeed! I am Lazu of the infinite dawn, supreme commander of everything between the two ethereal horizons. And what is your name?” 

“I’m Minji, leader of the 33rd squadron. It’s nice to meet you.” 

“That’s a boring intro,” Violet interjected bluntly. Lapis shrugged and spoke to Violet in a hushed whisper that was still clearly meant to be heard by Minji. “It’s fine. After all, it adds to her characterization as a mature, serious character! There’s no need to reveal her gap moe so quickly.” 

“Gap moe?”

While Lapis was filling Violet’s head with nonsense (which Violet eagerly accepted), Tanner leaned in to Minji. “Minji, you should do a similar introduction!”

“Why?”

“It’ll be fun! Try it!”

Minji stared at Tanner for a moment before averting her gaze and muttering in a voice low enough that Lapis and Violet couldn’t pick it up over their chatter (though Akito was still listening): “I’m Minji, agent of light for the 33rd specialized task force of the west —”. She broke off. “No more!”

Oh, so she has the fairy of light? Akito thought to himself.

“Why? That was so good though — ow!” Tanner began to complain, only to get hit with a flick to the forehead. Minji turned around and caught a glimpse of Akito peeking worriedly at her, praying that she didn’t have a bad impression of Lazu — after all, she could confiscate the radio at any moment. Minji let out a small reassuring smile. “Don’t worry, I’m not that shallow. Though,” she turned to watch Violet and Lazu discuss what gap moe Minji could have, “you have interesting friends.”

That doesn’t sound like a compliment… For now, Akito stammered: “Uh, umm…Sorry.”

~

“Let’s play a game!”

After having bombarded Minji with questions the same way she did to Tanner and Violet when they first met (though the leader of the squadron was noticeably more guarded than Violet or Tanner), Lapis suggested something a bit surprising. Violet immediately shot to her feet, sparkles in her eyes. “Sounds fun! What game?”

“Have you heard of twenty questions? Let’s play that, but we only get ten questions, and we have to choose one of our character traits!” 

Akito sighed inwardly. He had bad memories of that game — it was usually an icebreaker, and icebreakers usually meant meeting strangers. Violet shared none of his trauma, however, as she nodded eagerly with unfettered enthusiasm. “I’ll start.” Lapis thought for a moment. “Okay, I’ve decided on something related to me that most of you know. It could be an object, a person, or even an adjective, but it’s something about me. You all have ten yes or no questions to try and figure out what I’m thinking of. And…” she drumrolled dramatically, “...Start!”

Lapis’ turn. 

Almost immediately, Violet asked: “Is it related to being the main character?” On the couch, Tanner laughed. “That’s exactly what I was going to ask!” Minji and Akito, meanwhile, both nodded in agreement. Silence on the other end of the radio. And then, Lapis let out a very pained yes. 

“Is it: ‘I am Lazu of the infinite dawn, supreme commander of everything between the two ethereal horizons?’” Akito followed up, slightly blushing. All the other members of Base 33 nodded once more. 

An even longer silence. And then, Lapis spoke weakly.

“How’d you get it so quickly…”

“Hah, that was easy! You’re too predictable, Lazu!” Violet wasted no time in taunting Lazu; it was a competitive side of her Akito was well accustomed to whenever they played video games. Lapis grinned at the radio, but she was clearly shaken as she replied: “Let’s see if you can do better!”

Minji’s turn. 

“Is it fine if I just choose a random object, since three of you aren’t that familiar with me?”

Violet, who was taking this game far more seriously than she probably should have been, considered her proposal. Finally, she consented. “But we’ll still get it in ten questions!”

Though, eight questions in, it looked like she had been a bit overconfident. They had narrowed it down to a domestic animal, but nothing more specific than that. “Okay, strategy meeting,” Violet began to say, but Tanner spoke up. “Is it edible?”

Minji chuckled. “By everyone’s definition except for yours, no.” Meanwhile, Violet glared at him with more intensity than Lapis had ever felt from her. “Tanner, what are you doing? How dare you waste one of our questions! We only have one more!”

A nonchalant shrug. “It’s fine, right?”

“Argggh, you’re the worst!”

As Violet pulled Akito towards her to the radio, Akito looked back at Tanner. Tanner whispered something to Minji, who let out a smile wider than Akito had ever expected from her. Violet, however, completely missed this, and together with Akito and Lapis, they began their strategy meeting. 

“So, when you think of a domestic animal, the first thing you think of is a pet, right? And no one in their right mind would choose anything other than a cat or a dog. I think it’s a cat!” Violet spoke as if this were the most important thing in the world to her. Akito nodded. “I get the feeling that Minji wouldn’t pick ‘dog’.”

Violet turned to the direction of the couch. Akito got the feeling that Violet was going to say something dumb. Should I kick her…?

He decided not to, and it cost him. Violet asked brusquely: “Tanner, do you agree? You should know, since you’re literally hers. Surely, you’d know, right?” From the radio came a confused “huh”. Lapis didn’t know Tanner and Minji were a couple, and from the sound of things, she still didn’t know. On any other day, the main character would have realized it by now. Lapis was off her game. 

Tanner, meanwhile, shrugged. “I already got the answer!” Violet glared at him, but seeing that he remained silent, wanting her to guess, she turned to Minji. “Minji, is it —” 

“Peasants, all of you!” A boisterous laugh exited out the radio speakers. Lapis spoke rousingly, her first coherent words since having her turn guessed in two questions. “I agree that from first impressions, Minji may be more cat-like, but that is precisely why she would pick ‘dog’!”

“Why?” Akito asked, but Lapis brazenly ignored him. “Behold the main character’s genius! Minji, is it a dog?”

Minji stared at them all, as calm and composed as ever. And then, the corners of her mouth lifted upwards ever so slightly. “It was a cat.” 

Silence. And then, Violet erupted at the radio. 

“Lazu, you suck! You’re genuinely the worst! How were you so confident in such an incorrect answer? I’m revoking your right to talk, dumbass!” With each sentence Violet hurled her way, Lapis made a sound as if she was getting punched in the gut. Akito was secretly enjoying it — normally, Lapis was the one teasing and not being teased. “Arggggh, why are there only ten questions? That’s unfair! I could have gotten it in one more! Minji, you’re cheating!”

“That’s the rules of the game,” Akito pointed out amusedly.

“I know! I know, but that doesn’t make me feel better! She’s cheating! Cheater!”

Tanner’s turn.

“Is it a person?”
“Yep!”

Surprisingly, Tanner answered affirmative to their first question. From there, it was simply a process of elimination. 

“Is it someone we know?”
“Yeah!”
“Is it —” Lapis began to chime in, but Violet cast a surly glance at the radio. “No talking, Lazu. You’re useless.” Again. Lapis made a sound as if she were punched and clammed up.

“Is it Minji?” Akito asked Tanner their fourth question. Tanner nodded with a grin. “Yeah, that was fast!”

“Slower than Lazu,” Akito pointed out as Lapis made another sound of distress. “Why’d you pick Minji?” Violet asked Tanner. 

“Hmm,” Tanner put his hand to his chin, searching for a reason, “I just chose the first thing I thought of?” Besides him, Minji stared at him in surprise before pointedly turning away. Violet stared at the two of them before beginning: “Tanner…” Akito got the sense of foreboding that she was going to say something dumb once again. Should I kick her…?

“Tanner, you’re quite attractive at times —”

Alright, screw it.

Violet yelped as Akito kicked her in the shin. She pulled him aside, and they began conversing in heated whispers.

“Was I not supposed to say that?”
“Obviously not!” 

Akito’s turn.

Akito hadn’t originally planned to play, but Violet quickly strongarmed him into giving in. This time, it was Lapis who asked the first question, bravely ignoring Violet’s exclamations. “I already know you’ll answer yes beforehand! Is it related to your blueprints?”

“...No.” Akito grinned. “Sorry, I'm not that one-dimensional!” Lapis, once again, acted as if she were hit in the gut. It was really not the main character’s day. 

Though, truth to be told, Akito didn’t think he was that much more one-dimensional than Lazu. He had picked a line from his story, and Tanner quickly guessed if that was the case. Him and Violet began narrowing down the options.

“That’s unfair,” Lapis muttered as Akito answered their questions. In hindsight, Akito did think it was a bit unfair. Despite Lapis constantly asking Akito to share more details about his story, Akito refused to talk — he wanted to finish writing the book he was on before sharing anything with her. He was almost done, but until he was finished, Lapis was completely in the dark about what the plot was or what the story even was about. Akito couldn’t tell if he wanted to surprise her, or if her opinion was simply so valuable that Akito didn’t want to hear it lest she thought badly of his work. 

“Is it the phrase ‘take my hand’?” Minji brought him back to the game with her question. Akito nodded, surprised. “You read the book? I didn’t think you read it, let alone remembered that quote!”

A glimmer of a smile crossed Minji’s face. “I like that quote.” 

Though, the glance she exchanged with Tanner suggested that, maybe, there was a deeper story behind why she remembered it. 

Violet’s turn.

Lapis seemed to recover the moment she realized it was Violet’s turn. Immediately after Violet announced she had thought of something, Lapis stopped her incoherent mumbling and grinned brightly. “Is it the colour purple?”

“Okay, fuck you.”
“Wait, so was I right?” 
“Of course not! And that’s one question you’ve wasted, by the way. Too bad!”

“Just so you know, it has to be your character trait,” Lapis replied flippantly, “Something related to you.”

“Purple isn’t the only thing related to me!”

“Whatever you say, Purple."

While they were busy bickering, Minji and Tanner thought of questions to ask Violet. But just as Tanner was about to speak, Lapis cut him off. “Let me guess. I meant that question as a joke, so if I get this on the first try, I beat our resident Purple, correct?”

“Hah. Fine, I won’t count that first question. No chance you get it anyways, dumbass.”

There was a moment of silence. And then, Lapis laughed. It was a laugh Akito had heard many times before — the dramatic laugh of the main character.

“The main character defies chance!”

“Is it…”

“...”

For the rest of the night, Lapis was teased by all four members of Base 33 for her wildly incorrect guess. It was a night of losses for the main character, which, as Minji quickly found out, was an exceedingly rare occurrence.
