~~ A Windy Valley ~~
It was the last week of spring. The sun that had shone outside for most of spring had now fully warmed up, and today a mildly oppressive heat blanketed the archipelago. Many of the elves and vampires had shed their spring outfit for even lighter clothing, bar Erin, who seemed to be in some sort of dress no matter the weather. The person in front of Blue was yet another anomaly. Lapis was still in her cloak, blouse, and miniskirt. Sometimes, Blue wondered if she even had any other clothing. 

(She would later find out that Lapis didn’t: she had ten copies of the same outfit, and five similar metal umbrellas. The main character needed an uniquely recognizable silhouette for the readers.)

Now, Lapis suggested something they had only done twice in the past two months. “Blue, let’s patrol the west today.”

“Wait what? Today? Why?” In response, Lapis grinned. “Why not? We’ve barely explored the west, right?”

“No! Let’s go to the east today!” Blue was surprisingly adamant to the suggestion, especially since Lapis expected Blue to be elated about exploring a new region. She peered curiously into Blue’s eyes, and the child stared defiantly back at her. “Let’s go to the east today!” Blue repeated.

“Do you have some trauma in the west?” Lapis let out a mock gasp, “It’s a bit early, but is it maybe time for Bluebird’s flashback arc? Very well. Lights, camera, action!”

“Whatever you say.” Blue responded flatly. “But,” she repeated emphatically, “we’re going to the east! There’s still an island I want to explore there!” 

Lapis glanced sideways at Blue for a long time. Finally she shrugged casually. “I guess there’s no difference between whether we go to the west today or tomorrow.”

“Great!”

“However!” Lapis added slyly, “as a responsible older model, I can’t let a spoiled child always have their way.” 

“Screw you!”

Lapis laughed. “Is that how you want to talk to someone who has complete control over you?” Before Blue opened her mouth to interject, she continued. “But I’ll give you a chance. Let’s settle this fair and square, with rock paper scissors!”

As much as Blue hated to admit it, a game purely based on luck was far better for her than something like Uno. She jumped at the chance. Though, as they both brought their fist in front of them, Lapis smirked. “I’ll warn you, I’m really good at this!” Blue let out a wry laugh. “How can you be good at rock paper scissors? You better keep your word if I win!” 

Someday, Blue would learn not to set so many flags before she played against Lapis. Today was not that day. 

“Rock, paper, scissors, shoot!”

…

Less than an hour later, they were flying as low as possible over the sea, trying to escape the intensity of the sun. For the first time, Blue wasn’t the one doing the flying. Instead, she and Lapis were perched on the broad back of a transformed Evie. In any other situation, Blue would have jumped for joy at the wind through her hair and the rug-like feeling of fur beneath her legs. It was so amazing that it was almost enough to make up for the fact that they were currently further west than they had ever been east. Almost. 

But now, she gazed silently eastward — the exact opposite of their current heading — ignoring Lapis’ repeated attempts to get her attention. Lapis gave up and turned to Evie. “Evie, Blue is ignoring me because she lost in rock paper scissors. What should I do?”

Normally, a vampire wouldn’t be much better company in this scenario than Blue: vampires couldn’t talk while they were transformed. But, Evie, being able to control the extent of her transformation at will, had transformed her body into that of a full-sized vampire while keeping her human head and vocal cords. It was a comically hilarious sight to behold, and if Blue wasn’t busy sulking, she would have laughed at Evie until her belly hurt. 

“Have you considered testing the limits of her immunity shield?” Evie responded. She had quickly reverted back to her usual disdainful self after the day they had picked strawberries together. Even still, Blue found that she didn’t mind her contempt as much. 

Lapis put her hand to her chin in contemplation. “Truthfully, I have. I wonder if there’s a limit to how much damage the shield can take? What if I drop her from the stratosphere?” 

“You could always let me fight her.” 

“Would you actually want to fight a child?”

“I’ll gladly fight anyone except for you, Lapis.” 

But even as they continued discussing ways to break through her immunity shield, casually throwing jabs at her in the process, Blue remained silent and pointedly turned her body away from them. Until Evie's ears pricked up. She paused, as if testing the wind, before speaking in a low growl: “Fairies. Thirty kilometers 4 degrees of current position.”

Both Blue and Lapis stiffened. “How many?” Lapis asked. Evie concentrated once more before shaking her head. Even though vampire echolocation had amazing range and accuracy, it had its limits. “I’m not sure. More than 10, though.”

“What?” It was one of the few times Blue had seen Lapis caught truly off guard. “That many? The only notable thing this far west is Oni Island, though.” She fiddled with her pendant in silence before giving commands. “Let’s split here. Evie, you follow them.”

“Permission to engage?” Evie asked, clearly undeterred by the large number of fairies. Lapis stared at her, clearly leaning towards saying no, before sighing. “You’re free to engage them. But only after you’ve determined their objective. Trail them first without revealing yourself.” It was one of the advantages of echolocation — their greater range meant that they could sense the fairies without the fairies being able to sense them in return. 

Evie grinned, and were it not for the rest of her body being that of an oversized bat, Blue could easily admit it was a cute smile. “Understood, commander!” Before Lapis or Blue could say anything, she shrunk the rest of her body into a more compact, aerodynamic form, and shot off into the distance. Lapis and Blue were left in freefall only a few hundred meters above the water. 

As they fell through the afternoon skies, Lapis extended a cloaked sleeve. “Take my hand,” she mouthed, “I need a cool cutscene”.

Blue glanced at her hand before promptly ignoring it. Shaking her head, Lapis reached out anyways, twirling Blue around in a mid-air dance before seamlessly transitioning into level flight across the ocean.

~

Roughly halfway between the mainland and Complex Alpha was one of the largest islands in the archipelago. After a major battle between the two armies that had destroyed half the island early in the war, it had been cleared of nearly all vegetation by <Shadow> to avoid the human army from setting up a post there. The island had been turned into a hollow crater, an artificial valley. 

Right now, sitting listlessly within the narrow ring of trees that lined the cliffs — the only cover within the completely barren valley— was Violet, in the form of her fairy. 

“Why am I stuck standing guard here?” Violet asked. Even though she was the only person there, she was talking with Minji.

Fairies could set up a communication network between themselves and a few other fairies. They could communicate with one another, and within a certain range, they could share sensory information as well. Now, even though Minji (transformed into her fairy) was seated in her room in Base 33, she could see the barren landscape, health, and radar display that Violet had. This was one of the responsibilities of a commander, and it was an advantage the humans had that <Shadow> didn't know of. 

“It’s better to be safe —” Minji began to say. But she was cut off by a single blip on their radar screen, flying far faster than a normal fairy. Minji and Violet noticed it at the same time, and Violet immediately poked her head out of the sparse vegetation. A flash of black and blue light shot past her field of view, headed westward. 

“The heading to Oni Island.” Minji muttered under her breath, low enough that Violet couldn't pick it up and ask questions. “That alters our plans.” There was silence on the other end for a few seconds before Minji relayed her decision. “Please engage them. Escape with <Jetstream> if you reach half health.”

“Was that the enemy fairy I've heard about?”

“Yes.” Minji confirmed. All commanders had been warned about the fairy who sided with the elves and achieved such successful results. In many other scenarios, she wouldn't have asked a soldier to directly engage them. But now, she repeated, “Escape the moment you reach half health, no matter what.” 

Violet shrugged. “Understood. But I’ll be okay.” She smiled.

“I have Rocco-chan with me!”

~

“Lapis, where are we going?” Blue whined as they flew past a barren island heading west. She received no response from the elf, and she pestered her again. “Lapis? Lapis? Stop ignoring me!”

Lapis smirked. “Not interested in tasting your own medicine?”

“Ughhh, okay, I'm sorry!” Blue gave in and apologized. Satisfied, Lapis decided to answer her question. “We're headed to the place where the story began.” Blue mulled over her cryptic words for a moment before realizing what she meant. “Oni Island? But why?”

“The only notable destination this far west is Oni Island.” Lapis explained. “I just want to check if anything’s amiss there.” A pause, and then, “I doubt there is though. The Oni have been neutral for so long I doubt they want to join a war.” Blue stayed uncharacteristically silent, thinking about her words. And then suddenly, she exclaimed: 

“From the right!”

Lapis twisted her body and scanned the open sky to her right. Even though there was nothing in sight, a marking had shown up on her radar, intercepting their route.

The wind shifted, as if announcing the arrival of a storm. Lapis stared at the mark on her radar before slowing down. She tilted her head back. 

A gray blade sliced the air just above her visor. 

As Lapis spun around, trying to get a visual on the fairy that had attacked them, there was the howling of wind. And then, their assailant shot through the sky, appearing directly in front of them.

The fairy was the colour of angry storm clouds. Two dark gray discs levitated around her, funneling the surrounding air like water to a drain. In her right hand was a silver greatsword, enveloped in a swirling maelstrom of wind — no, it was more accurate to say that the blade comprised the wind itself. Now, the fairy — Scirocco of the wind — raised her cleaver high in the air before swinging it down towards Blue’s crest. Lapis applied full left power in an attempt to sidestep it. The channels of light extending to her thrusters smoldered brighter. But they stayed frozen in place, as if her engines had ignored their commands. 
---------------------------------------------------------

LAPISNOTES

SCIROCCO OF THE WIND

Propulsion System: Normal
Speed: Normal
Unique Traits: None
Name: A hot wind from the Sahara

Attack:
<Breeze Blade>
User has a greatsword crafted from blades of wind 
 Very short range, no unload or reload speed, ability is always active
Is a physical object i.e. is affected by <Turbulence>
However, user is unable to let go of <Breeze Blade>, and it cannot be damaged by attacks

Defense:
<Turbulence>
Within a 1 km radius of the user, they can control the flow of wind within that area. This includes being able to control the flow of wind differently in subareas, controlling direction, and controlling intensity up to a certain force (roughly the same as a non-charged up <Jetstream>)
Done in mind, similarly to visualizing a trigger for general attacks
No unload or reload speed, ability is always active

Misc:
<Jetstream> (Utility)
User charges up a disc with wind from the surroundings. When the user desires, a tornado is released from the disc that propels the user with a speed proportional to how much <Jetstream> is charged up
Takes 5 seconds to fully charge, which will propel the user at Mach 1.1
<Jetstream> can only be pointed at the user itself (i.e. the user cannot use it offensively by pointing it at their enemy and away from them, nor can it be used to blow away projectiles by the same logic)
Fast unload speed (does not factor into account charge speed), medium reload, two ammo (two discs)

---------------------------------------------------------

At the last moment, Lapis threw a sharp right jab. The muzzle of her Gatling Gun connected with the base of the sword, delaying its swing enough for her thrusters to finally have an effect. But even then, their movement was sluggish. Though Lapis was applying full reverse thrust — which should have been far more than enough given the power of Blue’s thrusters — she was just barely able to backtrack out of range of Scirocco’s flurry of slashes. It was as if the air around them was conspiring to restrict their movements. “Blue, are you still ignoring me? Aren’t you too young to be playing hard to get?” Lapis asked as she evaded a forward thrust by a hair’s width. 

“It’s not me!” Blue exclaimed. “It’s the wind!” 

Lapis, in the mecha suit, couldn’t feel any physical sensations. Scirocco lunged at them with a forward thrust, and Lapis deployed her parachute, unable to will her mecha suit into dodging the next attack. As the greatsword cut into the dense black fabric of <Parachute>, she replied: “The reader’s not dumb! No need to name-drop the fairy’s attribute like that.”

“Hey, I’m being serious! It feels like flying in a hurricane!” 

Lapis feinted a sidestep, and her attacker fell for it, finally giving her the separation to ready her gun. She fired as Scirocco charged at them once more. But the moment she did, a ferocious gale appeared out of nowhere, curving most of the bullets’ trajectories downwards and sending them hurtling away from the target. Scirocco didn’t stop as she blocked the remaining stray bullets with her greatsword — if anything, she sped up, aided by a tailwind that had once again manifested from thin air. It seemed Scirocco had a way to control the wind around them at will. 

In a split second, Scirocco had closed the distance, slamming straight into Lapis’ <Parachute>. Sparks of amber flame jumped out into the air as the wind carved through the fabric, an unstoppable force overcoming the barrier despite its high survivability. With a final shower of sparks, the parachute ripped open, revealing Scirroco’s striking grey eye. It reflected the open skies in all its majesty. And it reflected something else — Lapis’ missile launcher, lying in wait for Scirocco to break through. 

Lapis grinned. “My turn.” 

Blue light flared around her left arm, and from within its depths, a <Missile> jettisoned out, straight on a collision course with Scirocco.

At that moment, Minji heard Violet yell: “<Turbulence>!”. 

In terms of defensive abilities, Scirocco’s was, while the weakest defensively, easily the most versatile. <Turbulence> allowed her to control the wind in a radius around her, noticeably changing the movement of both Violet and her enemies. An updraft appeared below Lapis and Blue. Lapis reacted instantly, counteracting it with her thrusters. But the missile she had just fired couldn’t react in the same way. The updraft carried it up and back in the direction it came from — straight towards Lapis. 

An explosion rocked the skies a few kilometers west of the barren valley. 

Both Lapis and Scirocco had been thrown away by the explosion. Lapis checked her health bar. It was a noticeable chunk below full health — the first substantial amount of damage she had taken since their fight with Circe. And it could have been worse. Had Lapis not fired her second missile to intercept the first, they would have taken the full brunt of the damage. “Blue, are you okay?” Lapis asked the voice in her head. 

“I’m good.” Blue responded. It only hurt as much as if she had been stabbed in the abdomen — she had been through far worse. She directed her anger to the grey figure in the sky. “What was that?” 

“Seems like I’ve been underestimating her a bit.” Lapis acknowledged.

Meanwhile, Violet’s peeved voice was filling up Minji’s communication lines. “Seriously? How was I also hit by that? They’re definitely hacking! Hackers!” Her health bar had also dropped below full health due to the explosion, though only by a smidge. Minji let out a small smile; Violet was up to her usual antics. 

~

Yet another bombardment of <Gatling Gun> fire poured down on Scirocco. Lapis and Blue were still within the range of <Turbulence>, and Blue could feel the wind willing them to the epicenter where Scirocco lay in wait. But Scirocco was forced to divert all her attention to the bullets raining down on her. Though she used <Turbulence> in conjunction with shielding her body with her greatsword, bullets still got through her flimsy defenses and chipped at her health. 

Lapis fired until she used all her ammo, and the moment she did, Scirocco rushed towards her, brandishing her sword. This time, Lapis was ready. Unlike before, Lapis had applied power to her thrusters beforehand, and now, they evaded Scirocco with far less sluggishness. As Violet let loose a ferocious upwards slash, Lapis deployed <Parachute> and slipped past Scirocco, firing a salvo of <Gatling Gun> before their respective momentums carried Lapis and Blue beyond the radius of <Turbulence>.

Blue exclaimed in glee as they were finally freed from the shackles of wind Scirocco had placed on them. The whir of their thrusters drowned out the wind as they streaked through the air like a bolt of black lightning.

Lapis grinned. “Let’s not experience that <Turbulence> ever again.” Blue agreed wholeheartedly: fighting at mid-range suited her best anyways. Lapis launched into a barrel roll to survey her surroundings and get a sense of the distance between her and Scirocco. 

They both realized the same thing at the same time. 

“Blue, aren’t you supposed to be the fairy of flight?”
“...I am the fairy of flight.” 
“Aren’t you supposed to be the master of the skies, unparalleled in speed and agility?”
“...I am.”

“Really?” Lapis took one more look behind her to confirm what she saw. “You sure you aren’t the dodo of flight? Because how are they catching up to us right now?”

“Shut up! How am I supposed to know!”

But Blue’s exasperated cry didn’t affect the fairy of wind that was rapidly bearing down on them. Lapis and Blue were flying at top speed, multiple times faster than any normal fairy. And somehow, Scirocco was travelling a few times faster than that. The outer edge of <Turbulence> overtook them first, and then a second later, Scirocco’s greatsword rushed past them, narrowly missing Lapis’ wing thruster. The streak of gray careened into the distance, overshooting them. 

And then, as Lapis and Blue watched, one of the dark gray discs surrounding Scirocco contorted furiously. It stopped funneling wind and began to compress, as if squeezing all its contents into a single point. The wind around it howled furiously in protest. 

From within that point, a towering tornado shot out, straight at Scirocco. Only, instead of sucking things in, the column of wind propelled her straight at Lapis. There was the sound of a thunderclap. It was a sonic boom. 

Scirocco’s only offensive option was her greatsword. But what she severely lacked in range, she made up for with sheer speed. The propulsion she received from <Jetstream> allowed her to surpass even the speed of sound. Now, as the two fairies zigzagged through the afternoon skies, a series of booms split the air one after another, startling the seabirds that nestled on the rocky cliffs of the valley. 

At Scirocco’s speed, it was impossible for Lapis to strafe her target with <Gatling Gun> for meaningful damage: though she could still chip away at Scirocco’s health with good aim, she couldn’t consistently land her shots. So instead, Lapis relied on her homing <Missiles> to threaten Scirocco instead. But even this couldn’t slow down the fairy of wind. Scirocco could easily reduce them to harmless explosions with a combination of <Turbulence> and her greatsword. Lapis’ many rounds of ammo couldn’t pause the game of cat-and-mouse in the airspace over the valley.

But despite Lapis’ disadvantages, Scirocco was unable to catch up to her. Lapis and Blue pitched up as they conducted yet another well-timed evasive maneuver, nearly instantaneously changing direction and climbing high above the clouds. Through their radar they saw Scirocco overshoot their position once more and have to use <Jetstream> to correct her trajectory. “Blue, I will admit that in terms of agility, you are unparalleled!”

Blue was caught off guard by the compliment. She waited, but Lapis didn’t expand further. “Is there a punchline?” Blue asked cautiously. 

“Nope! The main character sends you her regards.” She looked down towards the ocean. Scirocco had chased them up into the clouds and was quickly gaining on them. “Just as I shall send that fairy their regards soon enough.” 

They climbed higher and higher. Now, in front of them was a completely different world — one they had only seen once in their two months together. It was during their first full day together, when Lapis had first flown with Blue. Beyond them was an endless indigo, dotted by valleys of white cotton candy. It was as if someone had taken a glimpse of the valley a dozen miles below them and decided to replicate it in this alternate world. 

In this surreal world, Lapis began laughing. Blue didn’t associate anything good with that laugh. But it was weird. Because though she didn’t associate anything good with it, she trusted it. 

“Blue, you ready?” 
“Of course!”
“Then on the count of 3.” 

Below them, a layer of cloud broke apart and geysered upwards. Scirocco joined them in the exclusive world. The remnants of the momentum she received from <Jetstream> transformed her into a grey comet, shedding pieces of cloud as she aimed straight at the heart of Lapis and Blue.

“1. 2. 3.”

“Full power!” Lapis and Blue said in unison. 

Like a swimmer diving into a pool, Lapis elegantly turned head over feet, applying just enough power to her thrusters to dodge Scirocco’s attack. Lapis and Blue were now oriented straight down into the clouds. They took one more look at the world before them. And then, it all became a blur. 
 
They shot down through the stratosphere, blue flames streaming from Blue’s wing turbines and announcing the main character’s descent to earth. Blue felt the wind fight against her, resist her, and finally mold itself into her form. Meanwhile, Lapis grinned. “So Blue, you finally admit I’m the main character? Since you were willing to say ‘Full Power’ with me.”

“This and that are completely different things! And I was just caught in the moment! I’m not ever doing it again!”

The barren valley came into view. At first, it was just a dot amidst the field of blue at first, but as they blitzed towards it, it grew until it covered their entire visor. Lapis looked back towards where they had come from. Scirocco had followed them down as well, and now the fairy of wind was only a kilometer above the valley. 

“As expected.”

Lapis’ own altitude rapidly decreased. A mere second before she slammed into the edge of the valley, she pulled out of the dive and flew parallel to the ground, threading through the trees on the cliffs.

Violet couldn’t change directions nearly as quickly. From the moment she realized that Lapis was aiming for the island, she had used both of the <Jetstreams> she had stored within her discs to slow down and cancel her descent. Even so, she had to use one more <Jetstream> now. Her tornado scraped the desolate landscape, carving up chunks of long-infertile soil, as she flew mere meters above the valley bottom. Violet looked down at the ground to make sure she was maintaining altitude before looking back up.

The tall, rocky cliffs that marked the edge of the valley obstructed her view. 

Scirocco’s propulsion system (which didn’t factor in <Jetstream>) was the same as any other normal fairy. She had no reverse thrust to slow herself down, and though she instantly applied full throttle upwards, Scirocco wasn’t responsive enough to climb out of the valley. <Jetstream> was on cooldown. 

“Ahh, that’s unfair! Why is this dumb island here?” Violet’s gripe was to herself, though Minji heard her through her communication lines. Despite her words, Violet didn’t seem worried as she flew straight towards the cliffs. Just before she was about to impact it, she hoisted her greatsword over her head. With one diagonal swing, she reduced the portion of cliff in front of her to rubble. 

As uprooted trees and chunks of rocks rained down around her, Violet glanced at the displays on her visor. Her health bar had been repeatedly chipped down and her radar was filled with faulty readings from the debris falling down on her. But she still had the advantage. She still had slightly more health than Lapis and Blue, and <Jetstream> had almost reloaded.

A piece of rubble that had been obscuring her view fell away. Something in the corner of her eye caught her attention. Or perhaps, it was more accurate to say it was a colour. 

It was a blue as vivid as the sky. 

“If you are the wind, then we are the world’s mastery over that wind.”

Blue light surged through both of Lapis’ arms. She pointed them straight at Scirocco’s exposed crest. Violet’s greatsword, which she had just swung, was out of position; she had no time to react.

Lapis visualized the two triggers in her mind. She pulled both of them.

“Azul Void: Takeoff!” 

…

…

In Base 33, Minji sat up straighter as a blaze of light filled her vision. She calmly spoke through her communication line. 

“Scirocco. Escape immediately.”

“Understood.” Violet’s voice was perhaps surprisingly level, given her situation and personality. But first and foremost, she was a soldier of the army. Violet simultaneously took in Blue’s location, her bearings, and her health — she was substantially below the half-health limit Minji had imposed on her and had no room to argue against escaping. Using the debris as a smokescreen, she flew back towards the center of the valley and began charging up <Jetstream>. It would take 5 seconds to fully charge. That would propel her far away from the valley. 

The dark gray disc behind her began funneling air greedily, as if devouring it. It compressed into a single point. But just before the tornado could form, the cliff face Violet was hiding behind crumbled. A streak of black snaked past the rubble and rocketed straight towards her, neatly avoiding all the obstacles in her path. Lapis grinned as she placed herself in the path of <Jetstream>.

“Give me a ride!” 

A single tornado formed at the edge of the valley.  

~

The island was riddled with craters, remnants from when it was destroyed by the elves and vampires. In a crater that was far newer than the ones around her, Scirocco lay in the shade with her eyes half-open. There shouldn’t have been any cover on the island to provide that shade, but right now, a figure was standing in front of her, blocking the sunlight. Lapis pointed her right arm at Scirocco’s crest. Its stormy gray light was exceedingly faint. Right now, Scirocco probably could only take as much damage as a regular human.

“Did you predict that I’d do that?” Lapis spoke. Violet heard her voice normally and not in her head. It was a bit muffled by their mecha suits, but Violet could tell it was from a girl not much older than her. She replied bitterly: “Well, it clearly didn’t work, so shut up.”

Violet had predicted Lapis would try to do that. She knew if she had given Lapis a ride with her, there’d be no escape — she’d have brought her enemy along her flight. So instead, just before <Jetstream> activated, Violet had adjusted its aim in another direction, one which affected her but not Lapis. 

Even so, Lapis had still gotten on <Jetstream>. And then she had forced Violet into the ground with her thrusters, explaining the current situation. 

The truth was, even Violet didn’t know why her plan didn’t work. The only explanation was that Lapis and Blue moved even faster than <Jetstream> activated and obstructed its path once more before the tornado could reach her. But Lapis hadn’t known where Violet altered <Jetstream> to aim at — she had to react and make that decision on the fly. That seemed superhuman. 

Alternately, it was just dumb luck — Violet chose to believe that explanation. Now, she scowled at the black mecha suit standing over her. Violet could clearly see the elf’s long flaxen hair as she spoke: “I’m Lapis, commander of <Shadow>. What’s your name?”

“...It’s Violet.”

“Violet.” Lapis repeated. “That’s a nice name.” Blue light surged into her missile launcher, far more than enough to reduce Scirocco’s health to zero. Violet glared defiantly at her. But she was helpless to stop her attack. 

“I won’t forget you while my heart still beats.”

Silence. And then, Lapis broke into a grin. “Nah, just kidding. But I’ve always wanted to say that!” As the light faded from her missile launcher, which she had left unfired, Lapis turned around and prepared for takeoff. 

“See you on the battlefield…” She glanced back at the dumbfounded Violet and smirked.

“...Purple.” 

~

“G’evening, Lazurin!”

Minji and Tanner were the first people to greet Lapis when she turned on the radio. Lapis returned the greeting. In the background, she could hear some sort of commotion. Minji turned to look at the source of the clamor before letting out a small sigh. “Akito and Violet…aren’t here yet.”

Tanner grinned at Minji’s sigh. “It’s pretty funny though!” Minji laughed. “Well, yeah.”

“What is?”

As Tanner told her, a door in Base 33 opened, and Violet burst out of her room with Akito trailing behind her. “Tanner! Minji! Don’t you dare tell her!” Tanner looked at her with his goofy grin. “Too late! It’s fine, right? Since you’re okay?” Minji nodded, one of the few times she agreed with Tanner when he said things were ‘fine’.

“No, it’s not! And I’m not okay!” Violet ranted. 

“How dare that bitch just leave me there instead of killing me! Am I not a big enough threat to get rid of? I was winning without that stupid valley though! And she actually has the guts to mock me with that farce of asking for my name? I’m going to pay her a million times over next time! Even worse, she asked for my name at the end! Only to call me Purple! Fucking Purple! That can’t be something you come up with on the fly, right? I — Hey, Lazu, stop laughing! I can hear you! Seriously, it’s not that funny!”

~

Earlier that night, as they were walking together to Blue’s room, Blue had asked Lapis: “Why’d you spare the fairy? Wasn’t our promise just to spare the pilot?” In response, Lapis had ruffled Blue’s hair, ignoring the fairy’s futile attempts to swat away her hand. After a long moment of thought, she replied: “Who knows? But she did have a nice name.”

Blue stared at her in confusion. Lapis took off her sailor cap and smushed Blue with it. As Blue exclaimed in protest, Lapis spoke with her head held high: “Let’s work hard to make sure we don’t regret it.”

“But, it’s interesting!” She switched to a different tangent. “So the humans invaded Oni Island?” After their fight with Scirocco, they had flown straight to Oni Island. Evie was already there. But the oni were nowhere to be seen in their usual settlement. In their place was a large fairy force, more than ten percent of the human army. 

“I guess the script has reached Rising Action!”

~

“Come in.”

Akito entered the first door to the right of Base 33. This was the first time he was in Minji’s room. All around him were shelves upon shelves of folders and work materials. In the corner was a small bed that was neatly tucked in — it seemed as though it hadn’t been slept in for a long time. Minji sat by a table neatly covered by stacks of papers, facing him.

“D-did you need me for anything?” Akito asked, avoiding eye contact with Minji. He still didn’t feel comfortable around her, even though Violet had bluntly told him to hurry up and get used to it. “Just to talk. How has your first two months been?” Akito tried to read deeper into her words to see if he had done something wrong, but he came up empty. He just nodded in response. 

They made small talk about Akito’s experiences and life until a collection of things on a shelf caught Akito’s eyes. They were a series of lenses, prisms and mirrors, much like the ones Tanner had given him for his telescope. They were the only adornments in what was otherwise a completely work-oriented room. Minji caught him glancing at them. The corners of her mouth lifted ever so slightly. “They’re not mine,” she said.

‘O-oh, uh, sorry.” Embarrassed that he was caught looking, Akito instinctively apologized. Minji didn’t seem to mind though. She got up and took one of the lenses from the shelf, gazing at the rays of light trapped within it.

“Apart from being commander, my work has to do with figuring out what the fairies are.” Minji began. Though Akito was surprised by her unexpected topic of conversation, he stayed silent as Minji continued. “I guess apart from the fairy ambassador Eternity, humans have never met another fairy. But judging from these cores alone, it feels strange to call fairies ‘the fifth race’. Their powers don’t seem natural.” 

This was something Akito had thought of throughout his time at Base 33. The cores the human army used to fight were touted as carbon copies of the actual fairies’ abilities to transform into a mecha suit. If that was true, then the fairy powers and appearances seemed arbitrarily decided, as if someone else had decided what they were supposed to do. And besides, Chiaros had a strangely artificial sense to him. Akito couldn’t quite put it in words, but he seemed a bit like a hologram. He ventured to voice a hypothesis he had been thinking for a while now. “...Could they be ancient technology then?” 

Minji nodded, expecting Akito to say that. “I agree.” She placed the prism back down on the shelf and turned to him. “But in that case, what were they created for?” Realizing it wasn’t a rhetorical question, Akito answered to the best of his abilities. “As sentient, intelligent weapons to defend against something back then?” 

“That is the logical answer,” Minji conceded. “But it’s not what I believe.”

“I believe fairies are containers to preserve the souls of ancient humans.”

…What? Akito tried to understand what Minji was saying. “So…fairies are reincarnations of ancient humans?” Minji stared at him with an unclear expression before letting out a small smile. “That’s an interesting way to put it.”

A whirlwind of questions entered Akito’s mind. He decided to ask the one least directly related to Minji’s work, hoping he’d get an answer. “Why are you telling me this?”

“There’s no harm in doing so. That is just what I believe from my research, and I could be wrong.” Minji admitted. “As for why I’m telling you specifically…” 

“You’re the only person who has an actual fairy instead of a replica core. And apart from you, no soldier — not even in the early days of the war — was chosen personally by Eternity, the ambassador of the fairies. Furthermore, even though the war has stabilized, he ordered for you to be deployed immediately without training.”

“I’m not sure why, but you seem to be special.”

Akito mulled over her words. Now he knew his circumstances were extraordinary. But he didn’t know what to make of that. As silence began to settle in, Minji sat back in her chair. “Though I did say there’s no harm in telling you, that’s because I can trust you to keep secrets. Please don’t share what I told you with anyone.” 

Akito nodded. By her tone, it was evident that her words were meant to end the conversation. He bowed once before turning to leave.

“Oh, one more thing.”

As Akito turned around at the doorway, Minji held up a stack of papers in the corner of her table. Akito recognized it as one of his notebooks. He vaguely remembered that Violet had taken it at some point. She had never given it back. Now, Minji let out a small smile.

“You’re a great storyteller. Keep it up.”

~~ The Advent of Summer ~~
“Uhh, 39 kilometers, 190 degrees.”

Lapis and Blue were eating breakfast together. It had been a week since their fight against Scirocco and surveillance of Oni Island. Nothing unusual had happened since then. Even this radio message seemed to be an ordinary announcement of a skirmish, with the exception of a discrepancy that Blue picked up on. “Don’t they normally start with the number of fairies?” 

Lapis nodded. “Yeah, and that’s way too far west for anything normal.” The quiet noise of radio static filled the air for a moment as the Nightjar pilot stayed silent. Finally, they spoke. “It seems to be a large group of oni? Large enough to be nearly their entire tribe, I think. Commander, what should we do?”

“Lapis here.” A pause as Lapis’ finger hovered over the radio, thinking. 

“Continue monitoring them. We’ll be there in an hour and a half.”

…

…

Though it would only take Blue and Lapis twenty minutes to reach the location, Lapis wanted to head there with a larger task force. Vampires, despite their excellent physical strength, were far slower than the Nightjars (and even slower than the vast majority of fairies), and so Lapis and the elves matched their slow pace. Even so, they arrived in only an hour. It also helped that the oni had continued moving eastwards, towards them. 

Unlike the rest of the races, the oni lacked any means of flight. Though their physical capabilities exceeded those of the vampires on land, the only way for them to hop between islands was by swimming. They were able to swim for hours on end, but even so, it was an extremely slow and vulnerable method of transportation; as such, they always stuck to themselves and never left Oni Island. 

“Then why’d they come all the way here?” Blue piped up after Lapis explained all this to her. Lapis shrugged as she preceded the group of Nightjars and vampires, descending down to a strip of sand so small it could barely be called a sandbar, let alone an island. Four hundred human-like beings watched her on the crowded sandbar. Lapis stepped forward and transformed out of mech form, though she kept Blue within her mind. While in Lapis’ mind, Blue shared her senses, and now, she watched the oni through Lapis’ eyes. Were it not for their mossy green hair, in human form, the oni looked just like any other regular human. 

“That was fast.” One of the oni smiled at Lapis. His tone was cordial, but there was something in his smile that suggested he was hiding a bitter snarl. Lapis smiled back, unfazed. “We like to be a bit early for our guests. Is there anything we can help you with?”

The oni murmured to one another, though it seemed like they had already come to an agreement on what to say. Finally, one of them looked Lapis in the eye.

“We’d like to make an alliance for the war.” 

Silence. And then, the elves and vampires behind Lapis erupted in a loud clamor. Lapis motioned for them to stay quiet. “Why are you asking this?” She asked the oni crowd.

“Just over a week ago, we were attacked by the humans.” Another oni responded. Now that Blue looked closely, she could see that the vast majority of the oni had scars of some sort. Given that they had excellent regeneration, Blue could have only imagined the injuries they had actually suffered if those scars remained after a week. “There was no way for us to fight back, and we were driven off Oni Island.”

Lapis frowned slightly. That did match with the information they knew, but even still, it didn’t make sense. “Assuming that’s the truth, why would the humans do that? They’ve just made an enemy out of another race, and —”

“Do you think we know? All we know is that we were driven off what belonged to us for no reason. Though,” he added, his voice suddenly taking on a dark tone, “I suppose you wouldn’t know how that feels, elf.”

Behind Lapis, a few of the vampires transformed into their vampiric form. Lapis waved them off as the oni cleared his throat. His cordial tone clearly belied his words. “We don’t like you. Don’t think otherwise for a second. But right now, we need supplies, we want revenge, and the enemy of an enemy is our friend. So —”

Lapis cut him off with a polite smile. “We’re not interested in an alliance for the time being. We’ll provide as much supplies as we can spare, but we will not ask for your help in this war.”

The oni all stared at her. Evidently, they weren’t expecting that. They began murmuring uncertainly to one another. Until finally: “We can’t trust an offer like that. You have nothing to gain from it.” 

“It’s the best I can do,” Lapis replied coolly. A tense silence. And then, she spoke inwardly to Blue. “That sounded pretty cool, Blue, didn’t it?”

“Lapis!” Blue yelled at her in exasperation. All the while, the oni huddled around and muttered to one another. It seemed unlike the elves and vampires, they didn’t have a clear leader. One of them broke from the crowd to address Lapis. “Though we’ve remained neutral, we’ve been following the war to some extent. You’re in a stalemate now, right? We could easily help you kill off the humans and win the war.”

“For us, winning the war is different from what you believe. Eliminating all humans isn’t a win, nor is destroying the five complexes.” Lapis let out a dazzling smile as she replied. Blue didn’t have many chances to see her act like a commander — she normally kept Blue out of military meetings, and she and Blue fought solo — but seeing Lapis like this now, Blue could catch a glimpse of why one of the most influential characters in the war was an eighteen year old. Lapis continued:

“For us, winning is eliminating all fairies. Humanity isn’t our enemy. The fairies are. And against them, we will win by ourselves.”

Her declaration was met with uneasy silence from the elves and vampires. But neither they nor the oni spoke. Until, one of the oni closed their eyes. “We’re not interested in bowing to the likes of you, but we will accept your offer. Feel free to ask us for assistance at any time.”

~

As they were flying back to Complex Alpha, Blue spoke up. “Why didn’t you accept the alliance? If you’re willing to offer supplies, then why didn’t you just accept their help?”

Lapis grinned. “The level of your questions has come so far from ‘Main character? Who’’!”

“Shut up! And that’s a valid question!”

Lapis applied power to her front thrusters and pitched up into the clouds, launching into a series of aerial acrobatics. “I don’t trust the oni. After all, they do have a valid reason to hate us.” This was news to Blue. “Why?” She asked curiously. 

“This was before I was born, but Complex Alpha hasn’t always been ours. It was the oni’s until twenty years ago, when the elves invaded and drove them out with the help of the vampires. That was the beginning of our alliance with the vampires, and the start of the oni’s hostility with us.”

Blue remembered something she had recalled back when she had first met Lapis on Oni Island — that the oni had a deep hatred for the elves. “So that’s why,” she muttered.

(Coincidentally, the second thing Blue had remembered back on Oni Island was their cultlike obsession for the fairies. That had been borne within the oni because of their time living in Complex Alpha, after they had found some documents about the fairies from a civilization long past. Though, only the oni themselves knew this.)

Lapis continued, concern creasing the edges of her voice. “But no matter how I think about it, it doesn’t make sense. If what the oni are saying is true, then of course it would make sense why they are joining the war. And I guess the oni are hardy enough to resist an assault by the fairies, especially since the humans wouldn’t want to alert us with their attack. But,” Lapis sighed, “I just don’t see why the humans would take over Oni Island in the first place! It is closer to us than the mainland, and it does mean they can attack from another direction, but is that worth making an extra enemy over?”

Blue stayed silent, thinking about Lapis’ words as the commander of the army explained her train of thought. 

~

It was a typical lazy morning at Base 33. Akito was scribbling thoughts in his notebook. He didn't know what the actual writing process of a writer should be, but he preferred to jot down random snippets of the world in his head before actually writing.

“Akito…Akito!”

“Akito, take a look!”

Rubio…I’m selfish…A promise…

Once I finish this part, I can finally show Lazu, but it still feels wrong…

Violet's voice dragged him from his thoughts, and he let go reluctantly. Though, that reluctance immediately disappeared when he looked at the stacks of paper Violet was holding up in his face. “No way…are these the illustrations?”

For over a month now, Violet had been working on and off on the drawings for Akito’s story. Akito hadn't really known what to expect — she had done it on her own initiative, and he was just incredibly grateful to Violet for trying. Now, he stayed silent as Violet rambled proudly. “That was so hard! You didn't give me any good material to work with, since your illustrations were bad and your descriptions were really vague. And every time I asked you about their characterization, you'd just respond with ‘I don't know —”

“Violet, you're amazing! You're actually amazing!”

“Huh?”

Akito turned to her and grinned with shining eyes. “These look so professional! And they're, like, almost exactly what I envisioned! No, it's even better than that! You're seriously incredible!”

Violet seemed taken aback by Akito’s response. It was the loudest she had ever heard him speak. “Akito, you’re acting weird. Are you being possessed?”

“Of course not!” Akito began shuffling through all of Violet’s illustrations. A large majority of them were character portraits, but she had also done multiple full-page sketches of fight scenes. Now, he pointed out all the details to Violet. “Right here, the invisible hand for Return! And here, if you look close enough, you can see where she drops her first dagger!”

“Why are you explaining all this when I drew it?” Violet pointed out bluntly. Akito, too focused on the pages of pencil sketches in front of him, didn’t catch that she also had a grin on her face, mirroring his. The two began a lengthy discussion on each illustration, with Akito stunned into a shower of compliments every time he uncovered a page.

The next time Akito looked up at the clock, an hour had passed. He could have sworn it had only been a few minutes since Violet had shown him her drawings. Violet seemed to think the same. “Wow, Tanner should be coming back from patrol by now.”

Akito laughed. “Well, knowing him, he’s chasing an eagle right now. He’ll be an hour late.”

“I’d prefer if that’s not the case.” A new voice joined the conversation. Both of them whirled around. Though neither had heard her unlock her bedroom door, Minji was standing just outside the corridor. The corners of her mouth tilted upwards as she addressed them: “Sorry, you two looked like you were having fun. I didn’t want to interrupt.”

“What are you interrupting?”
“Did you need us for anything?”

Minji nodded in response to the latter question, which was Akito’s. “My commander is coming to the base today.” 

Akito thought back to what he had learned about the human army. The army was composed of squadrons, with each being led by a squadron leader. Due to the peculiarities of the fairy communication system, fairies couldn’t communicate with each other while they were in flight. As such, the squadron leader, despite having a fairy, didn’t participate in combat whereas the rest of the squadron did — instead, they acted as a central hub that stayed on the mainland and passed information to the fighting fairies. That information came from colonels, which were humans that didn’t fight, but oversaw the war in a specific sector of the archipelago. And above them were the three generals of the army, who worked with the ambassador of the fairies, Eternity, to coordinate the war effort. 

“A colonel?” He asked Minji, since she was a squadron leader. But she shook her head. “Higher than that. General Algernon Prischett.” 

“What?” Akito and Violet both exclaimed in unison. It wasn’t the rank that surprised them, but the name. “Algernon Prischett? The richest human in the world?” Violet seemed surprised — even though she had been here longer than Akito, this was also news to her.

Despite the self-sufficient nature of the human complexes, they were still a market economy. Payment was made with small black cards that contained an electronic currency — known as debit cards, though banks or any similar institution were a thing of the past. The debit cards and currency were all relics of the ancient civilization, and though Akito didn’t know the specifics, the currency was governed by a superintelligent artificial intelligence on an island to the northwest of the mainland. 

By what was almost definitely a bug in the system, someone had been given control over that artificial intelligence in the morning. That person was Algernon Prischett, someone who did nothing to deserve to become the richest man in the world but acquired the title anyways. Perhaps it was more accurate not to call him the richest man, but that he controlled money himself. 

Akito hadn’t known he was also a general of the war, though. Ever since he joined the army, he realized that a sizable portion of the war was hidden from the general public. Even now, it was a secret that a fairy had sided with the elves and vampires. Now, Minji spoke. “I thought I’d warn you. Since he’s quite important, please try not to offend him.” She levelled her gaze on Violet. “Especially you, Violet.” 

“Why me?” Violet protested obliviously. Minji let out a breath and turned to Akito. “I’ll be counting on you to stop her. Please don’t let her do anything rash.” 

“Okay.” Akito nodded. Violet looked back and forth between them, clearly confused. 

~

As the hour passed, Minji began standing around restlessly in the living room, then pacing back and forth in a small circle. Violet noticed. “Is Algernon that scary?” 

“Well, he is an interesting person, but…” Minji trailed off, and Akito guessed the real reason she was restless — Tanner still hadn’t come back. 

The main entrance opened. Minji quickly reacted and strode briskly to the doorway. “Tanner, you —” 

But though the person at the doorway was a man around the same age as Tanner, it wasn’t him. He was far better dressed than Tanner could have ever been, and exuded an air of singular importance. As for his appearance, Akito tried to come up with an apt phrase — describing people was definitely not his strong suit. 

So hot a straight man could cry, and a gay man…

No, no, no, no, that is terrible on all levels. Akito waved off his thoughts with red embarrassment, and Violet shot him a curious look. Though, the stranger at the doorway was definitely attractive. 

Minji’s face fell the moment she saw him — a rare departure from her usual calm demeanor. “Oh, it’s you, Algernon.” She said flatly, clearly rather wishing it was Tanner who had come back before Algernon arrived. “I’m incredibly glad to see you too, Minji.” Algernon laughed. He glanced at the interior of the base, his eyes passing over Akito and Violet. As he sat himself next to the kitchen counter, they stood up and introduced themselves. 

“Hi, I’m Akit —”

“Don’t bother. I don’t need to learn names from the likes of you two.” Algernon waved his hand churlishly at them, not even bothering to look in their direction. Akito was taken aback. He instantly shut up, though he was unsure when he had made such a bad impression on Algernon. Violet, meanwhile, raised her voice. “And what the fuck — hey!”

Akito kicked her in the shin, and she whirled on him. “Why are you kicking me? How is that my fault?”

“Minji said not to offend him!” Akito motioned for her to lower her voice, and they exchanged angry whispers. All the while, Algernon ignored them as if they didn’t exist and took out a wooden toy from the depths of his coat pocket. Akito caught a glimpse of a gun — one of the only ones they had on the mainland, pilfered from the elves. Algernon began arranging the wooden toy, separating it into its constituents and stacking it into a tall tower. 

As Violet sat down in a huff, muttering grumpily to herself, Minji poured him a cup of tea from the kitchen and passed it to her guest. “What brings you here, Algernon?”  

“Two things. I wanted to check up on your work, and…”

“What work?” Violet interjected, ignoring Akito’s desperate attempts to get her to shut up. Algernon stacked yet another wooden block on his tower in tedium. “Minji, this base has gotten some pests recently, hasn’t it?” 

“Did you just call me a pest?” Violet leapt to her feet, and it took all of Akito’s physical strength to pull her back down towards the table. He whispered to her, “I know he’s being insulting, but seriously, he’s not only the general of the army but also the human with the most influence in the archipelago! Just stay quiet and pretend he doesn’t exist!” 

Hearing this, Violet sat back down and muttered, in a voice loud enough for anyone to hear, "I swear I’ll punch him if he ever gets in range..” 

“Hey!” Akito kicked her again. He looked up, expecting the worst, and stared straight at Algernon’s stony blue eyes. Algernon stopped arranging his wooden blocks and got up from his spot by the counter. His footsteps made no sound as he sauntered casually over to their table. Akito began to apologize on Violet’s behalf. “S-sorry! She didn’t mean —”

“Shut up, vermin.”

Violet immediately jumped to her feet, and Akito did too, trying to hold her down. This time, his whisper was more of a hiss in her ear. “Wait, Violet, just —”

“Don’t stop me, Akito.” She shook off his arm and stood squarely in front of Algernon. The general of the army towered over her, staring down at her impassively. Until, his lips curled into a cruel smile. “3 cents.” Violet reared her arm back, and Algernon simply scoffed. “One cent to bribe that rat over there,” he motioned to Akito, “one cent to bribe the fairy ambassador to break you up with Scirocco, and one cent to bribe the cleanup clue.”

Violet brought her fist forward, straight at Algernon’s face. He didn’t flinch. His features, which seemed like those of a god, contorted in a wicked smirk. “That’s all it’ll take to get you out of the army and dead in a ditch.”

Algernon laughed as Violet’s fist froze just in front of his face. “I’m in range. Now what?”

Before Akito and Minji could react, Violet drew her left arm back and unleashed a sucker punch straight into Algernon’s gut, powerful enough to rattle the wooden blocks on the kitchen counter. She didn’t even spare a glance at Algernon as he doubled over on the floor, instead flicking her left hand about as if it had touched something terrible. “Ughh, I need to wash my hands now. I’m going to the washroom.” It didn’t seem like she was joking — she began walking nonchalantly to the washroom.

“Heh.” Algernon’s voice, from behind her. “What’s your name?”

“It’s Violet.”

As Algernon stood back upright, about to say something, Violet paused. Her back was still turned on the general of the army. “If it’s not a heartfelt apology, I’m not interested.” Algernon simply smiled and walked towards her, reaching for something within the depths of his coat. His gaze was focused on Violet. 

Minji, meanwhile, wasn’t looking at either of them. Her attention was directed to her side, straight at Akito. That was why unlike Algernon, she saw Akito staring straight at him. 
  
Don’t you dare treat her like someone to harm. Don’t you dare hurt her. Don’t you dare.

The glint in his eyes was the same one Minji saw when he had told her that Lazu wasn’t an enemy. As Algernon leaned closer to Violet, Akito muttered something so low only Minji, who was actively trying to listen, could hear.

“Chiaros.” 

The right side of his body began armouring itself in metal the colour of amber, and glimmers of a bow the shape of a clock appeared in his right arm.

Truthfully, one of the reasons Minji accepted the radio was because of that glint in his eyes. Akito himself wasn’t aware of what he looked like then. But to the people who saw it, even if they weren’t familiar with Akito’s typical timid personality, they all thought one thing.

“Surely, someone with that stare must be the main character of a fairytale.”

But Algernon didn’t see it. Just as Akito raised his right arm straight at Algernon, he bowed deeply to Violet. “Sorry, Violet. Please accept my apology.” And then, he winked, pulling out not the gun he kept concealed, but a debit card. “And if you don't think my heartfelt apology is worth accepting, maybe you’ll think this else is?” 

Violet turned back to him, a bit surprised at his change in demeanor, and then grinned. “Don’t mind if I do,” she said, ignoring that Algernon had blatantly done it in jest. She swiped the card from him and glanced at it excitedly like a child. Though Algernon had meant it as a joke, he shrugged and walked back to his chair. The money in the debit card wasn’t a big deal to him. 

Akito silently reverted his Chiaros transformation and relaxed back in his chair. Minji was the only one who even realized he had transformed. 

As Violet drooled over her unexpectedly acquired riches, Algernon turned to Minji. “Did you expect Violet to earn my respect?”

The hints of a smile appeared on Minji’s face. “Perhaps.” She issued a silent apology to Akito as she spoke — she had been testing him. Though he hadn’t passed Algernon’s test, he had passed hers. “But anyways,” she continued, “what was your second reason for visiting us?”

“I came to send you off to battle. Nothing raises morale like hearing some posh rich guy wish you luck in war while he stays as far away from the front lines as possible, right?” Though Minji didn't seem surprised, Akito and Violet both perked up at this. “S-so, um we’re being d-deployed to actual combat?” Akito asked Algernon.

“I thought I told you to shut up.”

“Hey!” Violet began to protest, but Minji interceded. “Sorry, Akito, but,” she turned to Violet, “Don’t bother trying to fix him. Algernon, just answer the question.”

Algernon grinned at Minji. “Am I the crazy ex in this case? Anyways,” he made eye contact with Violet, ignoring Akito, and responded: “Yes, Base 33 is being deployed. Now that we’ve reached our objective, we can finally mobilize the western front. Report to the headquarters in Complex Zeta the night of the 20th. We’ll be launching an all-out initiative on the first day of summer —”

“What objective?” Violet interrupted rudely, ignoring Akito’s pointed glance. “And what will our attack change? I thought we were in a stalemate with the enemy?”

Algernon grinned — a smile, which despite his unwarranted abrasiveness, contained surprising character. “I can’t answer the first question, but for the second, this war should be in its final stage. He paused for a moment, thinking how to best continue, before asking: “Do you know how the elf/vampire army operates?” Violet and Akito glanced at each other, before simultaneously shaking their heads.”

“Unlike the human army, <Shadow> doesn’t have squadrons or ranks in the military like the humans do. They have one person higher up than everyone else, who is not only the leader of the military, but also their strategist and one of their strongest fighters. I guess you could call them their ‘supreme commander’. That system is not necessarily a bad thing, but it does make it clear where we should target.”

Algernon reached over towards his tower of wooden blocks. With one precise chop of his hand, he struck the bottom block of the tower and snatched it in his hand. The rest of the tower wobbled. And then, as it crumbled into a heap of wood, he spoke:

“If you isolate the linchpin from the rest of the army, it will collapse.”

“What do you…” Violet began to interrupt, but Akito nudged her foot hard to silence her. Algernon finished his explanation uninterrupted, that smile still shaping his defined features.

“Either way, we’re a lot closer to victory than it seems.”

Minji seemed posed to say something, but just then, the door opened and Tanner waltzed in. “I’m back, Minji!” He looked around, seeing an extra face beyond the usual three. “Algie, you’re here!”

Violet laughed brashly at Algernon’s nickname, ignoring Akito’s leg kicks and trepidation. Algernon just smiled. “Good to see you, Tanner.” 

“Did I miss any — ow!”

Before he could finish asking his question, Minji ran up to him and silenced him with a flick to the forehead. She glared at him. “You. Are. Late!”

~

June 20th, the day before the summer solstice. Though it wasn’t a holiday for the archipelago, it had been a day long celebrated by Complex Alpha. It was Erin’s birthday.

The grassy meadows in the center of the island had been transformed into a breathtaking setting. Stalls, like the ones you might see in a festival, were set up along the grass, and now all the residents in the complex were gathered around them, chatting about topics far removed from the war. Pink lanterns flew overhead, and small lights hovered above the tall grass as if they were pixies from a fairytale, mirroring the twinkling stars of a vast night sky. 

“WHOAAA! AMAZING!”

In the midst of all of it, Blue exclaimed with unrestrained excitement. Everywhere she glanced was something new — a takoyaki stall, a dessert shop, a carnival game, even a few magic and talent shows. And that was only the things in her line of sight. Beyond this meadow were so many more things to do, so many more places that she could explore every inch of.

 “Where should I go?” She wondered to herself. Of course, it was a rhetorical question.

She went to all of them. 

Now, she was leaving a donut shop. In her hands was a large pack of donuts that had been extra-glazed with honey just for her. As they began filling her belly like water into a bottomless well, she set off once again — she wasn’t done exploring the entire fairgrounds. As she pranced through a field far from the main festivities, flitting from carnival game to carnival game and trying every one of them,  a familiar face caught her eye.

“Happy birthday, Erin!”

The princess of the elves was playing a ring toss game with a large number of the island’s children. Erin grinned at Blue as she ran up, before trying to hide it with an unnaturally stiff expression. “Thanks!” Her eyes scanned the surroundings. “Is Lapis not with you?” Blue shook her head — Lapis had given her free roam to explore — and Erin glared into the distance. “That elf told me ‘Happy birthday, mom’ and ran off.”

In spite of herself, Blue laughed. Erin seemed like she was about to retort, but then her expression softened. “Well, I’ll pay her back later. Have fun exploring. Oh,” Erin added, remembering something, “Have you seen Mitsui or Evie?” 

“Not Evie, but I saw Mitsui a while back.” While Blue had been exploring another one of the outer meadows, she had run into Mitsui walking alone amidst the throng of people. He had seemed noticeably out of place in the crowd; Blue realized that apart from their mornings and weekly excursions, she hadn’t seen him with other people much. They had parted ways after exchanging greetings, and now she told Erin, “I don’t know where he is now, though.” Erin frowned slightly. “I haven’t seen them all day. I wonder where they are.”

“Do you want me to search for them?” 

Erin considered Blue’s offer. “I guess I trust that Mitsui’s fine, but could you check on Evie for me? I’m a bit concerned about her.”

“Why?” 

“Erin let out a wistful smile. “Just a few lies we’ve told in the past.” Blue looked at her curiously, trying to decipher her cryptic answer, before deciding it wasn’t worth thinking about. “Okay, I’ll find her first then!” She pranced away, waving back as Erin called out after her to not be late for the evening dance. 

Though completely by accident, it didn’t take long for Blue to find Evie. A few minutes after she left Erin at the carnival games, a nondescript tent caught Blue’s eyes on the very outskirts of the festival grounds. Without any hesitation, she peeked in. The tent was completely devoid of people, and the only furnishings inside it were a series of portable cabinets. It seemed like a preparation space of sorts. 

“What’s this for?” 

Blue tilted her head in confusion just as she felt the beating of wings behind her. A familiar vampire with ruby eyes burst past her into the tent, quickly glancing around its interior. Her eyes fell on one of the portable cabinets. Before Blue could say anything, Evie hissed at her: “Don’t you dare snitch on me.” The vampire dashed into a cabinet and hid inside it. 

The sound of brisk footsteps came from behind her. “Evening, ma’am. Have you seen Evie?” Blue whirled around. It was Erin’s bodyguard, Tsukuyo. Blue considered saying no…

Obviously not. She didn’t consider that for a second.

As Tsukuyo opened the cabinet and exposed Evie, Blue stuck her tongue out at the vampire. “That’s what you get for calling me overheal!” Evie glared daggers at her before staring down Tsukuyo as the elf approached her. But to Blue’s surprise, though she bared her fangs at Tsukuyo, she didn’t attack her as Tsukuyo coaxed her out of the cabinet. After a while, Evie retracted her fangs and docilely let Tsukuyo pet her as if she were a housecat. 

“So there’s someone other than Lapis that Evie won’t attack,” Blue muttered to herself. She watched on curiously, wondering why. As Tsukuyo ushered Evie out of the tent, the vampire cast another surly look at Blue. “Flying fish, have you seen Mitsui?”

Blue flared the crystals around her, which, under the light, really did look like the wings of a flying fish. “Screw you! I was just about to find him!” 

~

After finding Evie that quickly, Blue expected finding Mitsui to be a piece of cake. But she had retraced her steps through all the meadows, combed the beach she and Erin had played volleyball at, and even checked the grotto with the massive gemstone. Mitsui wasn’t in any of them. And though she normally would have loved getting lost on the island trying to search for him, it was almost time for the dance. She needed to hurry up and find Mitsui. 

There was a place that had been in the back of her mind ever since she tried to find Mitsui. There was no one in the complex as she opened its front entrance and tiptoed down to the second floor. A familiar voice halted her in her tracks the moment she entered the view of the lounge on the second floor. “Blue?”

Mitsui was standing a few feet from her, the surprise evident in his stare. He glanced up at the sky where the stairs where Blue had come down from, but Blue ran towards him, embracing him before he could say something. “Mitsui, why are you here? Evie and Erin are looking for you!”

No answer. The only sound that met Blue’s question was the crashing of waves against the rock. Until finally: “Good. Let them look for me.” 

There was none of the gentle warmth Blue had expected from him. His voice was cold, lifeless, and Blue glanced up sharply at his face. From his one non-eyepatched eye, she saw an emotion she couldn’t quite grasp. Mitsui continued, with that voice Blue had never heard before. “I wonder if they can find me? I am quite invisible.”

“Mitsui?”

Another long silence. And then, the vampire unfolded his jet black wings before wrapping them around himself as he sat down on the cold rock. Mitsui smiled weakly at Blue. “Sorry, it’s nothing. Could you leave me alone?” 

Blue didn’t understand, but she somehow knew not to listen. She sat down slightly behind Mitsui, trying to stay as soundless as possible. The two of them stayed there quietly. There was a window in the lounge, and they gazed out at it together. There was a full moon tonight. It outshone all the other twinkling lights. 

The dance was probably starting now. Though, Blue had no way of knowing that. She wasn’t sure how many minutes had passed until Mitsui spoke again. “It’s not their fault, but sometimes I just don’t want to see them. Especially today, when it’s her birthday.”

“The people’s princess, the strongest fighter, and the main character…they shine so brightly they don’t see the shadows they cast on the rest of us.” 

As Mitsui said those words, he really did seem invisible. “It’s funny how Lapis thinks I’m good at communicating when I’ve never managed to tell them.” He smiled, a fragile smile. “Tell them that I hate them.”

“W-why?”

But Mitsui didn't answer her confusion. Instead, he turned to Blue and smiled weakly. “Thanks, Blue. I’m impressed you found me. I wonder if they can?”

Blue didn’t know what to say. And so, she said what was on her mind at that moment, “I don’t understand what you’re saying. I really don’t, but, well…”

“Isn’t this exactly the sort of moment in which Lapis would appear?” 

“...”

Before Mitsui could say anything, they both heard the door to the second floor open with a bang. Someone leapt down the staircase railing beside them, making another one of her flashy entrances. “What on earth?” Blue exclaimed as Lapis landed, tucking into a graceful somersault that brought her to an elegant curtsy in front of them. “How are you seriously here?” 

“What do you mean ‘seriously’?” Lapis grinned, thinking of something. “Aww, were you just talking about how I’d find you or something?”

“N-no way! Shut up!” 

“Stuttering isn’t your character trait, Blue! Anyways,” She turned to Mitsui, “No clue what you two were talking about, but it’ll have to wait. Erin postponed the dance to search for you. Let’s hurry!”

A gentle laugh. Blue whirled around. It was the Mitsui she was used to. “Sorry, but I don’t feel well tonight. I don’t think I can go. Could you send Erin my condolences after the party? I don’t want to worry her.”

Lapis paused. She studied Mitsui closely, before finally shrugging. “Alright. You’ve worried her and Evie plenty already, though. They’ve spent much of the night searching for you.” Mitsui chuckled again. “Sorry.” 

“Don’t be. Get better soon, okay? And tell us what we can do, if anything.” Lapis flashed a teasing grin. “But you know, it’s bad manners to leave your girlfriend hanging for a dance! At least try to dance with her before the night is over.”

“I haven’t asked her out yet.”

“Then you’re an idiot, because the main character guarantees you’ll succeed. After all, you're an amazing person!”

Mitsui stared at her for a moment, before letting out a soft smile. “I’ll think about it. Have fun at the dance.”

~

The crowd of elves and vampires stopped their preparations, all gasping in wonder as Lapis and Blue performed a low pass over the crowd before flaring straight in the center of the main meadow. Lapis uncorked a triple axel as she transformed out of Blue, sticking the landing with more precision than any gymnast. Besides her, Blue hit the ground with an ungainly thump. They had flown straight from the complex to the meadow to avoid being late for the dance. It seemed they had made it just in time. 

Evie ran up to them, paying no heed to the beautiful kimono she wore. “Did you find that stupid one-eyed Bigfoot?”

“He was in the complex. He said he didn’t feel too well, so he’ll be skipping.” 

Evie, who had looked ready to claw Mitsui to pieces when she heard he was in the complex, frowned. “Is he okay?” Lapis nodded. “Let’s check on him after. But don’t you have something important to do right now? I wonder how you’ll invite them to dance? Maybe ‘Erin, I’ll indulge in all the pet play you want later, so please dance with me?’”

“Who said I wanted to dance with the all-you-can-eat?” Evie retorted, her ruby eyes flashing under her bangs. Apart from the kimono (which had been modified to accommodate her wings), she also had light makeup on that accentuated her natural catlike cuteness. As had been tradition for the past few years, Tsukuyo had tried to make her as cute as possible for Erin’s birthday.

“Your crush’s tsundereness is rubbing off on you.” Lapis grinned as Evie glared daggers at her, torn between her loyalty to Lapis and the urge to swipe at the elf’s face. She chose the middle ground and ran off. Lapis waved at the vampire’s retreating figure with a bright laugh. “Tell us how it goes!” 

(As it turned out, Evie would quickly return to them. She had invited Erin to dance, succeeded, and then ended up unable to resist biting her midway through the dance. She had been chased out by Erin and everyone else. Lapis would shake her head in jest, saying “Don’t you ever learn?”)

Lapis had, of course, taken center stage, and now the crowd formed around Lapis and Blue. The beautiful sound of merry chatter filled the air. Blue turned to Lapis. “Did you really not eavesdrop on me and Mitsui?”

“No. Should I have?” Lapis gave her a curious look, and Blue sighed a bit, thinking to herself that Lapis really hadn’t eavesdropped. With the meddlesome main character, one couldn’t be too sure. Blue started to reply. But something cut herself short. Her mind had been too preoccupied with Mitsui to notice the appearance of the elf besides her. 

Though her pendant was still nestled in its usual place, Lapis wasn’t wearing her cloak, miniskirt, or sailor cap. Instead, a beautiful flowing white dress, almost like that of a wedding gown, melded with her curves. Her long flaxen hair was swept back in a ponytail, exposing her bare shoulders. The pendant nestled on her collarbone mirrored the unfathomably deep blue of her eyes, which shone as if the first rays of an infinite dawn were passing through them. Even amidst the dressed-up elves and vampires behind her, she was from another plane of existence. And then, the elf opened her mouth. “Aww, were you stunned speechless by my beauty? That’s pretty cute!” 

“Shut up!”

A dazzling grin, one that could pierce even the darkest of nights. “It is only natural! After all, the main character is beautiful.” 

“So superficial,” Blue muttered. In response, Lapis shrugged. “Not just external beauty. And besides, everyone has the power to write their own story.”

“What does that mean?” 

But before Lapis could say anything, the pixie-esque lights in the grass began moving. Like a breathtaking swarm of fireflies, they took flight into the starry sky, illuminating the meadow — no, the dance floor — below in a swath of warm colours. Music began playing around them, supplemented by yet another invention from the ancient civilization: loudspeakers with an uniform sound amplitude across a wide area. All around them, elves and vampires paired up, taking each others’ hand. Blue whirled around and around, awestruck. 

Lapis smiled, seeing Blue twirl around like a top. She extended a hand as Blue turned towards her. 

“May I have this dance?” 

Blue stared at Lapis, unable to take her eyes off her. Right now, with this backdrop as her stage, with that outfit, with that expression, one thing was unequivocally certain. 

Lapis was beautiful. 

Blue began to open her mouth, but Lapis interjected before she could: “How was that line? I’ve always wanted to say that!”

“Heyyyyyyyyyy!” 

Lapis laughed, a beautiful, bell-like tinkle. “So may I?” Blue stared at her for a moment before grinning. “I don’t know how to dance though.” She reached for Lapis’ hand…

…Only for Lapis to withdraw it and ruffle her hair before Blue could react. “Then I’ll be sure to tease you all the more!” 

June 20th, the day before the Summer Solstice. Though <Shadow> didn’t know it, that was one of the last days of peace they would have in a long time.

Because the next day, with the advent of summer came the advent of 217 fairies on the horizon of Complex Alpha. It was the most the elves had vampires had seen in a long time, an assault on par with that from the early days of the war.

~

At around the same time that Lapis and Blue were dancing, Akito was pacing in front of the entrance to Base 33. They were departing for Complex Zeta tonight, though neither Algernon nor Minji had really coordinated what time they’d be leaving. Akito was currently the only person at the door. 

In his hands was the radio. They were permitted to bring some of their belongings to Complex Zeta since they’d be staying there for a few weeks to coordinate the war effort.  He had asked Violet if he should bring some of the blueprints, but she had responded that she had already brought the only one they needed. Though he didn’t know what, it seemed that she had chosen their next project. 

“What time is it?” He murmured. A robotic voice answered using telepathy. “It’s 10 in the morning.” Akito glanced out at the sky, which was pitch black were it not for the stars. “Yeah, I don’t think that’s right. Thanks a lot, Chiaros.” No response to Akito’s sarcastic thank you. Over the past few months, Akito had tried out every common phrase he could think of to get Chiaros to respond, but the fairy only ever responded to variants of ‘What time is it’’.

A voice groaned from the couch. “Is it time to go?” Tanner flopped off and crawled over to the front entrance like a slug. He was the exact opposite of being ready to go. His unkempt bedhead (couchhead? Akito thought to himself) obscured his half-lidded eyes, and he was still in his pajamas. Akito smiled at him as he got to his feet like a zombie rising from the grave. “Not yet. But you really should fix your appearance a bit. You look like a zombie.”

“Zombie…that sounds fun,” Tanner murmured to himself, and Akito chuckled — Tanner probably would like being a zombie. As Tanner rubbed the sleep from his eyes, he let out a rare dejected sigh. “Why do we have to fight…Why can’t I just laze around all day….” 

“You know why, Tanner.”

“Ehh, but I don’t like it!” 

Akito thought about Tanner’s words. Truth to be told, he had thought the exact opposite of Tanner. He couldn’t have waited for today to come any sooner. The sooner they were deployed, the sooner they could kill everyone in <Shadow>. And the sooner we can save Lazu…

Unbeknownst to Akito, Tanner had stopped rubbing his eyes and was looking straight at him. Tanner let out a quiet “hmm”. Every once in a rare while, Akito had a captivating, yet scary, look on his face. Tanner had first seen it when Minji was trying to confiscate his radio, and since then, he had seen it a few more times. Now, he patted Akito on the back, and Akito jolted to attention as if broken out of a trance.

“Don’t worry! Let’s have fun!” 

Akito clutched the radio in his hands a bit tighter. “Tanner, you’re probably the only person in the world that can say that while being sent to battle.” 

“Really?” Tanner put his hand to his chin in thought. “But the more fun you have now, the more stories you can tell Lazu when you rescue her!” 

“...”

Akito stared at Tanner for a long moment. And then, Akito smiled. “Sorry, you’re right. Thanks.” 

Half an hour later, the four members of the 33rd squadron departed the base. They would be one of the last squadrons to arrive at Complex Zeta, doing so a few minutes before midnight.
