~~ Selfish ~~


Blue rubbed her eyes lethargically as she made her way to her bedroom doorway. She tried to open the sliding door three times before realizing it was locked, and with a sleepy yawn she fumbled it open. “Sho sweepy…” she mumbled, relying purely on muscle memory to make her way to the lounge on the second floor.

“Good morning, Blue.” 

“Mitsui!” The sleep clouding her mind cleared away when she heard the familiar voice. Blue gratefully accepted the glass of honey water Mitsui had prepared for her. “That hits the spot!”

A gentle laugh. “You’re starting to sound like an old woman.” Blue pouted in jest. “Lapis still treats me like a child though. Anyways,” she grinned, “Let’s play Uno! I need to go fight soon.”

Blue pulled out the deck of cards and passed them over to Mitsui, who began shuffling. There was no trace of the sentiments he had let slip on Erin’s birthday. Ever since that day, he had acted normal to the point where Blue wondered if she had hallucinated the words he had confided to her. 

She had wanted to ask him, but just this once, she didn't let curiosity get the better of her. Now, Mitsui had a peaceful smile on his face as they began placing cards on the lounge table. 

“I won't lose today!”

“I look forward to it. I think you're the same level as me now.”

Though, as much as Blue hated to admit it, neither of them were close to Lapis.

A week had passed since the start of summer. By the time Blue had woken up after Erin’s birthday, it had been a few hours since the vampires first detected the fairies on the horizon. Lapis, despite acting like what Blue believed to be a dubious commander most of the time, had already coordinated the military.

The fairies’ offense was in essence, a simple, brute force assault. At the cost of being unable to communicate with some fairies during battle, the humans had deployed a large majority of their squadron commanders to actual fight (who were normally responsible not for fighting, but for communicating with those on patrol). Furthermore, taking over Oni Island had allowed the humans to attack from the west and north, and so in conjunction with their force coming from the mainland, they attacked all sides of the island. With a few exceptions, they worked alone, having been given their own flight level and sector of airspace so they would not get in the way of each other. 

In response, Lapis had set up a defensive hemisphere twenty kilometers in radius. That hemisphere was the frontline of the battle and marked the boundary between the two armies. She had told Blue a few days ago that the number was for a few reasons — the longest range of a fairy attack was within that distance, and vampire echolocation extended just beyond twenty kilometers. It was her goal to prevent fairies from getting within twenty kilometers of Complex Alpha.

Neither side had deviated from their initial strategies. The humans had tried rotating their fairies to get favourable matchups, but without the ability to coordinate like the elves and vampires, Lapis was quickly able to adjust. They had also tried some more insane things — for instance, they had launched Scirocco using <Jetstream> straight at the aircraft hangar in Complex Alpha in the hopes of destroying it. Lapis and Blue had laughed as they watched her bounce right off: according to Lapis, the hangar was protected by an unbreakable barrier. Apart from chipping away at their forces with Nova of the Stars, which, though only being able to target one opponent at a time, was essentially a surefire kill, the humans hadn’t made progress in breaking through Lapis’ defence.

Now, as Blue triumphantly proclaimed “Uno”, she couldn’t help but notice Mitsui’s various scars, still not healed despite his regeneration. Vampires were far slower, bulkier, and larger than anything else in the air, which made them easy targets. The one thing they did have for them was their excellent regeneration and tankiness due to their greatly strengthened body. Lapis was using them as recyclable meat shields, having them rush at the fairies to pressure them backwards before rotating back to the infirmary to be healed and then sending them out again. It probably wasn't a fun role to play. 

Mitsui caught Blue looking and let out a reassuring smile. “The vampires have been doing this since the start of the war. We’re used to it. Also, it’s not like the elves have it any easier” Because the vampires were slow and lacked any range, it was up to the elves alone to get kills. Though the fighter jets were frail and they had a limited number of ammo, their railguns were powerful enough to blast through even Blue’s high survivability parachute (Lapis tried) and fast enough to even give Blue some trouble in evading. Even so, they were far weaker individually than a fairy, and it required quite a bit of skill to survive, let alone defeat an opponent.

The second part of Mitsui’s response caught Blue’s attention. “I've heard Lapis talk about it, but how bad were the early days of the war actually?” 

Mitsui thought for a moment as he dealt out another round of cards. “In terms of our losses, I'd say it was twenty times worse than it is now. The generation of vampires and elves above were nearly wiped out. My parents were killed, as were Erin’s — the previous king and queen of the elves. The commander of the army before Lapis was also killed. It's why so many people on Complex Alpha are children or teenagers like us.”

“...”

Blue found herself lost for words. Finally, she managed to say: “That’s…a lot more people than I expected.”

“Don’t worry, Blue.” A comforting smile. “I don’t think the war will ever be that bad again. Besides, the humans had it far worse. In the first two months they were still adjusting to using their fairies, so they suffered heavy losses. Furthermore, unlike Lapis, the previous commander specifically targeted complexes. There were previously six complexes that humanity lived in, but one was destroyed at the start of the war.”

There were a lot of things Blue was learning today. Things which, she ruefully thought to herself, she should have known. But before the girl could formulate a reply, she vanished from the lounge without a trace, as if she were a ghost. The cards that she was holding collapsed onto the table soundlessly. Mitsui sighed; he was used to it. 

In the aircraft hangar of Complex Alpha, Blue’s aggrieved voice resounded in Lapis’ head. “Hey, at least let me say goodbye to Mitsui before you transform into mech form!”

~

In stark contrast from the daytime, nights in the archipelago passed serenely. Because vampire echolocation far outclassed fairy radar, the human army relied on visibility to attack. Come dusk, the fairies retreated back to Oni Island or the mainland, and both sides were content to leave the day of fighting at that. It was the only time they could do things that weren’t related to the war.

Now, fifteen minutes before ten in the evening, Lapis vaulted onto her bed and turned the knob on the radio. Though she was a bit early, the radio instantly latched on a cheerful voice. “G’evening, Lazurin!” 

“Hey, Tanner.” Lapis grinned. “Did you finally learn to be early for a change?”

“Nope!” Tanner replied, a hint of pride somehow evident in his voice. “Actually, I’m late! I was supposed to go get ice cream ten minutes ago.” The four members of Base 33 were living temporarily in Complex Zeta, hence why they could acquire luxuries such as cold ice cream. Tanner himself said he was looking forward to it, though he didn’t seem too concerned as he shrugged. “Well, it’s fine. Fate will deliver the ice cream one way or another.”

Lapis shook her head disapprovingly, though half in jest. “Try not to disappoint Minji too much, She is your wife.” Tanner grinned in surprise. “Eh? How’d you know?”

“Things of this nature do not elude the main character! Besides,” Lapis added, “Given how much you two flirt, I’d either have to be deaf or Violet to not realize.” Tanner scratched his head lazily. “Do we flirt a lot? I mean, I never see Minji since she’s always working. I think I’ve watched the first episode of One Pi*ce more than I’ve watched her.”

Lapis couldn’t help but laugh at that. “Tanner, that’s so depressing I don’t think I can even tease you about it.” Though to be fair, someone could point out that Lapis didn’t have the right to say anything. After all, the one thing noticeably absent from the main character’s story thus far was romance. Tanner shrugged in response to Lapis. “That just means I should maximize my time with her!”

“Fair enough.” Lapis conceded. She continued on a tangent, eyes suddenly shining. “Tanner! So which was it? Enemies to lovers? Childhood friend? Or perhaps the trope where you start with a fake relationship but it gradually turns into true love?” It took a moment for Tanner to realize Lapis was asking about his relationship with Minji, converted to story tropes. He let out a bright laugh. “That’s impressive, Lazurin!”

“Oh, was I right? Which one?”

Tanner began to reply, but he was interrupted by a flick to the forehead. Minji glared at him, the expression on her face a frown that contained hints of something else. “That’s a secret, Tanner.” Lapis grinned. “Look, they’re flirting!” Minji immediately objected, the slight bit of embarrassment in her impassive voice only being picked up by Tanner.

Behind Minji, Violet and Akito crowded the doorway to their shared room. Violet called out to Tanner as she took off her shoes. “Tanner, where’s the ice cream?” Tanner flashed a smile that seemed far too unapologetic for the situation. “I’ll go get it now — ow!” As Minji flicked Tanner, Akito made his way into the room. “I stopped by to get it already.” He held up four cartons of ice cream. “I figured Tanner would be late.”

Violet dove at the ice cream in Akito’s hand, trying to swipe the chocolate flavour for herself, but Akito kept a firm grip over the cartons. As Violet and Akito began bickering over who deserved which flavour, Lapis laughed. “Is Akito fate in this case?” She asked Tanner.

“Akicchi is!”

…
…

Over the weeks, their meetings had fallen into a regular rhythm. Akito and Violet sat next to the radio, conversing with Lapis while working on their latest project. Minji kept to her work a short distance away, though she listened attentively and didn’t mind being included in the conversation. Tanner did whatever he wanted, which usually meant a mixture of pestering Minji, joining Akito and Violet by the table, or lounging around on the couch watching a TV show. 

Today, Violet broke out a topic of conversation she had been saving for a while. Shortly after she had finished licking the lid of her chocolate carton (Akito, unfortunately, was still pushed over too easily), she announced: “For our next project, we’re building a plane!” 

“Wait, what?” Akito turned to her. Evidently, this was news to him. Violet grinned. “Didn’t you know? There was an entire book dedicated to blueprints for a plane! It seems like it’ll be fun! And doesn’t flying sound cool?”

Neither Lapis nor Akito spoke for a moment. And then, Lapis let out a laugh in spite of herself. “Violet, socially, you never fail to choose the worst possible option. It’s quite impressive!” Akito chuckled as well. “I don’t mind it, but I agree. It is impressive.”

“What? What’s wrong with building a plane” Violet turned to Akito confusedly. “Six years, my dad died in a plane crash while testing the plane in the blueprints. So,” he added a quip to try and lighten the topic, “there’s a chance it’s not airworthy.”

“Well, you don’t know until you try!” Violet replied, completely missing the first part of his response. Meanwhile, Minji muttered to herself, “so those blueprints were your dad’s…” In researching Akito to try and determine what made him special, she had discovered that his father was the legendary inventor — one which had, among other things, pioneered the human army’s radio. It was thanks to him that humanity wasn’t fully reliant on ancient technology, and if not for his death, humans could have progressed far further.

There was a rumour that the plane crash was a shootdown by the elves. Though, there was no way to know — to Minji’s knowledge, no trace of the plane was ever discovered. 

It took Akito a few tries to explain his dad’s death to Violet. Her mouth formed a perfect “o” as she finally understood. “Sorry, I didn’t realize some people don’t have parents.” She apologized bluntly — so bluntly if it were anyone else, Akito would have thought Violet was insulting him. “You know what I mean, right, Lazu?” 

Violet… 

Akito issued a silent plea, and then a kick to the shin that elicited a surprised yelp. Meanwhile, Lapis couldn’t stop laughing. “Sorry, but I don’t. My parents died when I was seven, long before the war began. It was in a plane crash too!” Violet, realizing she had messed up, apologized before quickly continuing. “But isn’t that all the more reason to do this? Let’s actually make the plane fly!”

“I agree. Though, I think it might be unfeasible.”

“Why?” Lapis asked Akito. Flying seemed like the simplest thing in the world. So simple that, for instance, even a certain child could accomplish it. Akito explained: “There are so many aspects for a plane that we have no knowledge in, especially when we don’t understand how any of it works. It’s not like a telescope, where you can figure out the physics easily.”

“Can’t you just have three thrusters on the bottom to provide lift, and then an extra thruster at the back to provide thrust?”

Akito had no clue where Lapis got such an idea, and he quickly shook his head. “First, you'd have no yaw control, so you'd just spin endlessly. And even if you somehow fix that, weight distribution would need to be perfect, and you’d need to change thrust levels at superhuman speeds Besides,” Akito added, “unlike the elves, we can’t access ancient technology, so we don’t have motors powerful enough to even move a plane, let alone get it off the ground. My dad was forced to turn the plane in the blueprints into a glider. I think we’ll have to do the same.”

“Ehh, really?” Tanner spoke up lazily from the couch. “But we have the fairies, right? Why not just attach Scirocco to the back of the plane and use <Jetstream> to propel it?”

“You’re crazy, Tanner.” Lapis, Akito, and Violet spoke in unison. They huddled back together to discuss better options. And then…

“Wait a minute…”
“Why wouldn’t Tanner’s suggestion work?”
“I guess if we don’t use the maximum output…”    

For the rest of the night, they drew sketches, trying to add a tornado onto the back of a wood-and-canvas plane. 

~

The clock read just after midnight. Violet had long since left abruptly in the middle of their brainstorming session without so much as a good night; she was fast asleep. As Akito stacked the sheets of scrap sketches the three had compiled together, Lapis asked him: “Akito, I won’t wait forever. How long until you give me your answer?” As Akito’s head spun in dizzying circles, Lapis continued: “How’d that sound? I’ve always wanted to say that!”

“So you want to be the one who confessed and is being kept waiting?”

Lapis put her finger to her pendant in thought. “I guess not, fair enough. But you know what I mean? When are you done with your book?”

“Ah, um, actually…I finished today. I only have one book left to write in the series, and I guess I can explain the story now…”

Silence. And then, a livid sigh. “Akito, you’re so dense I’ll give you the title of main character. Why didn’t you tell me this earlier?”

Akito had no adequate response to that. He apologized to her over and over, and in response Lapis grinned. “Your story better not be as disappointing as you are. Keep me up all night, okay?” Akito, in spite of himself, grew embarrassed enough to stammer out his affirmation. And then, he began explaining the premise.

“So, the world is split into four countries placed within a giant maze. Since the start of this current world, there have been monsters known as Selfless and certain magical powers known as Blessings. Selfless are pitch black monsters that are featureless and shaped like morphed humanoids, and their attacks damage the soul. Blessings, meanwhile, allow humans to use a certain supernatural power with an exception or drawback. So for instance, one Blessing I have is the ability to ‘make anyone fall in love with me, except for the one I love…’”

Lapis, who had been listening patiently, interrupted to ask the obvious question. “Wait, that’s so cool! What’s the main character’s Blessing?” Akito predicted Lapis would ask that. “Rubio? He can wield the hardest material, but has the most brittle body. He has a magical piece of paper that he can transform into the hardest metal by touching it, but in exchange, he had to undergo surgery as a child for an exoskeleton to strengthen his body.”

Silence as Lapis tried to wrap her head around that. Finally, Lapis cast a disappointed glance at the radio. “Seriously? Akito, that’s the type of ability you give to a background character because you’ve run out of ideas! That’s so much less cool than being able to make anyone fall in love with you! And what’s with being able to cheat your way out of a drawback without any repercussions?"

“It wasn’t easy choosing a Blessing where an umbrella was a logical weapon choice!” Akito shot back. “And besides, it’s plot relevant!”

“Right. Let me guess, plot relevant because there’s a point in the story where his Blessing fails and the ‘hardest material’ turns to paper.”

No response. Lapis laughed. “Minji, is Akito blushing really hard right now because he was found out? Is his expression, say, as fragile as paper?” Despite the bad joke, both Minji and Tanner, who were sitting together whispering to one another, smiled. Their glances at Akito confirmed Lapis’ suspicions. Lapis continued. “Anyways, surely you gave the main character something else that makes him special besides getting hard by his own touch.”

It took Akito a while to stammer out a rebuttal. “He’s selfish!”

A long sigh. “Akito, you must really hate main characters? Why are you insulting them on purpose?” She added an extra poke in jest. “You know, I’ll be sad if this is your impression of me.” To her mild surprise, Akito regained composure and objected. “Being selfish isn’t an insult! Selfishness isn’t a bad thing! It’s even the title of my story!”

Lapis hadn’t expected that. “Do explain.”

“How would you define selfishness?”

“Acting solely according to your own needs?”

Akito agreed. “Right. In that case, isn’t every single action done by a person selfish? Let’s take the action furthest from what you define as selfish, such as sacrificing your life to save someone else’s. Even for something like that, you are acting according to your own desires — if you didn’t want to do it, you simply wouldn’t have done it. Doing terrible things, yes, but also being a good samaritan…All of that is you acting according to your own needs, and putting yourself first. All of that is selfish. It’s neither good or bad — it’s human.”

“And,” Akito continued, “what about the opposite of selfish, selfless. Isn’t that just like the word suggests — selfless, or without self? If you are ever able to act without self, doesn’t that mean you are denying who you are? In other words, aren’t you treating yourself like you are worse than a human? I won’t deny that being selfish isn’t always good, but always being selfless means that you don’t think of yourself as human. Isn’t that just as bad?”

In the wake of Akito’s rant, a stunned silence fell over both Lapis’ room and the room in Complex Zeta. Tanner was the first to speak. “That was amazing, Akito!” Minji nodded in agreement. Meanwhile, a laugh blazed through the boundaries of the radio. A beautiful laugh, that of the main character. 

“Akito, Akito, touché! Simply touché What an imaginative notion! What an excellent notion!” Lapis exclaimed with glee. In response to all the praise (and recoil from embarrassment after his rant), Akito turned into a stuttering mess. “Wha, uh, um, th-thanks?”

“I’ll be selfish. Tell me more!”

---------------------------------------------------------

From Akito’s Notebook
Selfish, Chapter 6

Rubio let out a breath and muttered to himself. “So that's how it is, huh?” 

So that's…how it is.

If they went on the journey with him in spite of themselves, that would be the one thing Rubio hated. That would be selfless.

But they did have their own wishes. In that case…

Still looking downwards, Rubio asked the two in front of him, “Are you sure you want to go with me?”

Skye and Anton looked at each other, then both said: “Nah, we’d literally take anyone else over you.” 

Rubio heaved a sigh. “Screw you two…”

Silence, one last time. And then, Rubio began to laugh. A beautifully clear laugh, one which broke the stillness of the autumn night. Skye looked at him, half in disgust and half in confusion, until Rubio finally stopped his nonsensical laughing to speak.

“Well, I recommend you choose me.”

Anton took the bait. “And why is that?”

At that moment, the wispy clouds covering the sky parted, revealing a black canvas full of stars. There was a full moon, and its gentle light filtered through the tall oaks, finally coming to linger around the three figures seated in a circle. As he stood up, Rubio turned his gaze from the ground straight towards Anton and Skye. The starlight danced in his eyes, mingling with the intense light of someone who thought he could take on the world, and win. When he spoke, it was without any of the hesitation he had just displayed, any of the sadness, rage, nor uncertainty. His voice was resolute.

“Because I’ve decided. From here on out, you two are a part of me. Your problems are now part of my problems, your lives are now part of my life, and your wishes…they’re my wishes too.”

“So I’ll make a promise to you. I swear on myself that I will fulfill your dreams, now that they’re mine as well. And if there’s one thing I’m good at, it’s that I will do everything to make my dreams come true.”

A grin, one which shattered the night sky.

“I’m selfish after all. I’ll definitely lead you to a better future.”

In those words, there was another promise as well. A selfish promise that no matter what, Rubio Carone would not lose any more parts of himself.

Anton stared at him, transfixed. In the few months that he had known Rubio, he had come to see Rubio as a man without morals, a coward who abandoned others. The lowest of the low, inhuman, selfish. That last one was evidently still true. But, for the first time, Anton thought that the man grinning there in front of him was, in some sense, truly human.

Meanwhile Skye acted completely normal. The way she saw it, the idiot in front of her was the same as he always was. He had just expanded his definition of “self” to include two more people. Still, she was in a much better mood than before.

“Any option to decline?” She smirked..

Rubio’s grin spread even wider.

“Too late! I am selfish!”

---------------------------------------------------------
~

The sky was a deep, endless black, a void filled with the epitaphs of countless sparkling stars. Despite the late hour, the lights in the main bedroom of the princess’ palace were turned on. Blue sat in one of the comfortable beanbags in the corner of the room, reading from one of Erin’s reading tablets. Evie and Erin were lying together on the covers of the bed, sharing a book comfortably. The only source of discomfort was the glare Evie cast towards Blue every once in a while. The vampire did that more and more recently whenever Blue was hanging out with Erin, even though Blue was pretty sure she hadn’t done anything wrong. Apart from that, it was a cozy atmosphere, one which Blue had started to look forward to every night.

The doors to the bedroom opened with a bang. Lapis leapt gracefully into the room, the edges of her cloak splaying across the rug as she struck a pose on the rug. Erin glared at her. “It's well past midnight! And don’t be so loud. You’ll disturb everyone.” 

“Sorry, mom,” Lapis replied flippantly as Blue ran up to her, proudly displaying the reading tablet. “Lapis, Lapis, this is so cool! There’s so many stories here! I asked Erin, and she said I can come here all I want to read!” Lapis laughed and addressed Erin: “Don’t spoil her so much.” She glanced around Erin’s bedroom. “Where’s Mitsui?”

“The cyclops went to get supplies. He said he’d meet us there” Evie let out a yawn, showing her cute fangs, as she replied. Blue perked up. “What supplies?” 

“Did you forget?” Erin grinned. “It’s Sunday!”

It was the first Sunday since the start of summer. The fighting hadn’t lost its intensity since the beginning of the assault, and so they hadn’t met for the regular Sunday excursion. Blue assumed they had just cancelled it. “What are we doing?” She asked, her grey eyes even more invigorated than before. Lapis and Erin exchanged a glance. “You’ll see!”

The four of them made their way outside. Evie grumbled as she transformed into her full size and let them get on her back, though even her complaints and insults seemed milder than usual. They lifted off, traversing the width of the island. As they flew over the dark silhouettes that marked Complex Alpha, Blue spotted a few lights making their way down the gravel path. They were the supply team Lapis had created for the Oni. 

The Oni had settled on an island only a few miles away from them. Despite that, the only time it was safe to deliver supplies was at nighttime, when the war was on standstill. It wasn't something the elves wanted to do: Blue had heard them complaining about why they owed the Oni valuable supplies or why Lapis had ordered them to do it without enlisting the Oni in the war. Though the Oni were cordial in their meetings, it was clear the relationship between the two races wasn't the best. 

For now, they flew past them. Evie landed at their destination shortly after. The sound of waves and the scent of the sea breeze greeted Blue as she hopped off Evie’s back into the sand. It was the beach. 

“Wow!” Blue exclaimed as she ran towards the waves without a second thought, her footsteps throwing up arcs of sand behind her. She had never seen the beach at night before. There was an otherworldly, mystical feeling to it. 

“Welcome, Blue.”

“Mitsui!”

The vampire was organizing an assortment of things Blue had never seen before. She curiously picked one of them up — it was a small, thin plastic cylinder with a tube of dull colour inside. “What is this?”

“Lapis asked to bring it. It's a glow stick!” Erin caught up to them and grabbed another glowstick. “If you snap it like this…” Blue stared, transfixed, as the dull colour began taking on a vivid luminosity. She snapped her glowstick, and it did the same. Mitsui chuckled as Blue tried to snap it again to make it brighter. “I'm afraid that won't work.” Undeterred, Blue began experimenting further with the glowsticks while Erin waved Evie over. “Let's play catch, Evie!” She said, holding up a glowstick.

“I'll snap you like that glowstick, chocolate bar.” Evie glared at her. “Why a chocolate bar?” Blue wondered. Though, both she and Erin would soon find out that Evie ate chocolate bars by snapping them into small pieces and devouring them one by one. 

In the meantime, Lapis began setting up some of the other objects Mitsui had brought. Mitsui sauntered over to help her, and Blue followed closely. Waving a bundle of multicoloured glowsticks in front of her, she could see that they were shaped like much smaller versions of the missiles from her launcher. “What are those?” Lapis and Mitsui answered at the same time. “Fireworks!”

“Like the things that explode into flowers of any color when you launch them in the air?” Blue exclaimed excitedly, eyes shining. “I’ve never seen them before! I want to see!”

Lapis grinned. “You'll see plenty! We're lighting up the sky tonight!”

~

“Ahh, I’m exhausted! Moving around so much really doesn’t suit me.”

Blue collapsed on the sand besides Lapis. The majority of the fireworks and glowsticks were used and littered the beach. Only one firework remained, having likely malfunctioned from spending too much time unused — after all, fireworks were ancient technology only accessible by the elves. Mitsui and Evie huddled around the broken firework, trying to get it to bloom. Erin lay on the ground beside them with a somewhat satisfied look. At the cost (reward?) of having her blood sucked out by Evie, she had gotten the vampire to play catch. 

As Blue watched them, Lapis glanced teasingly at her. “What moving around? Weren’t you just standing still staring at the fireworks the whole time?” Blue glared at her, though she was far too happy for her glare to have any intensity. “Shut up! That counts as moving for me! And besides,” she added, “you’ve been sitting here for a while now, so it’s not like you’ve been moving any more. What are you even doing, anyways.”

Lapis smiled contentedly. “I was thinking.”

“About what?”

The elf’s hand moved, almost instinctively, to her pendant. Over the weeks they had spent together, Blue had noticed that whenever Lapis was deep in thought, she usually did that, as a habit. “Do you remember our contract, Blue?”

“It's Jaquavious.” Blue responded. Lapis glanced at her in mild surprise, and then she laughed. “Aww, you still remember that?” Blue shrugged. “I try not to forget the names people give me.”

Lapis didn't reply, and a comfortable silence settled over the two. Both of them watched Evie and Mitsui in the distance, the former of which almost clumsily snapped the firework in two much to Mitsui’s trepidation. Erin got up from the sand and moved in close to Evie, who jumped away; the three began bickering once more. Finally, Lapis asked Blue. “Do you hate me for that contract?”

Blue sniffed. “Weird question.” Lapis leaned in and ruffled her hair, trapping her before Blue could pull away. “It’s rhetorical. I know you’ll say yes, so just go ahead and say it.”

“Yes? You think I hate it? I mean, you do treat me like a child, and…” Blue turned to Lapis in surprise. Their gaze met, and even in the dim light, Blue could see the gem-like glimmer in Lapis’ eyes. The elf nodded. “I’ve made you my slave and I’m taking full advantage of you. Both you and the reader should loathe me for that.”

“If you know you owe me, then you could let me go.” Blue pointed out. Lapis responded wryly. “I’m not a nice enough person to free you and lose such a big advantage in this war. So,” she added, “how about this? Once we win the war and I’m done with you, I’ll do anything you want from me, for the rest of my life. Absolutely anything. I promise.”

Had Lapis not spoken those last two words, Blue might have passed it off as her usual attempt at teasing. But she had, and Blue stayed silent for a long time. Finally she replied: “It’s a promise. But I really don’t think you understand. I did hate you for a bit, and maybe you deserve to be hated. But ever since I’ve known you’ll keep your promises, I haven’t been able to hate you.”

The girl shrugged. “If anything, I kind of like all of you.”

Lapis stared at Blue. Her expression was one Blue hadn’t seen from her, one of surprise mixed with something else. Blue wondered what teasing was coming her way, and she was starting to regret saying her thoughts out loud. 

As it turned out, that teasing would come belatedly, a few days later. For now, Lapis smiled, a soft, gentle smile that held its witnesses, even the stars captive. It was the smile of the main character, but even more so, it was that of the girl named Lapis.

“Thanks.” 

It was a beautiful smile. 

In the distance, there were three shouts as Mitsui, Evie, and Erin scrambled back. The sound of fizzling, almost like a can of soda being opened, buzzed through the air as a dark silhouette split the starry sky in two. And amidst that sound, there was a boisterous laugh, one which could take on the world and win.

“With that out of the way, the main character shall indulge in her selfishness. You, my friends, everyone I interact with offstage — all of you are a part of me! And I promise…”

A singular firework shell bloomed into two, then three, then four bursts of light, each a different, vibrant flower. They were the last fireworks of that night. Though, Blue’s attention was on something else — an existence even brighter than the fireworks. 

Lapis leapt up and into Blue’s direct field of view, planting her feet in the sand like an actor taking center stage. Her cloak billowed behind her resolute back as she raised her right hand up towards the night sky. She clenched it into a defiant fist.

“...I’ll definitely carve out a better future for myself.”

For a few seconds, there was only the sound of the fireworks crackling and the other three people on the beach exclaiming in awe. And then, just as Lapis began to turn around excitedly, Blue spoke: “Yeah, yeah, that was cool, so don’t even bother asking.”

“I won’t take credit for it.” Lapis laughed, then added: “You know me so well.”

“Not by choice!”

~

Still later that night, after the five friends on Complex Alpha had cleaned up the beach and crawled into their respective beds, the artificial lantern illuminating Mini's bedroom was still on. There was a knock on the door, and she got up and let her visitor in. It was one of three generals in the human army, Algernon Prischett. 

As Minji locked the door behind them, Algernon surveyed the room full of folders. “How's work?” He asked. Minji shrugged and took the only chair available. “Good. Chiaros has been adapting well to combat.”

“That's great.”

They conversed about the war for a few minutes, in a manner akin to small talk, with Algernon passing on information about the human army’s next moves. As Algernon talked, he paced around the room. Finally, he stopped at a shelf next to Mini's work desk, thumbing through the layers of documents until he reached what he was looking for. Algernon paused. “How's the other thing I asked you to look into?”

“Little progress,” Minji admitted. “I don't have much to go off of.” Algernon nodded in understanding before taking out a manila folder. “You know,” he mused, fiddling with the folder cover, “from the ancient texts, we were able to decipher that fairies were containers for the souls of ancient humans. But connecting that to reincarnation is a pretty big leap.”

The hints of a smile appeared on Minji’s face. “It was the first thing Akito said.”

“Who?” Algernon asked, genuinely confused. Clearly he hadn’t bothered to remember Akito. Minji sighed. “Nevermind.”

“Anyways,” Algernon continued, talking to himself, “I suppose if you do make that connection, the rest is logical. If you can reincarnate the souls of ancient humans, why wouldn’t it be possible to reincarnate present-day humans?” As he spoke, he absentmindedly studied the folder. It was nondescript and unlabelled; in fact, its contents were so thin that one might think it was an empty unused folder. Algernon opened the folder. 

Inside was a single page of notes. Annotations were jotted down in the margins, and a few photos and sticky notes were neatly clipped on. But the most notable thing was a string of three words, written in large, scrawling font at the top of the page. A name. 

Bluebird of Flight.

Minji got up from her seat and joined Algernon in examining her notes. “Reincarnation itself is illogical, though. To be able to bring someone perfectly back to life in a new body, complete with their psyche and memories, is absurd.”

Algernon smiled. He creased the paper, underlining the name at the top. “But somehow, it did happen.” He repeated words he had only ever told to Minji, though she didn't know where or how he got his information.

“After all, ‘Bluebird’ is a present-day human reincarnated into a fairy’s body.”
