~~ Minji Best Girl [1] ~~

It was nearly midnight. Within the gigantic self-sufficient city known as Complex Zeta, the two hundred soldiers of the human army were fast asleep, preparing for another day of fighting. With two exceptions. 

“Minji, do you want a cinnamon roll?”

Tanner knocked on the room assigned temporarily as Minji’s workplace, where despite the late hour, the light was still on. Hearing no response, Tanner flung open the door and pranced in, carrying a plate of cinnamon rolls. Minji was hunched over her desk, poring over a stack of papers. She didn’t notice him come in. Tanner thrust the plate right in front of her nose. 

“Look, Minji! Fluffy, warm, freshly baked cinnamon rolls! They’re so good, you should take a break —”

“I don’t want them! I’m busy, so get out!”

Minji threw Tanner out the door and slammed it shut. He got up, unperturbed, and pranced back down the hallway, cinnamon rolls still in hand. 

“Where was I…” Minji muttered. “I lost my train of thought. Tanner’s such an idiot…”

“...”

“...”

A few minutes later, Tanner stood in the common space, twenty four cinnamon rolls in hand. “I guess I made too much!” He said brightly, deciding not to worry about how to dispose of the rolls. Just then, the door behind Tanner opened, and Minji wordlessly took a seat beside him, grabbed a bun, and bit into it. Tanner stared at her in surprise for a moment, before breaking into a smile. 

“It's good, right?”

“It is. But you made too much.”

Tanner laughed. “I did, didn’t I?” 

As Tanner sat down next to her, Minji finished her first bun and reached for another. She didn’t care much for sweet things, but these were unbelievably fluffy and warm — anything Tanner made always tasted good. In between bites, she asked: “How has the fighting been?” 

“I’ve still managed to avoid killing elves!” Tanner flashed a victory sign, and Minji pursed her lips slightly. “That’s good, but,” she hesitated, her voice quieting a bit, “please prioritize your safety. Please…”

Before she could say her next words, Minji felt Tanner’s hand on hers. He flashed a wide grin. “Don’t worry, I’ll come back home. I’ll be back so quickly, you won’t realize I’m late!”

“...”

For a brief moment, their eyes met. And then, Minji withdrew her hand and pointedly averted her gaze, doing her best to ignore the heat spreading across her face. “So you’re saying you’ll still be late,” she muttered underneath her breath, her tone belying the smile that had appeared on her face.  

They ate cinnamon rolls in comfortable silence until Tanner asked casually: “Is tomorrow a rest day?” 

“We don’t get rest days. It’s a war.” 
 
“Seriously?” Tanner sighed, momentarily displeased. But with a shrug, he quickly shook it off. “Well, whatever. Let’s go somewhere tomorrow!” 

“...Okay.” Minji once again concentrated her gaze on anything but Tanner’s eyes. “Where?”

“No clue! We’ll figure that out when we get there!” 

Shortly after, as rain began falling outside, Minji returned to her work desk. It was a far less productive night than she would have liked — she kept getting distracted by thoughts of tomorrow. 

~


---------------------------------------------------------

From Akito’s Notebook
Selfish, Chapter 7

Their hunger finally drove them to move from the outskirts of Naratu to the city center. They walked in the shadows of the city market, blending in amidst the exchange of gold and the bustling of the townspeople. 

“So apart from food, what supplies are we getting?”

“I need a lot of wood because someone keeps wasting arrows.”

“Have you considered not missing people with that massive umbrella of yours?”

Rubio and Skye bickered back and forth, until suddenly, Skye stopped dead in her tracks. Rubio crashed into her. “Did your heart stop or something?”

Skye gestured towards a stall opposite their current location, a wicked grin spreading across her face. Amidst the crowd of people, two familiar faces were buying candied apples. Even with their faces masked, Rubio could tell it was Anton and Mitsuki. 

“...No way.”

Skye grinned. “So you were thinking what I was thinking!”

“Yes, and I was thinking it was a bad idea. We are not following them.”

“It’ll be fun!”

“Only a Cupid like you would think stalking two people clearly on a date is fun.”

“I’ll take the compliment! And besides, you murder people for fun, so are you really one to talk?”

“Say what you will.”

“Really? Then we’re going!”

---------------------------------------------------------

“Akito. Akito! Let’s get going already!”

From underneath an overhang where he was taking shelter from the rain, Akito looked up and saw Violet waving at him. He put away his notebook. “Coming!”

~

As Violet pulled Akito through the large sliding doors of the entrance, they were met with a blast of warm air, blown in by large overhead fans. Akito adjusted his eyes to the lights and took in his surroundings.

The complex was ridiculously large. It was split into eight levels, and from their position by the entrance, the building opened upwards and they could see into all of them. Buildings of different textures and sizes, parks filled with lush artificial greenery, entertainment complexes and even a waterpark — just about everything humans could envision was crammed into a space the size of a bustling town. And neatly organized in the space that remained were market stalls as far as the eye could see, which transformed the raw materials generated by the complex into consumable goods. 

Even though Akito had lived in a similar complex for the eighteen years of his life, he never got tired of the kaleidoscopic view — especially if he didn’t need to interact with people while doing so. Seeing as Violet was also whirling around like an excited kid, she was also amazed by the sight. Akito had to stop her from bumping into a passerby.

“Let’s go to the waterslide!” Violet pointed up to the second floor after apologizing to the passerby. 

“We don’t have much time though,” Akito muttered, looking at his pocketwatch. It was around eleven in the evening, just after their meeting with Lazu. Ever since the war began, the vast majority of their waking hours were now spent either fighting on the frontlines or debriefing with other soldiers. Any recreational activities now had to be done after nine in the evening, and as they got up early the next day, there was a strict curfew at one in the morning. They had just two hours in the complex.

“It’s just materials, right? Fabric, wood, and plastic if we can find it.” Violet recalled a piece of paper from her pocket and read off it. It was a list of materials they needed for their airplane. “That doesn’t seem that hard to find.”

“Yeah, but we need a lot of wood. I don’t think one shop alone can provide what we need.”

Violet sighed. “I still think we should substitute it with that self-healing plastic.” 

“And exactly how much money do you have?.”

As far as raw building materials produced by the complex went, wood was the cheapest and most widespread, as it was the only one that wasn’t artificially fabricated. Everything else, from steel to brick and plastic, was the same basic material that had been “overlaid” with a different texture, density, and appearance to derive their material properties. There were also self-healing variants, which comprised everything ancient within the complex. It was how the complex had survived a rumoured three thousand years of existence. Unsurprisingly, nowadays those materials were ridiculously expensive. 

Violet avoided answering how much money was in her credit card. “We can just ask Minji and Tanner for money!” 

“Definitely not. That’s bad manners.”

“Seriously? You say that for everything I do.” Akito couldn’t resist bursting into laughter — it was true — and Violet glared at him. Before he could react, she shoved him into one of the escalator pods leading to the upper floors and closed its doors shut, trapping him inside. He caught a glimpse of Violet’s smug grin as the pod carried him up and away from her.

By the time he made his way back, Violet was long gone. In her place was a handwritten note telling him to suck an egg and challenging him to a competition to collect the most building materials. 

This girl…

…

…

The headstart Violet gave herself was completely unnecessary. 

An hour later, they were back outside the entrance on the first floor. Violet was gloating loudly, her voice clearly heard by the spectators who had gathered around her.

“Akito, I win! You're so bad!”

Huddled underneath the artificial shrubbery in a building beside her was Akito, who was muttering “I don't know her I don't know her I don't know her —”

Akito had managed to talk to exactly one and a half shopkeepers, stammering his way through his request. The half was because that shopkeeper hadn't been able to understand his unintelligible stutter, and Akito had fled from the scene without buying anything (and tried to flee from reality in the process). He had managed to buy around a hundredth of what they needed. Everything else had been bought by Violet — and she had done so in an hour. 

Violet had decided to use Scirocco to get around, in an effort to save time. Though she hadn't expected it, that naturally drew a lot of bystanders — and undeterred, she had roped them into looking for supplies for her. It wasn't long before she revealed Akito was also a soldier, and the two of them were swarmed by people. 

Much to Akito’s utter horror, of course. 

Now, as Violet peeked beneath the shrubbery, Akito yelped at her, trying not to expose himself: “This is all your fault!”

“You lost!” Violet emphasized smugly. 

“Okay, okay, yes, I lost! How are you going to get us out of this?”

“Don't worry, when I realized this would happen I made sure to prepare! I figured you wouldn't like it, after all.”

Akito momentarily felt a wave of gratitude wash over him, which immediately crashed against jagged rocks and burst into spray when Violet brought out two black face masks, clearly fake wigs, and pairs of sunglasses. 

“What is this for?”

“Don't you know? They wear these in movies to escape. It always works!”

Akito glared at her, especially because she seemed to be dead serious. “That's just because it's a movie. This will just draw more attention in real life!”

“Seriously?” Violet exclaimed, shocked.

The crowd of people drew ever nearer to their hiding spot. One of them asked Violet if there was someone beneath the shrubs. Akito felt his mind working harder than it had ever worked. 

What would Lazu do, what would Lazu do…

Akito found the answer. 

“Violet, use <Jetstream>!”

And so, as the clock struck midnight, a tornado touched down on the first floor of Complex Zeta, violently lashing out at the buildings and people all around it. Two blurs, one bronze and one dark gray, rocketed to the top floor of the complex in dramatic fashion, leaving every spectator below dumbfounded.

~

After their escape to the top floor, which were the dorm rooms for the complex’s residents, Akito and Violet took an unassuming elevator down to the second level. Violet began pulling him through the corridors the moment they exited the elevator. 

“W-wait, where are we going?”

A mischievous grin. “Obviously the waterslide! Since there’s no one there right now.” Everyone that had been on the second floor had either been enlisted by Violet to help find supplies, or had rushed down to the first to check out the commotion. As they raced through the empty corridors, Akito asked: “How much of this did you plan?” 

“I’d be lying if I wasn’t thinking of it the whole time.”

Though Akito hadn’t seen any other water park, he got the feeling that even compared to back in ancient times, it was massive. It was the size of a small city block, and completely deserted — the lifeguards that were supposed to be on duty had left an hour ago, since no one was carefree enough to want to go after midnight. Though, just as Akito was about to point that out to Violet, two people climbed the waterslide stairs and came into view.

So we aren’t the only people…

…Wait. Don’t I know them?

Akito instantly dove behind the sign stating the water park rules, pulling Violet along with him. She let out a yelp, which he quickly muffled with his hand. In a low whisper, she hissed: “What was that for?” 

“Look!”

Violet peeked out of the sign. Tanner was pulling Minji up the stairs. Both of them had tropical-themed floaties around their waists, and though Minji was in her swimsuit — a rather immodest bikini that Tanner had bought ten minutes ago — Tanner was in a T-shirt and shorts. Everything about the duo was an odd sight, not least the fact that Minji wasn’t working, and her smile was far brighter than her usual impassive expression. 

Violet waved at them. But just before she could exclaim her greetings, Akito kicked her in the shin. She yelped once more and fell back into the cover of the sign. “Don’t interrupt them!” Akito whispered.

“Interrupt?” 

“They’re on a date!” 

“...The red fruit you eat?” 

Though she seemed to be completely serious, Akito kicked her lightly. Heated whispering ensued, and a minute later, it finally occurred to Violet what Akito was saying. 

“Understood? Then let’s go to the water park another day.”

“Yeah.” But then, Violet reached into the outer pocket of her blazer and took out the face masks, wigs, and sunglasses. “So instead, let’s follow them!”

“Didn’t I literally just tell you to leave them alone? And why do you still have those?” 

Akito’s words fell on deaf ears. Violet had already transformed into her comically terrible disguise, and it took all of Akito’s strength to keep her away from instantly revealing herself.

“We’re not stalking them!” 

“Yes we are!” 

“No, we’re not!” 

“We are! We are!” 

Akito was getting a weird sense of deja vu, though he didn’t know why.

It only took three more minutes for two figures to creep out from the sign, wearing wigs that were obviously fake, face masks that barely covered their face, and sunglasses that belonged anywhere but indoors. One of them was rueing his existence as a pushover.

~

“I’ll admit I was looking at the cat, but seriously, I don’t have time to take care of him!”

“Don’t worry! I’ll definitely keep him well fed!”

“Do you even know what he can eat?”

“Huh? He can eat anything, right?”

“This is why I said you shouldn’t have bought him!”

It was exactly one in the morning when Minji and Tanner opened the door to the bedroom reserved for Base 33. They were met by a huge commotion between Violet and Akito. 

“Change out of your clothes already! And put that wig in the trash can! Wait, no, don’t strip here!”

“Do you want me to change my clothes or not?”

Both of them jumped to attention and met Minji’s and Tanner’s stare. Violet began to give them a salute, but was interrupted with a kick in the shin by Akito. 

Though, if he had to say, Minji and Tanner looked far more out of place. Tanner was shirtless, and his shorts were dripping wet. Minji had a pet crate with a tabby cat. 

Both Akito and Violet knew how that ended up happening. Tanner went on the waterslide with his regular clothes still on, taking Minji along despite the water park rules clearly saying only one person was allowed at a time. And then, as Minji was angrily drying Tanner’s hair, Tanner had noticed she kept glancing at a cat in a pet shop behind her. When Minji excused herself to go change her clothes, Tanner bought him. Akito recalled that when they were playing their introduction game with Lazu, Minji had chosen a cat. It seemed there was a reason she chose it after all.

Now, they all stared at each other. A long silence ensued. The cat meowed. 

Minji put her head in her hands. “I’m too tired. I’m dealing with this tomorrow.”

“It was fun, right?” Tanner grinned. Minji stared at him, before averting her gaze, sighing, and giving him a well-placed flick on the forehead. Just before she exited the room, she looked back. “By the way, in two days, you three are heading back to Base 33. I’ll explain everything tomorrow.” 

“You aren’t coming?” Violet asked. Minji shook her head. “Truthfully, I was never supposed to be at Base 33 to begin with. All squadron leaders stay at Complex Zeta. I just didn't stay because…” she paused, thinking how to best phrase it. “It’s convenient.”

“Why —” Violet began, but Akito stopped her before she could blurt anything else out. “Let’s ask her tomorrow.” Minji flashed him an incredibly grateful look.

And so, at five minutes past one in the morning, the four members of Base 33 (and one cat) said their good nights.

~

Later that night, Minji finally turned off the lamp on her work desk. She headed to the communal space to get a glass of water before sleeping. As she walked past Tanner’s bedroom, she paused. The door was open. Tanner lay sprawled out on the bed, snoring softly. Minji hesitated for a moment before quietly entering the room and leaning in.

…

…

Minji smiled as she hurriedly got back up to her feet. She blushed slightly and muttered to herself:

“This is why it’s convenient.”

~

It was a rainy day, an anomaly in the archipelago’s summers. A storm had blanketed the skies with thick, brooding clouds, reducing visibility so much that the fairies couldn’t effectively fight. The airspace above Complex Alpha was quiet. The army of elves and vampires, <Shadow> was either resting or on patrol

Lapis and Blue landed on a large desolate island roughly ten kilometers southwest of Complex Alpha. A handful of humanoid beings with mossy green hair — one of the archipelago’s five races, the oni — stirred and watched as the commander of <Shadow> transformed out of her mech. Blue materialized out of nowhere and landed next to her, her white dress unblemished despite the drizzling rain. The oni went up to meet Lapis. 

“Nice weather, isn’t it?” 

Lapis chuckled. “Yeah.” She took a look around. The island had been given the name “New Oni Island” by its inhabitants; Lapis had secretly criticized the name for its lack of originality to Blue. Blue, for her part, thought “island” was a bit too generous. There was little greenery or places for shelter, and it was flat rock as far as the eye could see. The Oni had carved out large pits in the rock — an easy feat with their transformation — and by covering them with tarps provided by the elves, they could create a makeshift rainproof shelter. 

It wasn't the best conditions, but moving them into Complex Alpha was one thing Lapis adamantly refused to do. She told Blue it was because she didn’t trust them enough. 

Turning back to the Oni, she smiled in polite apology. “Sorry for not giving you any notice before Code Name: Windbreak.” The Oni shrugged. “Name aside, I don’t blame you for that. It makes sense you don’t trust us yet. Having inside information leaked would probably be the one thing you don’t want. And besides, you're already generous enough to give us supplies every day.” 

The island was more full than usual. Around a dozen elves and vampires were sitting within the tarp-covered pits, talking to a few of the Oni. Unlike the supply team, none of them were required to visit Oni Island. They were all active soldiers. 

The vast majority of elves and vampires still had an unfavourable impression of the Oni. But after their success in Code Name: Windbreak, a handful of them had slightly warmed up to their allies. Though they were clearly still guarded, Blue could see that the atmosphere between them was far less tense than it had been when they first met. Now, an elf ran up to Lapis. “Commander, have I introduced you?” He greeted the oni talking to Lapis. “This was my partner during Windbreak. His name is…”

As Lapis, the elf, and the oni struck up a conversation, Blue wandered off. It wasn’t long before a pair of familiar ruby eyes met hers. “Oh, it’s the sylphic screwdriver.” Evie was perched on a rock, using her black wings to shield herself from the driving rain. 

“Why screwdriver? And why are you here?” Blue remembered that a while back, Evie had said she couldn’t have cared less about the oni. “Didn’t you say you weren’t interested in them?”

“I’m not interested in almost all of them.” Evie replied. “But that mosshead is a decent fighter, so I came here to fight him.” 

“At least call me by my name.” 

From behind Evie’s wings, a pair of figures turned their heads and greeted Blue. One of them was an elf she had seen a few times before. The other was a tall oni, nearly twice as tall as Blue. He wore a thick coat that concealed his entire body, and his rain-slicked hair was the colour of fallen leaves. Evie shot the oni an apathetic look as he sat down besides her. “I’ll think about it if you defeat me, Bryophyta.” 

“Then I’ll pass. No way can I win.” He turned to Blue and smiled warmly. “I’m Geischt. I was their partner for Windbreak.” He gestured to Evie and the elf beside him. The elf, who seemed barely older than Blue, scratched his head. “And, um, I guess I’m the prince of the elves.”

“Nice to meet — wait, prince? Erin has a brother?” Blue cut off her greeting to yelp in surprise, and the boy quickly shushed her. “Not so loud, not so loud!”

“So you actually are her brother? How come I’ve never seen you with Erin?”

The boy scoffed and averted his gaze. “And why would I ever be seen around that idiot? It’s not like I’m proud of being her brother, since she’s well-loved and the pride of the elves. Actually, I stay far away from her so she doesn’t think that!”

Blue and Evie exchanged a glance. The vampire shrugged. “Tsundereness runs in the family, I guess.”

“I am not a tsundere!” The prince turned desperately to Geischt. “I’m not, right?” The oni chuckled. “You sure seemed to be one back when I saved you at Windbreak.”

“And I keep telling you, it’s not like you saved me or anything!” 

Blue would later learn from Lapis that the trio was responsible for three of the eight bases destroyed in Windbreak, as well as the deaths of the fairy of gravity and earth. That strength was expected, given that the squad was composed of Evie herself and someone whose fighting capability she acknowledged. Even the prince was an excellent Nightjar pilot.

For now, Geischt turned to Blue, so that the others couldn’t glimpse his face. He smiled at her again — no, his first smile was welcoming, and this was none of that. It was a cruel smirk, perhaps the expression one would have while looking at a banquet to be devoured. One of worldly desire, ecstatic greed. 

“Anyways, it's a pleasure to fight on the same side as you.”

“...Same.” Blue replied stiffly. 

~

Erin joined them a few hours after Lapis, Blue, and Evie departed New Oni Island. The rain was pouring down, heavier than ever, as the soaked princess rushed inside Complex Alpha and greeted them. 

“Sorry I’m late, I was helping someone outside. What are we doing today?” 

It had been exactly one week since their night at the beach. The first Sunday without Mitsui.

Lapis looked at Evie, who looked at Blue, who looked back at Lapis. There was a long, awkward silence as they tried to come up with an answer to Erin’s question. 

Mitsui had always been the one who suggested what to do every Sunday. 

When Erin had heard that Mitsui had died, she immediately excused herself and walked off. She reappeared a few hours later, and her eyes were slightly swollen, though she maintained that she hadn’t cried. And then, the people’s princess immediately went to visit the family of the elf that had died along with Mitsui.

Evie learnt the news an hour later, when she came back from Windbreak along with the prince and Geischt. For the next few days, she spoke a bit less than she normally did. Four days later, Blue overheard a conversation between her and Lapis. 

“Give me one good reason why I should let you attack the human army again..”

“I like fighting. I’m a strong fighter.”

“That’s not a reason.” 

“...I’m a strong fighter. Mitsui was just weak. If I were fighting, I would have killed every single human there. They would have all died.”

“So what?”

“...And Mitsui wouldn’t have.” 

Lapis didn’t give Evie another chance to attack, and the day after she was back to her typical disparaging self. 

And as for Lapis herself…

The day after his death, Blue woke up early and went down to the lounge out of habit. She found Lapis shuffling Uno cards. After they had played a few rounds (all of which were won by the elf), Lapis had said: “I miss him.”

“Huh?” It hadn’t been something Blue had expected to hear from the commander. She walked right into it.

“He gave me a much better challenge than you!”

“Shut up!” 

Lapis hadn’t changed. Not at all. Judging from her behaviour alone, Blue would have guessed Mitsui was alive and well.

The main character needs tragedy and suffering.

If it hadn’t been for her deep blue eyes back when she said that…

Now, Lapis spoke up. “I don’t want this to be our Sunday, but can we go somewhere really quickly?”

“Where?” Erin and Blue asked at the same time.

A smile. “You’ll see.”

Lapis led them to the elevator. Blue knew the first floor, the ground floor, contained everything needed for daily activity. The second was their sleeping quarters. The fourth was where they received raw materials from the self-sufficient complex. But now, Lapis pressed the button for the third floor. It was a place Blue had never explored — she had been forbidden to. 

The elevator doors opened. The four stepped out and found themselves on a high balcony, overlooking a grid of tightly packed cells no more than one meter in length and width. Looking down, Blue could see dots, thousands of them, one huddled within each cell. 

They were humans. 

“That’s…” Blue started to say something, but no words came out. She was reminded of a white room, one that didn’t contain freedom — only a bunk bed and a friend. These cells didn’t even have either. 

Lapis smiled, a smile whose meaning couldn’t be discerned. “It’s a nice life, you know? Nice and simple.” 

“You wake up whenever you want, and at eight in the morning you get a breakfast made by the ancient technology within the Complex. Then you sit around for four hours and get lunch the same way. You aren’t chained so you can walk around, if you’ll be satisfied with walking around in a one meter cell.” 

“Lapis.” Erin said in a low voice. But Lapis didn’t stop speaking.

“There’s even a screen in the cell, so you can watch a movie you’ve probably watched a thousand times. Though the walls are soundproofed for some reason we can’t change, so if you want to talk to someone else, you have to yell until your voice is hoarse.”

“Lapis.” Erin said again.

“And it’s a pretty painless execution! We just press a button, and your cell gets flooded with poison gas. You die in a matter of seconds, and then we ship you off to the butcher and turn you into a nice delicious salami.”

Lapis turned to Blue, that smile still on her face. “That is how we live. There is no other choice, but even so, the humans are justified in attacking us.”

“Blue, the humans are not our enemies —”

With a loud clang, Erin slammed Lapis against the wall. “Please, shut up. I know what you’re trying to say, but in the end, the humans are the ones we’re fighting against in this war. That does make them our enemies. And I'm not the only one that thinks that you're wrong!”

“So don’t say the humans aren't our enemies, not after they’ve killed so many of us. And not after they killed…”

The princess trailed off, though everyone knew what she was going to say. Lapis stayed silent. Neither spoke for a long time, until the princess clutched the lapels of Lapis’ cloak a bit tighter. 

“I know you won’t change your opinion…I’ll always support you, Lapis.”

Lapis closed her eyes. She reached out her arms and pulled Erin into a hug.

“...”

“If you’re jealous I’m hugging your girlfriend, then come here,” Lapis told Evie.  

Evie did so, wrapping her wings around the two of them. The vampire spoke in a low yet clear voice.

“Lapis, I’ll always support you too.” 

The smile on Lapis’ face softened slightly, becoming one much more recognizable. She turned to Blue. “You’re short, so it might be a bit hard to hug us, but try anyway.” 

Blue stared at her. “Screw you,” she muttered. She stepped forward, hesitated. 

And then she joined in. 

…

…

Afterwards, the four of them played Uno in Lapis’ bedroom. Lapis kept winning, Erin kept saying she didn’t cry, and Evie’s fangs kept a firm grip on Erin’s shoulder.

And all the while, rain kept falling outside their window. 

~

The rain continued for three days. 

And then, suddenly, it cleared up. A faint rainbow, framing a brilliant sunset, appeared above the skies of the archipelago. 

Lapis backflipped up the steps of the princess’ palace, striking a pose in greeting to Erin’s bodyguard, Tsukuyo, along the way. She rolled to her feet and flung open the door to Erin’s bedroom. 

“Blue, we’re going!” 

The fairy lay on a beanbag in the corner of Erin’s room, reading from her reading tablet. After the night they had all gone out to the beach, Erin had allowed her to enter her room without permission to read — much to Evie’s great irritation, since she was barred by Tsukuyo from doing the same. Despite the vampire insulting her whenever she got the opportunity to, Blue still headed over to the palace whenever Lapis was busy. Now, she jumped to her feet upon seeing Lapis. 

“A fairy attack?” Even though the skies had cleared up, she didn’t think the human army would attack, given how late it was. Lapis shook her head. “Nope! We’re going down the rabbit hole!” 

“What?”

“You’re reading Alice in Wonderland, right? Or,” Lapis grinned, “Were you just looking at the illustrations?”

“Shut up, I was actually reading it! And how’d you even know what my book was?”

While looking at the titles available on the reading tablet, Blue came across one she hadn’t expected to see. She instantly began reading it. Though, it wasn’t nearly as good a book as she expected, and the English was a bit old-fashioned and hard to comprehend. She turned the tablet off and changed the topic. “Anyways, what are we doing?”

“The weather’s nice now, and I doubt the fairies will attack, so let’s go exploring!” 

That was all Blue needed to hear. She shot out of the room like a rocket. “Let's go! Hurry up and transform, Lapis!” 

…

…

Much to Blue’s surprise and excitement, she found out that their mode of transportation wasn’t herself. The two of them took off from Complex Alpha in a Nightjar. Blue sat in Lapis’ lap, gleefully flicking the panel of switches and buttons in front of her. The cabin was cramped and uncomfortable — the Nightjar was a single-person utility jet, with a small cargo hold in the back which Lapis had filled to the brim with an assortment of items. Blue wasn’t complaining, though.

“Do you want to fly it?”

“Can I?” 

Lapis placed her hands on Blue’s, guiding her as she turned the yoke of the Nightjar. The plane gently turned to the left and flew south, in full view of the sunset.

“Whoaa, amazing!” Blue tilted the yoke back and forth, up and down, and the Nightjar climbed and dove like a seabird searching for prey.  

“And you can even do this!” Lapis, still holding Blue’s hands, executed a series of inputs that were too fast for Blue to decipher. The plane did a barrel roll before spiralling down towards the sea, and Lapis brought it under control just before they hit the water, the left wingtip skimming the whitecaps. It was an evasive maneuver she often executed in mecha form, and Blue hadn’t thought it was possible with a Nightjar given its worse agility and size. She remembered that the fairy they had fought a few days ago, Echo, had said Lapis was the strongest and most decorated Nightjar pilot among the elves, to the point that she had been chosen as commander of <Shadow> because of it. 

“You didn’t think I could do that?” Lapis spoke right into her ear, causing Blue to jolt to attention. “Shut up! That barrel roll was fun! Let’s do it again!” 

They performed airborne acrobatics until Blue found an island she liked — a picturesque slice of multicoloured granite adorned with a splash of lush greenery. Lapis landed the Nightjar onto a narrow piece of flat granite like a helicopter and opened the cargo hold. Both her and Blue peered inside. There were umbrellas, capes and carves of every colour arranged neatly in boxes, sunglasses and hats, and some things Blue didn’t even have a name for. “What’s all this for?”

“They’re props!” Lapis replied excitedly. “I need a good cover picture.”

Blue frowned, deciding not to spend that much brainpower trying to understand Lapis’ words. She pointed at a shiny chain on the side of the cargo hold. “What’s that?”

“A kusarigama! You use it like this!” Lapis demonstrated on a piece of granite beside her, much to Blue’s silent, reluctant amazement.

“And that?”

“Those are earrings!” 

Blue picked up a conical hollow container, about the size of her face. “What about this?”

“That’s one of the only things there that aren’t a prop. Try speaking into it!” Blue did, and though her voice didn’t seem to have any change in volume, a flock of gulls in the far distance flew into the sky, startled. “It’s a loudspeaker.” Lapis explained. “Though it doesn’t work through thick walls, it has uniform sound amplitude over a large distance, so even the birds over there can hear you as clearly as I can. Every Nightjar has one.” 

After Blue experimented with the loudspeaker further, she helped Lapis unload the crates of props. “You said something about a cover picture? Does that mean someone will be painting you? How else are you going to get a picture?”

Lapis glanced at her, also confused, and then she let out a clear laugh that rang out on the breeze. “You know about Uno, but not cameras?” Blue vaguely recalled hearing that word, in the same memory as the one where she learnt about television. Unlike television, however, humans didn’t have cameras. Searching through the recesses of her mind, she asked: “Camera…is that the one like a digital eye? It instantly captures what your eyes see and remembers it forever?”

The elf thought for a moment. “Yeah, that’s a pretty good description. Try it for yourself!” She reached inside one of the crates in the cargo hold and drew out a small box with an embossed lens jutting out. “Put your eye against here, and then press this button.”

Click!

Blue and Lapis looked at the image displayed on the camera screen. The granite outcrop, the aquamarine water, the gently rustling trees — it was exactly the same scene Blue had been capturing with her eyes a few seconds prior. 

And in the middle of the photo, still standing out amidst the stunning backdrop, an elf stood with her back facing the camera, having struck a pose before Blue could react. Her long black coat billowed out of frame, and her head was turned just enough that the viewer could see her unfathomably deep blue eyes, the same colour as the pendant swinging from her neck. 

“Splendid job, Blue! I look pretty good, don’t I? Though it’s only natural for the main character to be this good at playing to the camera —”

Blue shoved the camera into Lapis’ hands, stopping her narcissistic rambling. “Shut up and take a picture of me.”

“Aww, you can’t accept that I look this —”

“Heyyyyyy!” Blue interrupted her and struck a pose, and Lapis took the picture. Blue nudged against Lapis’ side, standing on her tiptoes to take a look at the image. It was far worse than what she had secretly been expecting. She looked up to see Lapis grinning at her.

“Were you expecting to look as good as me? The camera simply depicts the main character differently!”

“Screw you! You just took the photo badly!”

Lapis sighed mockingly. “Fine, I’ll take another. Wear this.” She took off her aviator goggles and handed them to Blue, who obliged. She smiled into the camera and heard the shutter click. 

“I bet that was better!” She exclaimed triumphantly as Lapis handed her to the camera. No sooner than the camera landed in her hands did she hear Lapis’ muffled snicker. 

“W-what is this? Lapis!” Blue yelled at the elf, who was now rolling with laughter on a patch of grass. “Why do I look so stupid?” Lapis burst into laughter again, and Blue shoved the goggles back at her. “No one would look good wearing these things. You try! I bet you’d look stupid too!”

Really, some day Blue would learn to stop setting flags around Lapis. But a few seconds after she said that, she stared in utter silence at the new photo she had taken of Lapis, with goggles on, which was undeniably beautiful. The elf ruffled her hair in amusement. 

“Blue —”

“You definitely changed the camera settings or something! I’m not accepting this!”

Lapis laughed boisterously. “If you’re so sure, then let’s take one with both of us!” She flicked a switch on the camera, and as if by magic, it began hovering in place. She took out her umbrella from the depths of her camera and spun it to face the camera. “I’ll be using this.”

“Hey!” Blue, not to be outdone, dove into the pile of props within the Nightjar and came out with a tan-coloured sunhat. “Then I’ll take this!” 

Lapis adjusted the camera in their direction, and both of them took a moment to orient themselves.

“Okay! On three, two, one!”

Click!

~

The sun had long set by the time Lapis and Blue clambered back into the Nightjar, exhausted. Unlike when they arrived at the island, Blue squeezed into the cargo hold along with the props and began focusing intently on the camera. She swiped through the hundreds of photos they had taken. 

“Lapis, they all look terrible. I’m deleting all of them.”

“I know I far outshine the world in photos, but seriously?”

As Blue nodded, methodically deleting each photo using the method Lapis had taught her, the elf piloted them back to Complex Alpha and let out an aggrieved sigh. “But the records of my brilliance! My cover pictures! Blue, please don’t!”

“Like I care! I’ve deleted all —”  

“Hah, did you think I’d say that? There’s a way to recover deleted photos, you know. Or I guess you wouldn’t know, since I never told you.” Lapis interrupted, a smugly triumphant grin on her face. 

A pause. And then, Blue tapped a few more buttons. “You can recover them from the trash bin, right? I just emptied it.”

“......Eh?” 

The Nightjar’s automated system let out a warning ping as Lapis, too shocked to move a muscle, let her hands slide off the controls. “W-w-w-wait —”

Blue just smirked in self-satisfaction. She swiped through the remaining photos, deleting one after another without a second glance. At some point, her finger hovered motionless over the delete button, and she smiled to herself for a long time. 

“All done.”

She pressed the power button on the camera, and with a low whir, its shutter faded to black. 

A short while later, the vampires detected Lapis’ Nightjar entering the airspace around Complex Alpha. It wasn’t flying with its usual flair, and if its occupants were using the loudspeaker of uniform amplitude, they could have heard Lapis mumbling about the heartlessness of the fairy girl sitting behind her and mourning the loss of all their pictures.

The fairy girl in question was laughing, “Serves you right!”

Only Blue knew one photo remained in the camera. Two girls, grinning into the camera amidst a beautiful rainbow. 

It was their first selfie.
